601 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Morrison v. Sadler


No. 49A02-0305-CV-447


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


821 N.E.2d 15; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 75



January 20, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49D13-0211-PL-1946. The Honorable S.K. Reid, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, three same-sex couples, sought review of a judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which dismissed their declaratory judgment complaint. The couples sought to obtain marriage licenses from defendant county circuit court clerks. The Indiana Attorney General intervened on behalf of the clerk, and five amicus curiae briefs were filed in support of the State's position.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were all in same-sex long-term relationships, and had traveled to Vermont to enter into civil unions. The only impediment to their marriages was the opposite sex requirement of Ind. Code § 31-11-1-1(b), and they sought a declaratory judgment for issuance of marriage licenses by the clerks. Plaintiffs claimed that § 31-11-1-1(b) violated Ind. Const. art. 1, §§ 1, 12, and 23. The trial court granted the State's motion to dismiss the complaint for failing to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. Plaintiffs appealed and the court held that there was no violation of the Equal Privileges and Immunities Clause of Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23, as the reason for the disparate treatment was reasonably related to the State's responsible procreation justification and the interest in raising children within a stable environment. Similar reasons supported the court's holding that there was no violation of Ind. Const. art. 1, § 12. Further, the limitation of marriage to opposite-sex couples did not materially burden a "core value" protected by Ind. Const. art. 1, § 1. The court noted that it was doubtful whether art. 1, § 1 was capable of independent judicial enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

602 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Lutz v. City of Indianapolis


No. 49A05-0404-CV-198


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


820 N.E.2d 766; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 34



January 18, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Michael D. Keele, Judge. Cause No. 49F12-0311-OV-003760.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Marion Superior Court, which, after a bench trial, found that defendant violated plaintiff city's unlawful noise ordinance, Indianapolis, Ind., Rev. Code Consol. City & County § 391-302 (Ordinance).


OVERVIEW: An officer cited defendant for violating the Ordinance due to loud music coming from his vehicle. After a bench trial, judgment was entered against defendant. He appealed, arguing, among other things, that the Ordinance was unconstitutionally vague because it prohibited any unusual or unnecessary noise, or any noise that annoyed others, within the city. The city argued that since Indiana's disorderly conduct statute, Ind. Code § 35-45-1-3(2), was held not to be vague and contained language that was less clear than the Ordinance, the Ordinance should survive the vagueness challenge. The court found that the disorderly conduct statute, unlike the Ordinance, contained a reasonableness test and required that a person be warned before being cited. Indianapolis, Ind., Rev. Code Consol. City & County § 391-302(a), (a)(2) did not include a sufficiently ascertainable standard of conduct to enable individuals of ordinary intelligence to adequately comprehend what conduct the Ordinance prohibited. Therefore, it was unconstitutionally vague. However, a portion of § 391-302(a)(2) that clearly defined what noise was prohibited during a certain time period was not vague and was severable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision that defendant violated the city's unlawful noise ordinance.

 

603 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


SCI Ind. Funeral Servs. v. D.O. McComb & Sons, Inc.


No. 02A03-0401-CV-22


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


820 N.E.2d 700; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 23



January 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by SCI Ind. Funeral Servs. v. D.O. McComb & Sons, Inc., 2005 Ind. LEXIS 495 (Ind., May 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Daniel G. Heath, Judge. Cause No. 02D01-0009-CP-1371.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is reversed, and this cause is remanded to the trial court with instructions that it enter summary judgment for SCI.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant successor cemetery (SC) sought review from a judgment of the Allen Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment to appellee funeral service providers in their action, alleging breach of a settlement agreement and intentional interference with a contractual relationship. The trial court had held that the application of the Exclusive Rights Act, Ind. Code § 23-14-46-7, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The providers' prior antitrust action resulted in a settlement agreement with the predecessor cemetery, which set forth a relationship between them of unlimited duration which was binding on successors. The SC indicated that it would not be bound by the agreement. The providers filed suit, and each party sought summary judgment. The trial court granted partial summary judgment to the providers, finding that the providers were entitled to specific performance of the agreement. The trial court struck a cemetery official's affidavit. The cemetery appealed, and the court found that it was error for the trial court to have stricken the supplemental affidavit of the cemetery, as it provided additional evidence to rebut the providers' assertion that they had performed under the agreement. Further, the providers failed to meet their burden of showing that they were entitled to specific performance under the agreement. The court held that application of the Act was not unconstitutional, as there was no violation of the Contracts Clause of Ind. Const. art. 1, § 24. Further, the Act was reasonably necessary to protect the health, safety, and welfare of the general public.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, and remanded the matter with directions for the trial court to enter summary judgment in favor of the cemetery.

 

604 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


LaRose v. State


No. 29A02-0403-CR-221


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


820 N.E.2d 727; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 25



January 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Larose v. State, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 211 (Ind., Mar. 10, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HAMILTON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Bernard L. Pylitt, Judge. Cause No. 29D02-0207-FC-73.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an interlocutory appeal seeking review of the judgment of the Hamilton Superior Court (Indiana), which denied defendant's motion to dismiss in his criminal action. Defendant had alleged that Ind. Code § 35-42-4-6, regarding class C felony child solicitation, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The police detective logged on to an internet chat room and impersonated a 13-year-old girl. Defendant allegedly instant messaged the detective, made several sexually explicit remarks, and arranged a meeting. When defendant arrived at the time and place of the meeting, he was arrested. Defendant argued that Ind. Code § 35-42-4-6 violated his right to free speech. In order to pass constitutional muster, § 35-42-4-6 had to be necessary to serve a compelling state interest, and it had to be narrowly drawn. Section 35-42-4-6 served the compelling state interests of preventing adults from urging children to have sex and proactively seeking child predators prior to the child being harmed. The use of an undercover officer instead of a child was a necessary means to accomplish the State's compelling interests. Section 35-42-4-6 was narrowly drawn despite defendant's argument that it merely criminalized solicitation of an adult police officer. Section 35-42-4-6, however, involved the belief that the police officer was an underage girl. Furthermore, § 35-42-4-6 was not unconstitutional merely because it failed to protect speech that involved a mistake of fact.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

605 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Napier v. State


No. 55A01-0406-CR-237


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


820 N.E.2d 144; 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 1



January 6, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by Napier v. State, 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 888 (Ind. Ct. App., May 17, 2005)
Reaffirmed Napier v. State, 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 825 (Ind. Ct. App., May 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MORGAN SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 55D03-0311-CM-330. The Honorable Jane Spencer Craney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Morgan Superior Court (Indiana), finding him guilty of operating a motor vehicle with a BAC of 0.08 percent or more.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that his conviction could not stand because admitting breath test results by certification documents and a BAC DataMaster Evidence Ticket violated the Confrontation Clause of the United States Constitution. Defendant further claimed that the admission of the breath test ticket violated the Indiana Rules of Evidence, inasmuch as that evidence was inadmissible hearsay. The appellate court concluded that the admission of the breath test instrument certification documents at issue here did not violate the rule set forth in Crawford. The appellate court noted that certificates regarding the inspection and compliance with relevant regulations of breath test instruments were admissible in prosecutions for operating a vehicle with a BAC of 0.08 percent or greater. Such certifications were not included in the class of evidence that were subject to Confrontation Clause scrutiny. However, the appellate court also found that admitting into evidence the BAC ticket purporting to prove the breath test results, absent any "live" testimony that would establish a foundation for its admission, was improper because the State failed to establish an adequate evidentiary foundation.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed.

 

606 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Berry v. State


No. 49A04-0402-CR-122


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


819 N.E.2d 443; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 2481



December 16, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Berry v. State, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 241 (Ind., Mar. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G06-0309-FA-160328. The Honorable Jane Magnus-Stinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which was entered on a jury verdict finding him guilty of attempted aggravated battery and which sentenced him to 12 years' imprisonment. Defendant contended that the State did not present sufficient evidence to sustain his conviction and that the trial court abused its discretion when it imposed a 12-year enhanced sentence.


OVERVIEW: The evidence at trial showed that defendant was present during a fight between two individuals and rejected another onlooker's suggestion that they break up the fight. Defendant threatened to kill the victim, and defendant drove one of the individuals in a car while the individual fired a shotgun out the passenger window at the other individual. He, then, drove the individual away from the crime scene. Defendant was convicted. The trial court also imposed an enhanced sentence against defendant. On appeal, the court held that sufficient evidence sustained defendant's conviction for attempted aggravated battery as an accomplice because defendant's conduct before, during, and after the shooting was fully consistent with that of an accomplice. Further, the court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it sentenced defendant to two years longer than the presumptive sentence for the crime. While the trial court improperly considered an aggravating factor to which defendant did not admit and on which the jury did not make findings, the court found that the enhanced sentence was proper because the trial court found the existence of two valid aggravating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

607 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Ellenwine v. Fairley


No. 71A03-0403-CV-124


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


818 N.E.2d 961; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 2418



December 7, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by Ellenwine v. Fairley, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 361 (Ind., May 3, 2006)
Superseded by Ellenwine v. Fairley, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 359 (Ind., May 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable William C. Whitman, Judge. Cause No. 71D06-0110-CP-1497.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, parents of a deceased child, appealed from a grant of summary judgment by the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana) in favor of defendant physician in a wrongful death action arising out of the physician's alleged medical malpractice in delivering the child. The parents argued that Ind. Const. art. I, § 23 precluded the trial court's holding that their action was time-barred under Ind. Code § 34-18-7-1 (1998).


OVERVIEW: Although § 34-18-7-1 provided a two-year limitations period for filing medical malpractice claims, in the case of child patients, such a claim could be filed until the child reached eight years of age. The parents never filed a negligence action while their child was living, but they filed an action under the Child Wrongful Death Statute, Ind. Code § 34-23-2-1 (1998), when he died at the age of two. The two-year period had expired by then, but the parents argued that since the medical malpractice limitations statute had already been held applicable to wrongful death actions, its extension in cases involving injuries to children should likewise be applicable. The appellate court agreed. The parents were similarly situated to parents whose children had not died between expiration of the limitations period and their eighth birthdays, and yet their wrongful death action would be held time-barred under the physician's proposed interpretation of § 34-18-7-1 while the other parents' negligence action would not be. Such an unequal result would violate the privileges and immunities clause of Ind. Const. art. I, § 23.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Trusley v. State


No. 41A01-0403-CR-109


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


818 N.E.2d 110; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 2321



November 24, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by Trusley v. State, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 566 (Ind., June 17, 2005)
Superseded by, Remanded by Trusley v. State, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 537 (Ind., June 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE JOHNSON SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 41D02-0110-CF-158. The Honorable Cynthia Emkes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Matter is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A grand jury indicted defendant for neglect of a dependent, a Class B felony. The charge was amended to reckless homicide as a Class C felony. Defendant pled guilty. The Johnson Superior Court (Indiana) sentenced defendant to eight years, with two suspended. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the enhancement of her sentence violated her Sixth Amendment right to have a jury determine the facts on which the enhancement was based. The State argued that any Blakely error was harmless, as defendant admitted to the facts that would have supported one of the aggravating circumstances the trial court found - that defendant, a day care provider, was in a position of trust with respect to the victim and his family. The appellate court declined to hold that defendant's admission she was a day care provider, without more, necessarily substituted for a jury's determination she was in a position of trust with respect to the victim to such an extent that sentence enhancement was warranted.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded for resentencing.

 

609 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Howard v. State


No. 79A02-0403-CR-238


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


818 N.E.2d 469; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 2313



November 23, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Howard v. State, 831 N.E.2d 735, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 100 (Ind., 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Howard v. State, 2011 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1807 (Ind. Ct. App., Dec. 29, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 79D01-0205-FA-10. The Honorable Donald C. Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of Class A felony dealing in methamphetamine, Class C felony dealing in a Schedule IV controlled substance, Class D felony operating a vehicle while a habitual traffic violator, Class B misdemeanor false informing, and found to be a habitual substance offender, in the Tippecanoe Superior Court (Indiana). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the admission of evidence obtained from his search and seizure on the basis that the seat belt enforcement zone that led to his arrest was not reasonable and the search of his person and vehicle were improper. The appellate court disagreed, noting that, inter alia, defendant was pulled over only after officers observed him driving without a seat belt, he was detained only after giving officers the wrong name and the registration to another vehicle, and an inventory search was performed after officers properly impounded the vehicle for improper registration. Defendant also claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion for a mistrial on the basis that witnesses were being excused without the court asking jurors if they had questions. The appellate court found no error as the trial court informed jurors of the procedure for asking questions and was not required to inquire after each witness. Finally, defendant argued that he received an improper double enhancement. Because the appellate court found that defendant's habitual substance offender determination was the only enhancement, he was not the recipient of an improper double enhancement.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

610 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Wiggins v. State


No. 43A03-0312-CR-498


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


817 N.E.2d 652; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 2250



November 17, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE KOSCIUSKO SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 43D03-0211-FC-190. The Honorable Joe V. Sutton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Kosciusko Superior Court (Indiana) for operating a vehicle while intoxicated causing death and operating a vehicle while intoxicated causing serious bodily injury. Defendant argued that the trial court abused its discretion when it admitted the results of his urine toxicology test into evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had slowed and begun to make a left-hand turn into a gas station when he struck a motorcycle. The motorcycle driver was killed and his 11-year old nephew was injured. While speaking with defendant, a deputy did not observe any physical signs of intoxication, but had difficulty ascertaining defendant's physical condition because he was receiving medical treatment at the time. Defendant expressed some confusion as to what his address was. Without requesting permission or advising defendant in any way and without claiming on a hospital request form that he had probable cause to do so, the deputy asked the hospital staff to obtain blood and urine samples from defendant, and the hospital staff complied. The appellate court held the deputy did not properly attain defendant's consent to a portable breath test or chemical test without some objectively observed clear indication of intoxication, such as dilated pupils, telltale odor or failed field sobriety test(s). Defendant's difficulty in answering the deputy's questions was not significant enough, by itself, to provide the probable cause. Thus, the urine toxicology test results should not have been admitted into evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

 

611 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Gross v. State


Nos. 33A05-0402-CR-100, 33A01-0402-CR-79


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


817 N.E.2d 306; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 2233



November 12, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HENRY CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 33C01-0308-FD-50 and 33C01-0308-FD-51. The Honorable Mary G. Willis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Convictions reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants both appealed their convictions by the Henry Circuit Court (Indiana) for neglect of a dependent. Each defendant was convicted of two counts of neglect of a dependant. The issue for both defendants was whether there was sufficient evidence to support their convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendants lived together as roommates. During one occurrence, the female defendant had custody of her children, age five and age three. Also present were the male defendant's children, who were older, and defendant's brother. The brother decided to play a game with the older children called "hostage," where their wrists and ankles were taped together with light construction tape and the children competed to see who could break free first. While the female defendant was cutting the tape from behind the three-year-old's stroller with a pocketknife, the child reared back and sustained a superficial cut. On a second occasion children again took turns having their wrists and ankles taped and hopped about the house. The appellate court held that although the so-called "hostage" game was somewhat bizarre and not something many child development experts would condone, there was insufficient evidence that playing the game exposed the children to a substantial, actual, and appreciable risk of mental or physical harm. Furthermore, there was insufficient evidence that defendants were subjectively aware of a high probability that the children were endangered by the taping.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions were reversed.

 

612 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


City of Vincennes v. Emmons


No. 42A02-0402-CV-193


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


817 N.E.2d 291; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 2227



November 10, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by City of Vincennes v. Emmons, 831 N.E.2d 742, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 326 (Ind., 2005)
Superseded by City of Vincennes v. Emmons, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 54 (Ind., Jan. 25, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE KNOX SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 42D02-0006-OV-130. The Honorable Robert L. Arthur, Judge 42D02-0006-OV-132.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, appellant City brought proceedings against appellee landlords, alleging that the landlords failed to pay the annual landlord registration fee required by Vincennes, Ind., Code of Ordinances § 156.04 for multiple years in varying amounts. The Knox Superior Court (Indiana) found that the city Rental Housing Code, Vincennes, Ind., Code of Ordinances §§ 156.01-156.06 was unconstitutional. The City appealed.


OVERVIEW: The City argued that the landlords did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of the housing code because any injury to them was only speculative. The appellate court disagreed. Every two years, rental units were subject to a mandatory inspection, and it was clearly the landlords' interests that were implicated in the inspection. Therefore, the landlords had standing. In order to satisfy the requirements of Camara and thus pass muster under the Fourth Amendment, the housing code was required to give the landlords the option to consent and to include a warrant procedure to be followed in the event the landlords refused to consent to a search. The city Rental Housing Code did not, and it was therefore unconstitutional on its face. Because the ability to maintain a rental unit pursuant to the housing code was ultimately tied to the inspection of the unit, the constitutionally invalid provision was not distinct and separable from the remainder of the housing code.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

613 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Traylor v. State


No. 63A04-0309-CR-466


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


817 N.E.2d 611; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 2229



November 10, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Traylor v. State, 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 396 (Ind. Ct. App., Mar. 8, 2005)
Transfer denied by Traylor v. State, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 501 (Ind., May 20, 2005)
Transfer denied by Traylor v. State, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 502 (Ind., May 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE PIKE CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 63C01-0303-FA-00117. The Honorable Lee F. Baker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Pike Circuit Court (Indiana) convicting him on jury verdict of dealing in methamphetamine (by manufacturing it) and visiting a common nuisance. He challenged denial of his suppression motion, an alleged limitation on cross-examination, the sufficiency of the evidence, whether imposition of an enhanced sentence was proper, and various rulings regarding fees and bail.


OVERVIEW: Police investigating a tip regarding smells suggestive of a methamphetamine manufacturing operation approached a mobile home. Smelling chemicals and observing other "meth lab" evidence, they approached the house and arrested the occupants and others, including defendant. The appeals court held that under the totality of the circumstances, it was reasonable to have approached and entered the house without a warrant and that the evidence found there, including methamphetamine in process of manufacture, was sufficient to support conviction and a nuisance determination. Cross-examination was not limited where the trial judge merely warned the defense that certain questions could open the door to risky rebuttal. Under Apprendi and Blakely, defendant should not have been subject to an enhanced sentence without jury findings, since his criminal history was negligible. A drug fee should not have been assessed without a finding of means to pay, defendant's cash bail should have been returned to him, and, finally, his threats against the prosecutor and his family justified immediate revocation of bail as long as a hearing was held soon thereafter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction but vacated the sentence, as well as an order regarding payment of a drug fee and an order that his cash bail be retained. It remanded for resentencing and for a determination as to whether defendant had the means to pay a statutory drug fee and in what amount.

 

614 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Teeters v. State


No. 69A01-0312-CR-487


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


817 N.E.2d 275; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 2198



November 9, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Teeters v. State, 822 N.E.2d 984, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 1085 (Ind., Dec. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE RIPLEY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Carl Taul, Judge. Cause No. 69C01-0303-FC-005.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with battery while armed with a deadly weapon, a Class C felony, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-2-1(a)(3). A jury found defendant guilty as charged. The Ripley Circuit Court (Indiana) sentenced defendant to eight years at the Department of Corrections with three years suspended. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support her conviction. Defendant contested only one element of battery - that she did not touch the victim in a rude, insolent, or angry manner when she stabbed him. The appellate court concluded that the evidence produced at trial showed that defendant became angry with the victim, brandished a knife in an effort to intimidate him, and accidentally stabbed the victim instead of the couch. That evidence was sufficient for a reasonable fact finder to have concluded that defendant touched the victim in a rude, insolent, or angry manner. Defendant also contended that her sentence was inappropriate and was improperly enhanced. Defendant argued that her Sixth Amendment right to have the facts supporting the enhancement of her sentence tried to a jury was violated. Of the four aggravating factors used by the trial court, the only one at issue was that defendant was on probation at the time of the offense. Because a single aggravating factor was adequate to justify a sentence enhancement, the failure to have one of four factors proved beyond a reasonable doubt did not require reversal of defendant's enhanced sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

615 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Trimble v. State


No. 40A01-0311-CR-437


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


816 N.E.2d 83; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 2058



October 20, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by Trimble v. State, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 142 (Ind., Feb. 21, 2006)
Superseded by Trimble v. State, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 137 (Ind., Feb. 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE JENNINGS SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 40D01-0302-CM-116. The Honorable James Funke, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his convictions in the Jennings Superior Court (Indiana) for abandonment and neglect of an animal and harboring a non-immunized dog.


OVERVIEW: The officer pulled into defendant's driveway and saw a doghouse behind the house by the edge of the driveway. The officer knocked on the back door of defendant's house, when no one answered he went to the doghouse and pulled the dog out using the cable to which the dog was secured. On appeal, defendant argued that the warrantless search that resulted in the dog's seizure was improper because the doghouse was within an area where he had a reasonable expectation of privacy. The State asserted that the evidence was admissible under the "open fields" doctrine. The appellate court held that the warrantless search violated both the Indiana and United States Constitutions. Defendant had a reasonable expectation of privacy with respect to the doghouse and the officer's search, in the absence of exigent circumstances, was unreasonable under the totality of the circumstances. Among other things, the officer invaded defendant's curtilage when he left the obvious and direct route to the house and pulled the dog out of the doghouse. In addition, the officer walked into the yard even though he saw nothing from the driveway that would have given him suspicion a crime had occurred.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

 

616 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Irwin Mortg. Corp. v. Marion County Treasurer


No.49A04-0310-CV-536


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


816 N.E.2d 439; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 2015



October 18, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49D07-0303-PL-522. The Honorable Gerald S. Zore, Judge.
Irwin Mortg. Corp. v. Ind. Bd. of Tax Review, 775 N.E.2d 720, 2002 Ind. Tax LEXIS 64 (Ind. Tax Ct., 2002).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mortgage corporation challenged the decision of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which dismissed the mortgage corporation's complaint against appellees, a county treasurer, a county auditor, and a property tax assessment board of appeals. The mortgage company asserted federal claims pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 (1998) and state claims under the Indiana Tort Claims Act (ITCA), Ind. Code Ann. § 34-13-3-1 (1998) et seq.


OVERVIEW: The cause of action arose as a result of the mortgage corporation paying property taxes one day late on numerous parcels of real estate. The county treasurer assessed a penalty for the delinquent tax payment pursuant to Ind. Code Ann. § 6-1.1-37-10(a) (2003), which the mortgage corporation paid. The lawsuit was filed after the county auditor refused to refund the penalty. The trial court dismissed the complaint without specifying the grounds for the dismissal, though the motion for dismissal asserted that the actions were time-barred due to the applicable statute of limitations of two years to tort claims and because the mortgage corporation failed to file notice under the ITCA. The court held that the Journey's Account statute, Ind. Code Ann. § 34-11-8-1 (1998), saved the mortgage corporation's federal claims from the applicable statute of limitations. However, the notice requirements of the ITCA barred its state law claims because the mortgage corporation failed to demonstrate substantial compliance with the notice requirements of Ind. Code Ann. § 34-13-3-8 (1998).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the mortgage corporation's state law claims but reversed the dismissal of the § 1983 claims. The court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings with regard to the § 1983 claims.

 

617 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Combs v. Tolle


No. 08A02-0405-CV-422


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


816 N.E.2d 432; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 2002



October 12, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CARROLL CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 08C01-0209-MI-7. The Honorable Joseph W. Carey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner filed an objection to a petition to issue a tax deed which had been filed by appellee buyers at a tax sale. The Carroll Circuit Court (Indiana) issued an order directing the auditor to issue a tax deed. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner claimed that the property address changed due to the implementation a new system, and he did not receive notices sent to the old address. However, the owner did not ask the county auditor to correct his address. The owner argued that his statutory and due process rights were violated by an improper notice. The appellate court held that, since the owner did not argue to the trial court that Ind. Code § 6-1.1-25-4.5 was unconstitutional, he waived the argument on appeal. The buyers were required to send the notice of sale to the owner's last address, as shown in the county auditor's records. The buyers did send notices of sale and the filing to the owner's last address, as shown in those records. The buyers also sent the notice of filing to the owner at an alternate residence. The owner's wife signed for delivery, but the owner claimed that she did not give the notice to him. The auditor had no other records that linked the owner with a different address, and the auditor was not required to search other records to find a valid address. The buyers were entitled to rely on the auditor's official records, and the notices were properly sent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

618 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Clinic for Women, Inc. v. Brizzi


No. 49A05-0305-CV-259


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


814 N.E.2d 1042; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 1829



September 17, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by Clinic for Women v. Brizzi, 831 N.E.2d 735, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 70 (Ind., 2005)
Superseded by Clinic for Women, Inc. v. Brizzi, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 1034 (Ind., Nov. 23, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Gerald Zore, Judge. Cause No. 49D07-0303-PL-558.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant clinic challenged a decision from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which dismissed its complaint against appellee class of state prosecuting attorneys. The clinic's complaint sought to challenge the constitutionality of Ind. Code § 16-34-2-1.1, which was a statute requiring voluntary and informed consent to abortion.


OVERVIEW: The clinic challenged the constitutionality of Ind. Code § 16-34-2-1.1, claiming that the statute's requirement that women seeking abortions receive in-person counseling at least 18 hours before obtaining an abortion infringed the women's right to privacy under Ind. Const. art. I, § 1 by requiring two trips to the clinic. The clinic also claimed the requirement that abortion providers orally convey information specified in the statute to women seeking an abortion violated free speech under Ind. Const. art. I, § 9. When the complaint was dismissed under Ind. R. Trial P. 12(B)(6) for failure to state a claim, the clinic appealed. The court found that the privacy right in Ind. Const. art. I, § 1, protected the right to seek an abortion, and a hearing was necessary on whether the two-trip requirement was an impermissible material burden on that right. However, the statute was a valid exercise of the state's police power since it related to a legitimate state interest in making sure women gave informed consent to an abortion. Therefore, the statute did not infringe on the free speech rights in Ind. Const. art. I, § 9.


OUTCOME: The court reversed dismissal of the clinic's complaint and ordered that a hearing be held on whether the challenged statute imposed a material burden on the constitutional right to privacy.

Foster v. State


No. 02A04-0312-CR-644


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


813 N.E.2d 1236; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 1714



August 27, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 02D04-0201-FC-1. The Honorable Robert J. Schmoll, Magistrate.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to sexual misconduct with a minor as a class C felony. The Allen Superior Court (Indiana) sentenced defendant to four years in the department of correction with two years suspended and two years of probation, and then modified his sentence to three years suspended instead of two years. Later, the trial court revoked defendant's probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The conditions of defendant's probation included the following: "You will not possess or view any pornographic or sexually explicit material (including: books, magazines, computer images, internet files, photographs, VCR cassettes, film or other materials)." The trial court found that defendant violated his probation by possessing sexually explicit materials. Defendant argued that the condition of probation that he was found to have violated was impermissibly vague and that the finding that he violated a term and condition of his probation was unsupported by the evidence. The appellate court held that the condition was not sufficiently clear to inform defendant of what conduct would result in his being returned to prison. Consequently, this condition of probation was void for vagueness and the trial court abused its discretion by revoking defendant's probation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Wilder v. State


No. 71A03-0307-CR-284


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


813 N.E.2d 788; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 1639



August 18, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Wilder v. State, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 1049 (Ind., Nov. 10, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 71D08-9912-CF-744. The Honorable R. W. Chamblee, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana) that denied his motion to correct error after a jury found him guilty of murder, felony murder, and attempted robbery and the trial court sentenced him on the murder and attempted robbery counts. He argued that underrepresentation of African Americans in the venire violated the Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the manner in which jury venires were pulled in the county where he was tried, from six regions into which the 19 zip codes were divided, resulted in a venire, in his case, with only one African American. The appeals court held that defendant's bare assertion of unfairness did not meet his burden to show statistical underrepresentation resulting from the selection method used. On its own motion, the appeals court noticed that the trial court said it had merged the convictions of intentional and felony murder before sentencing him. There was nothing wrong with the sentences themselves, but, to avoid double jeopardy violations, if the trial court had in fact entered judgment on the felony murder count before claiming to merge the murder convictions (it was not clear from the record if this was in fact what the judge had done), it had let too many convictions stand. To sentence defendant on the intentional murder and underlying attempted robbery counts, it was necessary to vacate the felony murder conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions on which defendant had been sentenced, but vacated the felony murder conviction.

 

621 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Sanford v. Castleton Health Care Ctr., L.L.C.


No. 49A02-0310-CV-885


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


813 N.E.2d 411; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 1632



August 13, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Sanford v. Castleton Health Care Ctr., 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 2080 (Ind. Ct. App., Oct. 20, 2004)
Transfer dismissed by Sanford v. Castleton Health Care Ctr., 2006 Ind. LEXIS 199 (Ind., Feb. 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Gerald S. Zore, Judge. Cause No. 49D07-0301-CT-183.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff daughter, as personal representative of plaintiff mother's estate, appealed from an order of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) compelling arbitration of the estate's survival and wrongful death claims against defendant nursing home. The estate argued that the arbitration clause was unconscionable and illegal, that it had been deprived of the right to trial by jury, and that the clause was not binding on it as a nonparty.


OVERVIEW: The daughter placed her mother, who suffered from Alzheimer's Disease, in the nursing home under hurried circumstances in the midst of a care crisis. The daughter did not read much of the agreement and missed the arbitration clause. There was no showing of unconscionability, however, as the clause was prominently placed and nursing home staff were available to discuss the agreement with her. Shortly after her admission, the mother had a bad fall and developed other problems that soon led to her death. The appellate court upheld the validity of the clause. Not only was it not unconscionable, but it was also not forbidden consideration given in return for nursing home admission within the meaning of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1396r(c)(5)(A)(iii). The guarantee of a jury trial in civil cases under Ind. Const. art. I, § 20 could be waived, and that was accomplished by the arbitration clause. Finally, the estate could not argue that it was not bound by the agreement because it was not a party to it. Ind. Code § 34-23-1-1 made it clear that a personal representative could pursue a survival and wrongful death claim only subject to the same defenses that could have been raised against the decedent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Travis v. State


No. 34A05-0402-CR-98


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


812 N.E.2d 826; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 1467



July 28, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HOWARD SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 34D03-0209-CM-1602. The Honorable Douglas A. Tate, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Howard Superior Court (Indiana) convicting defendant of criminal trespass, a class A misdemeanor, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-43-2-2(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: While defendant was in a public park playing dice and gambling, a police officer encountered him. Defendant began to talk back to the police officer, who then ordered defendant to leave the park and placed him on a trespass list. Defendant was warned that he would be trespassing if he returned the park. Defendant was arrested two days later when he was seen sitting on a bench in the same park. There was insufficient evidence to convict defendant of criminal trespass in violation of Ind. Code § 35-43-2-2(a)(1). The State failed to show that defendant entered the park after having been denied entry by the park or its agent. While police had to enforce municipal ordinances pursuant to Ind. Code § 36-8-3-6(c)(3), the municipal ordinance, Kokomo, Ind., Mun. Code § 96.19, merely authorized an officer to order a person from a city park for misbehavior. The ordinance did not give the authority to ban a person from the park on a permanent basis. While Ind. Code § 35-43-2-2 permitted private property owners to permanently bar a person from the owner's property, the powers of police officers were limited by Ind. Code §§ 36-8-3-6, -10, neither of which granted such authority.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Gall v. State


No. 48A05-0305-CR-234


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


811 N.E.2d 969; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 1384



July 20, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Gall v. State, 822 N.E.2d 977, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 930 (Ind., 2004)
Related proceeding at Gall v. State, 2014 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 849 (Ind. Ct. App., June 25, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MADISON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Thomas Newman, Jr., Judge. Cause No. 48D03-0203-CF-95.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Madison Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him of dangerous possession of a firearm, criminal recklessness, and attempted murder. Defendant was sentenced to 30 years executed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was 16 at the time of the incident, had guests at his house who had an altercation. One guest's father came to pick her up, and as he started to drive a few of the guests away, defendant kicked in the door of his father's locked bedroom, retrieved a semi-automatic rifle, and fired at the car. Defendant was arrested and convicted of numerous offenses. On appeal, the court found defendant was properly charged in adult criminal court rather than in juvenile court, as the juvenile court lacked jurisdiction under Ind. Code § 31-30-1-4(a) (1998 & Supp. 2003). The jury reasonably inferred that defendant possessed the specific intent to commit the attempted murder. Exclusion of a witness's testimony as to defendant's possible motive to harm her was proper and even if erroneous, was harmless in the circumstances. Defendant's sentence was appropriate, as there were no mitigating factors found and several aggravating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Ledbetter v. Hunter


No. 49A02-0309-CV-770


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


810 N.E.2d 1095; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 1199



June 29, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by Ledbetter v. Hunter, 822 N.E.2d 982, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 1015 (Ind., 2004)
Superseded by Ledbetter v. Hunter, M.D., 842 N.E.2d 810, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 138 (Ind., Feb. 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49D02-9404-CT-384. The Honorable Kenneth H. Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother challenged the order of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which dismissed the mother's medical malpractice claim defendants, two attending physicians and a hospital, under the Privileges and Immunities Clause of Ind. Const. art. I, § 23. Originally, the plaintiff was the mother's child. Upon the death of the child, the mother was substituted as plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: The action arose from alleged medical malpractice by the attending physicians, which triggered birth complications to the child that caused serious and permanent physical and mental injuries. Within two years of the child's 18th birthday, the action was filed, which was in compliance with the law at the time the child was born. However, after the child's birth, the law changed and the Indiana Medical Malpractice Act, Ind. Code Ann. § 34-18-7-1-1(b), made the statute of limitations from the child's 20th birthday to her eighth birthday. Unaware of the change in the law, the child commenced suit within two years of her 18th birthday. The court held that § 34-18-7-1-1(b) was unconstitutional as it applied to minors, in that it violated the Privileges and Immunities Clause. The court held that that the classification between minors injured by medical malpractice and minor victims of other torts was no longer reasonably related to the goal of maintaining sufficient medical treatment and controlling malpractice insurance costs. Further, within the class of minors injured by medical malpractice, not all minors were treated equally.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of dismissal and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Nagy v. Evansville-Vanderburgh Sch. Corp.


No. 82A01-0308-CV-299


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


808 N.E.2d 1221; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 1007



May 28, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by Nagy v. Evansville-Vanderburgh Sch. Corp., 822 N.E.2d 977, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 864 (Ind., 2004)
Superseded by, Remanded by Nagy v. Evansville-Vanderburgh Sch. Corp., 844 N.E.2d 481, 2006 Ind. LEXIS 271 (Ind., Mar. 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable J. Douglas Knight, Judge. Cause No. 82D03-0210-PL-4388.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents, in a class action brought on their own behalf and on behalf of their children, appealed from an order of the Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana) that granted defendant school corporation's cross-motion for summary judgment as to the parents' claim that a $ 20 student fee violated Ind. Const. art. 8, § 1. The corporation cross-appealed from a finding of violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV guarantees as to poor children.


OVERVIEW: To balance its budget, the corporation instituted the student fee, which was used for many purposes, including paying certain educational staff members. The appellate court considered primarily whether the fee violated Ind. Const. art. 8, § 1. Looking at the provision in historical context and with attention to the plain meaning of "tuition," which was forbidden in the guarantee of common schools, the appeals court held that it related to teaching or instruction. Even though the fee was not very large, if it were allowed, there would be no way to prevent schools in the future from charging larger amounts in order to avoid raising taxes, thereby creating the very evil the framers had sought to avoid when they tried to assure an education for all.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order as to the Indiana constitutional claim and remanded the matter with instructions to enter summary judgment in favor of the parents.

Herron v. State


No. 75A04-0306-CR-289


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


808 N.E.2d 172; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 887



May 17, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Herron v. State, 822 N.E.2d 968, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 637 (Ind., July 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE STARKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable David P. Matsey, Judge. Cause No. 75C01-0212-FA-7.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the Starke Superior Court (Indiana) for aiding, inducing, or causing voluntary manslaughter under Ind. Code §§ 35-41-2-4 and 35-42-1-3, a Class A felony. Defendant contended that the testimony of the principal that he participated in the killing was insufficient evidence to support his conviction, and that his sentence was inappropriate.


OVERVIEW: While drinking in their apartment, defendant and his roommate became angered with their guest. Defendant left the room, returning and getting into a fight with the guest. He had left the room to don his prosthetic arm, which had a hook at the end. Testimony of his roommate showed that defendant had hit the victim, shouted to the roommate to continue beating the victim, and helped dispose of the victim. The victim's body showed that he was hit with a hammer and probably a screw driver. Defendant's own blood, but none of the victim, was found on his prosthetic arm and the roommate testified that defendant had told him that he would wash the area and his arm with bleach to eliminate any DNA. On appeal, the court found the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction. The court held that the uncorroborated testimony of the roommate as an accomplice was sufficient, rejecting defendant's contention that the "incredible dubiosity" rule applied. The court then considered defendant's sentencing appeal, holding that under Ind. R. App. P. 7(B), because his sentence was within the range and appropriate in light of the nature of his offense, it was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Kelver v. State


No. 46A03-0308-CR-322


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


808 N.E.2d 154; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 879



May 13, 2004,


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAPORTE SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 46D03-0209-IF-7790. The Honorable Paul J. Baldoni, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the LaPorte Superior Court (Indiana) that convicted him of violating Ind. Code § 9-19-10-2, the seat belt law. He argued on appeal that the statute violated his equal privileges and immunities guaranteed under Ind. Const. art. I, § 23 and denied him substantive due process.


OVERVIEW: Under Indiana's motor vehicle registration law, defendant's utility vehicle could have been registered as either a passenger car or a truck. He registered it as a passenger car and was arrested for noncompliance with the seat belt law, which applied only to passenger vehicles. The appeals court adhered to its earlier Price decision and found no unequal treatment depriving defendant of his privileges and immunities in the legislative decision to treat passenger vehicles and trucks differently, even though the categories overlapped. Defendant had waived a similar federal equal protection argument. The appeals court also found no substantive due process violation. It could not be said that a driver's right to drive as he chose was a property right or that it rose to the level of such issues as reproductive decisions, in which substantive due process was sometimes invoked. Moreover, the law was rationally related to the proper state aim of reducing traffic fatalities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a mobile home park and mobile home owners, filed a complaint against appellee town board of trustees in the Morgan Superior Court (Indiana), for injunctive relief enjoining the board from denying the park and the owners the right to park a mobile home in the mobile home park. The board counterclaimed for an order to remove the mobile home from the town. The trial court denied the complaint for a permanent injunction.

However, the ordinance specifically provided in a separate paragraph that mobile homes that were five years of age or older were restricted from being moved into the town for occupancy. As a result, the board voted against approving the requested license for the mobile home owners because their mobile home was at least five years old at the time the application for the license was submitted. On appeal, the court found that (1) the ordinance was not an ultra vires act or unenforceable as a matter of law; and (2) the ordinance did not violate the Equal Privileges Clause of Ind. Const. art. I, § 23.

Sharp v. State


No. 18A02-0309-CR-769


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Sharp v. State, 835 N.E.2d 1079, 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 1993 (Ind. Ct. App., Oct. 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE DELAWARE SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 18D02-9902-CF-13. The Honorable Richard A. Dailey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Delaware Superior Court (Indiana) entered a judgment that denied defendant probationer's motion to dismiss the State's petition to revoke probation and ruled that the probationer, pursuant to statutory law, was required to submit a DNA sample for inclusion in the Indiana DNA Data Base. The probationer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The probationer was convicted of burglary and received a sentence of probation. About seven months after his probation expired, his probation officer petitioned to revoke his probation and alleged, inter alia, that he failed to pay restitution, that he had failed to complete a drug treatment program, and that he was found in contempt of court after the probationary period ended because he had not paid child support. The probation officer knew of the violations at or near the time they occurred. The probationer moved to dismiss on the ground that the petition was untimely filed, but the trial court denied the motion. It then revoked his probation. It also overruled his objection that submitting a DNA sample was not required of probationers and ruled that a state statute required that he submit such a sample. On appeal, the appellate court agreed that pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-38-2-3(a)(2)(B), the petition to revoke was not filed within the required 45 days after the State received notice of the probation violations. However, it found his argument that the statute requiring the DNA sample was unconstitutional was waived since that claim had not been presented to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The trial court's ruling that required the probationer to submit a DNA sample was affirmed, but the trial court's denial of probationer's motion to dismiss the State's petition to revoke probation was reversed.

Garnelis v. Ind. State Dep't of Health


No. 49A04-0308-CV-429


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


806 N.E.2d 365; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 677



April 20, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49D05-0101-CT-84. The Honorable Gary Miller, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a husband and his wife, appealed an order from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment to defendant Indiana State Department of Health, and which denied a cross-motion for summary judgment, on the issue of whether the husband complied with the notice provisions of the Indiana Tort Claims Act (TCA), Ind. Code § 34-13-3-6(a), in presenting a personal injury claim to the Department.


OVERVIEW: The husband was tested for HIV at a clinic, which forwarded the sample to the Department. The husband was told he was HIV positive, but was not instructed to undergo re-testing. He was monitored for eight years, but was not re-tested. On a trip out of the country, the husband was required to submit to an HIV test, which returned a negative result. The husband served a tort claim notice on the Department. A complaint was also filed alleging the Department negligently performed the original HIV test and negligently failed to order retesting. The Department moved for summary judgment claiming the notice was not filed within 270 days after the loss occurred, as required by the TCA. After the trial court granted the Department's motion, the husband appealed. The Department argued the husband's loss occurred when the erroneous positive result was given, so the claim was not timely. The husband argued the negative result eight years later triggered the notice period. The court found the statutory period to file the notice was triggered when the husband's personal injury claim arose, which was when he discovered he was not HIV positive. The summary judgment grant was improper.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment for the Department, it reversed the denial of the husband's cross-motion for summary judgment, and it remanded for further proceedings.

 

631 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Stytle v. Angola Die Casting Co.


No. 93A02-0311-EX-970


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


806 N.E.2d 339; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 681



April 20, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Stytle v. Angola Die Casting Co., 822 N.E.2d 972, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 767 (Ind., Aug. 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE WORKER'S COMPENSATION BOARD. The Honorable G. Terence Coriden, Chairman. Cause No. C-154593.
Stytle v. Angola Die Casting Co., 783 N.E.2d 316, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 174 (Ind. Ct. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant applied for adjustment of claim against appellee, his former employer. He late amended his application to include appellee company, which he alleged was the former employer's successor. The Worker's Compensation Board (Indiana) dismissed the matter on grounds that the claim was time-barred. The claimant appealed, arguing that Ind. Code § 22-3-7-9(f) as applied to him violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 12.


OVERVIEW: The claimant, who was totally disabled, alleged he was diagnosed with possible Alzheimer's disease. A psychiatrist concluded that his exposure to aluminum while working for his former employer was the likely cause of his cognitive problems. The claimant filed his application more than 10 years after the last date on which he worked for the worker, and it was undisputed that his disability occurred more than two years after the last day of his last exposure to the hazards of his disease. Therefore, Ind. Code § 22-3-7-9(f) barred his claim. The claimant alleged he did not know, and in the exercise of reasonable diligence, could not have discovered that he had suffered a disease-causing exposure in the course of and arising out of his employment before the two-year period of repose expired. Therefore, he argued, § 22-3-7-9(f) was unconstitutional as applied to him. The appellate court held that precedent from the state supreme court compelled it to conclude that § 22-3-7-9(f), a statute of repose rather than a statute of limitations, did not violate Ind. Const. art. I, § 12 (which guaranteed citizens' access to the courts) as applied in the case.


OUTCOME: The dismissal was affirmed.

 

632 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Roberts v. ACandS, Inc.


No. 93A02-0309-EX-783


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


806 N.E.2d 1; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 575



April 6, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Roberts v. ACandS, Inc., 872 N.E.2d 217, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 1857 (Ind. Ct. App., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE WORKER'S COMPENSATION BOARD OF INDIANA. Cause No. O-159799. The Honorable G. Terrence Coriden, Chair.
PSI Energy, Inc. v. Roberts, 802 N.E.2d 468, 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 112 (Ind. Ct. App., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Board's decision reversed; cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Worker's Compensation Board of Indiana dismissed appellant former employee's claim against appellee former employer for worker's compensation benefits, ruling that because the employee had settled with one or more third parties, pursuant to Ind. Code § 22-3-7-36(b), the employer had no further liability to compensate him. The employee appealed, claiming, inter alia, that the dismissal was premature.


OVERVIEW: As a result of working with asbestos-containing products, the employee developed terminal malignant peritoneal mesothelioma. He and his wife filed a civil suit for damages against a number of defendants and accepted payment pursuant to several settlement agreements. A jury returned a verdict in their favor against several other defendants, including the employer, but there was no evidence that the judgment was paid and accepted. The employee argued that § 22-3-7-36(b) did not bar his claim against the employer until his third-party action was fully concluded by settlement or judgment which was procured and paid. The appellate court agreed. Even though the employee had settled with some defendants and had been paid by them, his third party action was not fully concluded because the judgment in his favor had not yet been paid. Therefore, the Board's dismissal of the employee's application for worker's compensation benefits was premature.


OUTCOME: The decision of the Board was reversed and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.

Fitzgerald v. State


No. 28A01-0306-CR-199


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


805 N.E.2d 857; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 574



April 6, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE GREENE SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 28D01-0205-FB-335. The Honorable J. David Holt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Greene Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him of sexual misconduct with a minor in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-4-9 (Supp. 2003). The trial court imposed the presumptive sentence as well as a term of probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a friend of the victim's father, and eventually the minor victim and defendant entered into a "romantic relationship," which resulted in the victim becoming pregnant and giving birth to a baby girl. Defendant was charged and convicted, and he was sentenced to 10 years' imprisonment, of which three years were suspended, as well as a term of probation. The trial court found that due to the balancing of the aggravating and mitigating circumstances, the presumptive sentence was appropriate, and further, that any sentence less than 10 years would depreciate the seriousness of the crime. On appeal, the court found that although two aggravating factors lacked record support - that the crime was likely to recur and that the victim was impeded in her future plans by having a child - no reversal of the sentence was required. The court found that the sentence imposed was appropriate. However, a probation condition authorizing searches by the probation department was violative of U.S. Const. amend. IV. Other conditions imposed were found to lack sufficient specificity to properly inform defendant of which conduct would constitute a probation violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence, but remanded the matter back to the trial court with instructions to revise the probation conditions in order to: 1) reflect that any search must be reasonable; 2) set out any prohibition against materials related to deviant interests and behaviors with more specificity; and 3) reconsider and clarify the prohibition against defendant's presence where children congregated.

Smith v. State


No. 64A03-0306-CR-204


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


804 N.E.2d 1246; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 446



March 23, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by Smith v. State, 812 N.E.2d 808, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 609 (Ind., 2004)
Affirmed in part and superseded in part by Smith v. State, 825 N.E.2d 783, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 385 (Ind., Apr. 20, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE PORTER SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 64D01-0210-FB-9017. The Honorable Roger V. Bradford, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of felony attempted rape, felony battery, felony criminal confinement, and felony intimidation, and alleged him to be a repeat sexual offender due to two prior rape convictions. The Porter Superior Court (Indiana) found defendant to be a repeat sexual offender and sentenced him to 20 years on the underlying convictions and to an additional 10 years based on his repeat sexual offender status. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court abused its discretion in instructing the jury that the uncorroborated testimony of one witness alone was sufficient to sustain a conviction so long as it convinced the jury beyond a reasonable doubt as to defendant's guilt on each essential element of the charge. The appellate court concluded that defendant waived the issue for review, having failed to object to the instruction at trial, and that, even if it had not been waived, any error was harmless as the subject testimony was corroborated. Defendant also contended that Ind. Code § 35-50-2-14 violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 19, because it does not allow a jury to determine the law and the facts regarding his status as a repeat sexual offender following a jury trial and conviction on the underlying felony. The appellate court concluded that the right to have a jury determine the facts and the law regarding a defendant's repeat sexual offender status existed by virtue of Ind. Const. art. I, § 19, and therefore, Ind. Code § 35-50-2-14 was unconstitutional on its face and as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed. The adjudication that defendant was a repeat sexual offender and corresponding sentence enhancement were vacated.

 

635 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Adams v. State


No. 49A02-0307-CR-568


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


804 N.E.2d 1169; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 430



March 16, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G02-0205-FB-155588. The Honorable Robert Altice, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with numerous criminal offenses, including Class A misdemeanor distribution of obscene matter and exhibition of obscene matter based on the images that had been displayed on the computer. Defendant's motion to suppress was granted. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) found defendant guilty of the aforementioned charges and sentenced defendant to concurrent terms of 180 days on each count. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that Indiana's obscenity statute was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to give the type of notice that would enable an ordinary citizen to comprehend precisely what conduct was prohibited. The appellate court found said argument waived on appeal. Defendant also contended that the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions because the materials he displayed and sold were not obscene and were displayed in the privacy of his own home. The appellate court concluded that it was within the fact finder's prerogative to find the materials, displaying a woman having sexual intercourse with a dog and a woman having oral sex with a horse, obscene. In addition, because defendant displayed the images in his home for the purpose of making a sale, his actions were not constitutionally protected. Finally, defendant's claim that his convictions violated double jeopardy principles failed, as each conviction required proof of an element the other did not; the conviction for exhibition required proof that defendant "showed" the obscene material, whereas the conviction for distribution required proof defendant did in fact distribute the material.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

636 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Woolley v. Wash. Twp. of Marion County Small Claims Court


No. 49A05-0309-CV-485


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


804 N.E.2d 761; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 325



March 3, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49D05-0204-MI-737. The Honorable Gary L. Miller, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen, an employee of an attorney who sued a law firm on behalf of several individuals and sought to compel appellee small claims court to allow him to inspect and copy an affidavit under the Indiana Access to Public Records Act (APRA), Ind. Code § 5-14-3, sought review of the grant of summary judgment by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) in favor of the small claims court.


OVERVIEW: The affidavit concerned the procedure for filing claims in the small claims court and it confirmed the judge's policy that no complaint tendered for filing in her court would be rejected by the clerical staff for lack of attachments. An attorney of the law firm asked the judge to sign it and she did not retain a copy of the affidavit. The parties to the lawsuit, which involved the affidavit, filed a stipulation of dismissal with prejudice pursuant to a settlement agreement. The appellate court held the citizen was not required to state a reason for his request. Thus, there was still an issue as to whether the citizen rightfully had access to the affidavit. The small claims court did not create the affidavit. Nor did it retain, maintain, or file the affidavit. The judge signed the affidavit as a witness. She was not acting in her official capacity. Because it was not a public record, the small claims court was not required to follow the mandates of the APRA with regard to the timeliness of its response and a reason for denying the citizen's request. Also, the small claims court did not have a copy of the affidavit and therefore could not produce it.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

637 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Conklin v. Fisher


No. 91A02-0310-CV-835


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


803 N.E.2d 693; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 238



February 19, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE WHITE CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 91C01-0110-CT-15. The Honorable Robert W. Thacker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the White Circuit Court (Indiana), which, after judgment was held in favor of appellee in appellant's negligence suit, ordered appellant to pay the trial court for jury per diem/mileage costs, jury lunch and dinner costs, and bailiff reimbursement for jury expenses.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sued appellee for negligence and a jury held against him after finding appellant 85 percent at fault and appellee 15 percent at fault. The trial court then ordered appellant to pay jury costs. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred in imposing jury costs against appellant as the losing party. The record did not reflect that appellee paid the jury's per diem or mileage costs, the jury's lunch and dinner costs, or the bailiff reimbursement for jury expenses. As such, appellant was therefore not obliged to "indemnify" her for such. Rather, the costs imposed on appellant seemed to be in the nature of a penalty imposed on him as the losing party and they were therefore improper. The jury costs the trial court assessed were not filing fees nor were they statutory witness fees. As a result, the trial court erred in assessing jury costs and expenses against appellant in the absence of authorization by statute or court rule.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court.

Sherrell v. N. Cmty. Sch. Corp.


No. 80A02-0304-CV-367


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


801 N.E.2d 693; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 28



January 16, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPTON CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 80C01-0105-MI-133. The Honorable Thomas Lett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant student appealed a judgment by the Tipton Circuit Court (Indiana), which upheld a decision by appellee school board to expel him from school; the student claimed that the decision was arbitrary and capricious, because his threat did not constitute "unlawful activity" under Ind. Code § 20-8.1-5.1-9.


OVERVIEW: While off school grounds, the student threatened to bring a gun to school and shoot students. The school board and the trial court upheld the decision to expel the student pursuant to Ind. Code § 20-8.1-5.1-9. The appellate court held that, although the student's expulsion had ended, it would consider the allegedly moot issue as a question of great public importance. The student's contention that he did not engage in unlawful activity was based on the faulty premise that a prosecutor had to make this determination, rather than on a cogent argument asserting that his threat to shoot his schoolmates did not constitute unlawful activity. As such, the student failed to establish that the board's decision to expel him was arbitrary and capricious, as defined by Ind. Code § 4-21.5-5-14(d).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

639 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


McGill v. Ling


No. 49A02-0303-CV-174


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


801 N.E.2d 678; 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 14



January 15, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by McGill v. Ling, 812 N.E.2d 807, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 560 (Ind., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49D12-9908-CT-1084. The Honorable Robyn L. Moberly, Judge.
Majors v. State, 773 N.E.2d 231, 2002 Ind. LEXIS 650 (Ind., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant widow sued appellees, physicians, hospital trustees, a nurse, and a county, in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) for medical malpractice. The trial court granted appellees' summary judgment motions, and the widow appealed.


OVERVIEW: The nurse killed six patients at the hospital, and worked there when the widow's husband died there. The appellate court held it could hear the widow's argument under the Journey's Account Statute, Ind. Code § 34-11-8-1, although the trial court granted a motion to strike that argument; despite granting the motion, counsel argued the issue and the trial court ruled on it. Under Ind. Code §§ 34-18-7-1 and 34-18-8-4, the widow had to bring an action before the Indiana Department of Insurance within two years of her husband's death, which she did not do. She had timely joined state and federal class action suits, but they were dismissed for lack of jurisdiction. Under the Journey's Account Statute, Ind. Code § 34-11-8-1, an action dismissed because it was brought in the wrong court could be refiled in the right court within three years. This statute did not save the widow's case, based on the prior class actions, or under the rule that she could file with the Department of Insurance before the class actions were dismissed, because those actions did not allege medical malpractice, and, for § 34-11-8-1 to apply, the later suit had to continue the prior suit.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.
