Alexander v. PSB Lending Corp.


No. 82A04-0212-CV-592


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


800 N.E.2d 984; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 2413



December 31, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Alexander v. PSB Lending Corp., 812 N.E.2d 805, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 487 (Ind., May 21, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 82C01-0111-CP-654. The Honorable Carl A. Heldt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lendees and a putative class, who had obtained loans secured by second mortgages, sought review of the judgment of the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana) which dismissed all nine lendees' cases against defendant non-holders of the loans. All nine complaints alleged similar violations of the Indiana Uniform Consumer Credit Code (IUCCC), namely, that excessive origination fees were charged on their second mortgage loans.


OVERVIEW: The complaints did not allege that the 64 non-holders were current or former holders of the second mortgage loans at issue, nor did they allege any relationship, contractual or otherwise. Rather, the complaints only contended that the non-holders held promissory notes related to the mortgage loans made to the lendees and the putative class members. The appellate court held the lendees failed to establish any personal stake in their lawsuits against the non-holders, and could not establish any injury or harm caused by the non-holders. Even assuming the loan origination fees were excessive, the lendees could not recover from the non-holders, who had no alleged connection to them or their loans. In short, the non-holders were not proper defendants. The dismissal of the non-holders on the basis of standing was proper. Also, the "class" had not been certified. The complaints were merely proposed class actions. Thus, there was no standing regarding the classwide basis against the non-holders. Neither of two defendant lenders could have relied upon or acted in conformity with a letter written after the loans were made. Therefore, the "safe harbor" provision of the IUCCC was inapplicable.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the grant of two lenders' motions to dismiss and remanded to the trial court for matters consistent with the proceedings. The judgment was affirmed as to the non-holders. Thus, the judgment was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and the matter was remanded.

Flowers v. Flowers


No. 48A05-0301-CV-34


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


799 N.E.2d 1183; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 2283



December 9, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MADISON SUPERIOR COURT III. The Honorable Stephen D. Clase, Master Commissioner. The Honorable Thomas Newman, Jr., Judge. Cause No. 48D03-9403-DR-135.



DISPOSITION: Case was remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner former husband appealed an order of the Madison Superior Court III (Indiana), regarding the husband's overpayment of an alleged child support arrearage.


OVERVIEW: The Indiana Title IV-D agency notified the husband of a significant arrearage in his child support payments. The husband responded immediately, contesting the existence of any arrearage and providing the agency with documentation of his payments. He then received correspondence with language that indicated that the matter had been resolved. Nonetheless, the agency, acting pursuant to Ind. Code § 31-16-15 but without notice to the husband, issued an order for employer withholding of child support. That action resulted in an overpayment of child support. On appeal, the husband asserted that § 31-16-15 was unconstitutional, that his due process rights had been violated, and that the trial court miscalculated the amount of overpayment. The court held that (1) the husband had waived his constitutional challenge to § 31-16-15; (2) the agency violated the husband's due process rights when it failed to follow the notice and hearing requirements of Ind. Code § 31-16-15-7 before issuing the withholding order; (3) the trial court failed to provide a coherent basis for its overpayment determination; and (4) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the husband attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case with instructions that the trial court first determine whether the agency possessed statutory authority to initiate the proceeding against the husband, and if so, to set forth a calculation of the proper overpayment to be credited to the husband. In the event the agency was without authority, the overpayment was to be determined and the withholding order was to be terminated.

Pinkins v. State


No. 45A03-0301-PC-30


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


799 N.E.2d 1079; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 2279



December 8, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Pinkins v. State, 812 N.E.2d 797, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 218 (Ind., 2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Pinkins v. Buss, 2007 U.S. App. LEXIS 2959 (7th Cir. Ind., Feb. 8, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 45G01-9001-CF-0005. The Honorable Richard W. Maroc, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of trial court and post-conviction court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, defendant challenged a judgment on jury verdict of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) that convicted him of rape, robbery, and criminal deviate conduct and from a judgment of the same court that denied his petition for post-conviction relief, sought on grounds of newly discovered evidence and counsel ineffectiveness.


OVERVIEW: Strong circumstantial evidence connected defendant and four other men to the abduction, robbery, and repeated rapes of the victim. In his direct appeal, defendant challenged various evidentiary rulings and an instruction, but the appeals court held that allowing a highway maintenance worker to testify regarding auto glass shattering was only harmless error, and that evidence about defendant's frequenting of strip clubs did not relate to misconduct at all. An instruction regarding the basis for finding defendant guilty as an associate of his co-defendants correctly stated Indiana law, despite overruled case law to the contrary. Post-conviction relief was also unavailable. Furthermore, since none of the objections counsel failed to raise during trial could have succeeded and affected defendant's outcome, the failure to object was also not ineffective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both judgments.

C.R.M. v. State


No. 42A05-0304-JV-204


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


799 N.E.2d 555; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 2236



December 4, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE KNOX SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 42D01-0206-JD-23. The Honorable W. Timothy Crowley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded for delinquency proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial of his motion to dismiss the State's petition alleging delinquency in the Knox Superior Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed a delinquency petition under Ind. Code § 35-48-4-11(1) subjected him to double jeopardy when, based on the same possession of marijuana, he had already been subjected to a forfeiture under Ind. Code § 34-24-1-1. While forfeiture under Ind. Code § 34-24-1-1 was tied to criminal activity, the government was not required to establish scienter. Serving more than a punitive purpose, civil forfeiture proceedings advanced diverse legislative interests; while punishing and deterring those who have engaged in illegal drug activity, forfeiture also advanced other non-punitive, remedial legislative goals. This evidence did not provide the clearest proof necessary to show that the proceeding was criminal. Therefore, an in rem forfeiture under Ind. Code § 34-24-1-1 was civil for purposes of the Fifth Amendment's Double Jeopardy Clause. Because civil forfeiture under Ind. Code § 34-24-1-1 was not punishment for Fifth Amendment purposes, the Double Jeopardy Clause was not violated when defendant was required to forfeit $ 550 and then was alleged to be a delinquent. Denial of defendant's motion to dismiss the delinquency petition was proper.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was affirmed and remanded.

Levy v. State


No. 49A02-0301-CR-28


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


799 N.E.2d 71; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 2199



November 26, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Levy v. State, 812 N.E.2d 791, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 76 (Ind., Jan. 9, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. CRIMINAL DIVISION, ROOM 7. The Honorable William Nelson, Judge. Cause No. 49F07-0111-CM-216700.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with the unauthorized practice of law. Defendant filed a motion seeking dismissal of the charges. The Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division, Room 7 (Indiana), denied the motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the supreme court was granted exclusive and original jurisdiction of matters concerning the unauthorized practice of law by Ind. Const. art. 7, § 4. Consequently, he asserted that the superior court had no jurisdiction to try him for a violation of Ind. Code § 33-1-5-1. Further, he claimed that the enactment of Ind. Code § 33-1-5-1 by the General Assembly amounted to a violation of the separation of powers between the legislative and judicial branches of government, in contravention of Ind. Const. art. 3, § 1. The appellate court concluded that the grant of original jurisdiction in Ind. Const. art. 7, § 4 did one thing--it gave the supreme court the power to entertain and decide all cases involving the issue of unauthorized practice of law. However, it did not give the supreme court the power to hear cases concerning the unauthorized practice of law to the exclusion of other courts. Thus, the appellate court held that trial courts appropriately had jurisdiction to conduct trials in which an individual was charged with the unauthorized practice of law under Ind. Code § 33-1-5-1. The appellate court further found no constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Bowyer v. Ind. Dep't of Natural Res.


No. 09A02-0303-CV-259


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


798 N.E.2d 912; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 2156



November 21, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Bowyer v. Ind. Dep't of Natural Res., 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 550 (Ind. Ct. App., Mar. 20, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CASS CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 09C01-0001-CP-5. The Honorable Julian L. Ridlen, Judge.
Garling v. Ind. Dep't of Natural Res., 756 N.E.2d 1029, 2001 Ind. App. LEXIS 1801 (Ind. Ct. App., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Indiana Department of Natural Resources was granted a temporary restraining order (TRO) ordering appellant landowner to cease any and all excavation and construction activities below the shoreline of a lake. The landowner ceased all activities that required entering the lake's waters. The Cass Circuit Court (Indiana) found the landowner in contempt for violating the TRO, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Department alleged that the landowner was dumping construction debris into the lake and altering its shoreline without a permit. The landowner was found to be in contempt of the TRO based on construction done below the shoreline. On appeal, the landowner argued that the trial court abused its discretion in finding him in contempt because, inter alia, the TRO failed to give any definition of the word "shoreline." The appellate court concluded that said failure rendered the TRO inherently ambiguous. The lack of clarity and certainty as to what constituted the lake's "shoreline," and hence what the landowner was prohibited from doing, meant that the trial court abused its discretion by holding the landowner in contempt. Although the Department presented evidence of where it eventually calculated the "shoreline" to be, it presented no evidence that the landowner was aware of its calculation, made several months after the TRO was entered. The Department, therefore, failed to establish that the definition of "shoreline" was so obvious that the landowner was on clear notice of what he could and could not do so as to support the conclusion that he willfully violated the TRO.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

Allen v. State


No. 49A04-0212-CR-605


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


798 N.E.2d 490; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 2111



November 13, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G20-0105-CF-118333. CRIMINAL DIVISION, ROOM 20. The Honorable David Shaheed, Judge Pro Tem.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division (Indiana), which convicted him of possession of cocaine and a firearm under Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6 and possession of cocaine under Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress, that the evidence was not sufficient to sustain the convictions, and that § 35-48-4-6 was unconstitutionally overbroad.


OVERVIEW: During the execution of a search warrant issued as part of a murder investigation, police discovered firearms and cocaine in defendant's apartment. Affirming defendant's convictions, the court first held that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress because (1) the information provided in support of the warrant affidavit was presumptively reliable; (2) the information was not stale because the probable cause continued to exist at the time of the search; (3) there was a fair probability that the weapons would be found in the apartment where the murder suspect spent a lot of time; and (4) a pistol was an object that might reasonably fit inside a cigar box. The court then held that the evidence was sufficient because the police found cocaine and a receipt for a handgun in defendant's name, drugs were found in plain view and in close proximity to items owned by defendant, and defendant made a furtive gesture towards the officers. Finally, the court held that defendant's constitutional challenge to Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6 was waived because defendant failed to raise the issue by motion to dismiss as required by Ind. Code § 35-34-1-4(c).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

Williams v. State


No. 34A02-0212-CR-1084


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


798 N.E.2d 457; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 2093



November 10, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HOWARD SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 34D03-0203-CM-400. The Honorable David A. Cox, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with domestic battery and convicted after a bench trial in the Howard Superior Court (Indiana). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction because the State did not prove that he was living with the victim as if he were her spouse, and the State did not prove that he touched the victim in a rude, insolent, or angry manner, causing injury to her. In affirming defendant's conviction, the appellate court noted that the record revealed that defendant and the victim were cohabiting and had an ongoing romantic relationship at the time of the incident. It was therefore reasonable for the trier of fact to infer that they lived together as if they were spouses, and the evidence was such that a reasonable trier of fact could have found defendant guilty of domestic battery beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

648 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Sec. Trust Corp. v. Estate of Fisher


No. 02A03-0210-CV-353


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


797 N.E.2d 789; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1971



October 16, 2003, Decided  
October 16, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Sec. Trust Corp. v. Fisher, 812 N.E.2d 796, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 179 (Ind., Feb. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Daniel G. Heath, Judge. Cause No. 02D01-0107-CP-1355.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, an investment advisor and the company with which he was associated, sought interlocutory review of a partial summary judgment of the Allen Superior Court (Indiana), in a rescission action, ruling that a viatical settlement contract purchased by plaintiff investor (represented on appeal, after his death, by his personal representative) was a security as defined by Ind. Code § 32-2-1-1(k) even before that statute was amended.


OVERVIEW: The viatical settlement contract (a contract under which the investor received the right to recover the proceeds of a life insurance contract after the terminally ill insured, who had already received discounted proceeds, died) purchased by the investor through the advisor had never been registered under the Indiana Securities Act. When the investor decided to rescind the contract for failure to register it, the advisor argued that viatical settlement contracts were not securities within the meaning of Ind. Code § 23-2-1-1(k), offering as proof the fact that after the contract in question was signed, the statute had been amended to add viatical settlement contracts to the statutory list of investment contracts to be registered as securities. The appellate court held that the statutory list was illustrative rather than exhaustive and that the amendment simply clarified that viatical settlement contracts had always counted as investment contracts. Applying the Howey test of Indiana case law, the court found that such contracts satisfied all the elements of investment contracts, even the expectation of profits to be derived from entrepreneurial or managerial efforts of others.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the partial summary judgment.

 

649 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


S.H. v. D.H.


No. 15A01-0309-CV-335


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


796 N.E.2d 1243; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1917



October 10, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE DEARBORN CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 15C01-9807-DR-179. The Honorable James Humphrey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; motion to reconsider order issued September 11, 2003, denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother appealed from an order of the Dearborn Circuit Court (Indiana) restraining the minor child from obtaining an abortion with the signatures of both the mother and appellee father. The parties were divorced and had joint legal custody over their daughter. The father moved the divorce court for an emergency hearing to enjoin the mother form signing a medical consent for the daughter to have an abortion.


OVERVIEW: The father learned that the minor was about 20 weeks pregnant and had scheduled an abortion. On appeal, the mother argued that the trial court erred in requiring both her signature and the signature of the father to give consent for the minor to receive an abortion. The appellate court concluded that only one parent's signature was required by statute. The appellate court noted that on its face, Ind. Code § 16-34-2-4(a) provided that the consent of only parent or legal guardian was required in any circumstance. Thus, the state was precluded from requiring the consent of two parents for the minor to receive an abortion simply because the parents happened to be divorced with joint legal custody where that burden would not be imposed on the minor child of an intact family.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

 

650 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Bennett v. State


No. 79A02-0303-CR-175


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


801 N.E.2d 170; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 2325



October 8, 2003, Decided  
October 8, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellee's Verified Motion for Publication of Memorandum Decision Granted December 8, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Bennett v. State, 797 N.E.2d 1186, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1938 (Ind. Ct. App., 2003).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of a trial court (Indiana), which convicted him of operating a vehicle with a controlled substance in the person's body resulting in death, a violation of Ind. Code § 9-30-5-5.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving on an Indiana highway when he disregarded a traffic signal and collided with a pickup truck. The pickup driver was ejected from his vehicle and died at the scene. Defendant's urine sample contained the metabolites for marijuana and cocaine. The court rejected defendant's argument that § 9-30-5-5 was unconstitutionally vague. The legislature clearly intended to broaden the scope of the respective statutes by sanctioning the use of urine screens to show metabolites in the "body." The term "body" was not synonymous for the term "blood." The court also rejected defendant's equal protection arguments. The legislature could have reasonably concluded that no level of Schedule I or Schedule II controlled substances could have been acceptably combined with driving a vehicle. Thus, it was rational for the legislature to impose the flat ban with regard to controlled substances while not imposing the same ban with regard to alcohol. The statute also had the effect of generally deterring illegal drug use, another legitimate government interest. The difference between alcohol and controlled substances warranted the classification under Ind. Const. art. I, § 23.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

651 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Chamberlain v. Walpole


No. 02A04-0302-CV-92


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


796 N.E.2d 818; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1876



October 6, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Chamberlain v. Walpole, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 2334 (Ind. Ct. App., Dec. 2, 2003)
Transfer granted by Chamberlain v. Walpole, 812 N.E.2d 800, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 299 (Ind., 2004)
Superseded by, Remanded by Chamberlain v. Walpole, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 143 (Ind., Feb. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] INTERLOCUTORY APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Daniel G. Heath, Judge. Cause No. 02D01-0201-CT-14.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: From the Allen Superior Court (Indiana), appellants, medial professionals and two hospitals, appealed from the denial of their motion for preliminary determination. Appellee son's father died while under the care of appellants. The son sued for damages based on alleged negligence.


OVERVIEW: The Indiana Wrongful Death Act (WDA), Ind. Code § 34-23-1-1 et seq., did not limit recovery under the Indiana Medical Malpractice Act (MMA), Ind. Code § 34-18-1-1 et seq., where a son sought to pursue claims for loss of services, loss of consortium, expenses, and other similar claims under Ind. Code § 34-18-2-22. The MMA was plain and unambiguous as to the damages recoverable thereunder. Therefore, the court could not construe the provisions of the MMA with the WDA. Even if the MMA were ambiguous, the two acts did not relate to the same general subject matter and were not in pari materia. Moreover, even if the MMA were ambiguous and in pari materia with the WDA, there was no need to harmonize the two acts because they did not conflict. Even if the MMA were ambiguous, in pari materia with the WDA, and in conflict with the WDA, the damages provisions of the MMA applied. The general assembly enacted the predecessor to the WDA in 1881 and the MMA in 1975; therefore, the MMA was controlling.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was affirmed.

 

652 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. State


No. 49A05-0211-CR-539


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


796 N.E.2d 798; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1872



October 3, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Davis v. State, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 33 (Ind., Jan. 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G16-0207-FD-202278. The Honorable Clark Rogers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, following a bench trial in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), of battery, as a class D felony, and domestic battery, as a class A misdemeanor. Defendant appealed, challenging the admission of evidence, the sufficiency of the evidence, whether trial counsel was ineffective, and whether the trial court relied upon an improper aggravating circumstance in sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been living with his girlfriend for six to eight months when he struck her. The girlfriend told the police that upon returning to her apartment, and while holding her child, defendant began striking her in the face, pushed her onto a bed, and then jumped on the bed on top of them both and started punching her, causing her to lose consciousness. The victims never testified at trial, and defendant challenged the use of his girlfriend's statements as hearsay. The appellate court found that the statements were excited utterances, under Ind. R. Evid. 803(2). Defendant argued that the statements were made too long after the battery. Although no length of time between the battery and the statements was established, the facts established that the victim was still under the stress of the excitement caused by the beating. As for sentencing, the trial court improperly considered that one of the victims was under the age of 12 because being under the age of 14 was an element of battery that elevated it to a class D felony. Although the age of the victim was not a valid aggravator, other proper aggravators existed, and there was no reversible error in the sentencing.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed.

 

653 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Reed v. State


No. 49A05-0301-PC-20


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


796 N.E.2d 771; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1864



September 30, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G01-9003-CF-39054. The Honorable Tanya Walton Pratt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: More than 10 years after conviction, defendant filed a petition for reduction of sentence under Ind. Code § 35-38-1-17(b), seeking a four-year reduction of sentence. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) denied his petition. Defendant filed his notice of appeal and continued to litigate in the trial court. The trial court denied a motion to reconsider. Defendant's second motion to correct error was denied. The instant appeal ensued.


OVERVIEW: While defendant's notice of appeal was premature, all matters raised in his subsequent motions to correct error, namely, his constitutional claims, were before the court on appeal because the notice of appeal replaced the praecipe under Ind. R. App. P. 2(I). Given the clear precedent on the constitutional attacks defendant raised, the appellate court rejected his contention that Ind. Code § 35-38-1-17(b) violated the separation of powers. The Indiana Supreme Court unambiguously held that, under Ind. Code § 35-38-1-17(b), a court lacked jurisdiction to modify a defendant's sentence if more than 365 days elapsed since that defendant began serving his sentence and the prosecutor did not approve the modification. Also, there was no evidence in the record to show that the prosecutor adopted a "blanket policy" of denying any request for a sentence modification under § 35-38-1-17(b). Without evidence in the record to support the factual allegation, any opinion examining the constitutionality of such a policy would have been purely advisory in nature. As the court did not render advisory opinions, the constitutional attack failed.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was affirmed.

O'Bannon v. Schindler


No. 40A01-0206-CV-200


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


796 N.E.2d 335; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1818



September 26, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by O'Bannon v. Schindler, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 2148 (Ind. Ct. App., Nov. 11, 2003)
Rehearing granted by Kernan v. Schindler, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 2513 (Ind. Ct. App., Dec. 30, 2003)
On rehearing at, Clarified by Kernan v. Schindler, 801 N.E.2d 189, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 2407 (Ind. Ct. App., Dec. 30, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE JENNINGS CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 40C01-0203-PL-0055. The Honorable William E. Vance, Special Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant various state officials sought review of the grant of a preliminary injunction by the Jennings Circuit Court (Indiana) based upon a request by appellee class which consisted of current and former patients of a state institution for developmentally challenged residents. The class members were characterized as "medically frail" and "at risk" individuals. The officials challenged the constitutionality of the injunction.


OVERVIEW: The United States Attorney General informed the officials that persons residing in or confined in the institution were being subjected to unacceptable conditions. The officials agreed to improve the conditions of the residents. The officials announced its intention to close the institution and transfer all patients to other types of facilities. Several parents and guardians of the patients examined the alternative facilities and determined they did not provide sufficient services. The trial court found that there was no evidence to show that any existing alternative facilities provided the same level of care and staffing as the institution. It further found that the injunction was necessary to maintain the status quo until such time as appropriate facilities were in existence. The appellate court held the evidence was sufficient to show the officials' transfer of patients deprived them of their rights of appropriate treatment. However, the trial court erred in forcing appropriation of funds to maintain staffing levels. The already transferred or discharged patients had to have the right to return. The injunction was vague as to prohibiting "pressuring in any way."


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in part and reversed in part. The trial court's provisions regarding staffing and "pressuring" of parents or guardians were clearly erroneous. On remand, they were to be stricken.

Monroe Guar. Ins. Co. v. Magwerks Corp.


No. 49A02-0208-CV-622


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


796 N.E.2d 326; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1783



September 24, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by Monroe Guar. Ins. v. Magwerks Corp., 812 N.E.2d 795, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 130 (Ind., 2004)
Affirmed in part and vacated in part by, Remanded by Monroe Guar. Ins. Co. v. Magwerks Corp., 2005 Ind. LEXIS 599 (Ind., June 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Gerald S. Zore, Judge. Cause No. 49D07-9902-CP-228.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee building owner sued appellant insurer, alleging breach of contract arising from the insurer's denial of the building owner's insurance claim. The building owner also alleged lack of good faith and fair dealing. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) granted summary judgment for the building owner, finding that the insurer breached the contract. A jury then returned a damages verdict for the building owner. The insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The building owner claimed that damage to the building roof and damage to property in the building were covered by its policy. The insurer argued that the loss was excluded because the loss was due to wear and tear to the roof, decay, deterioration, and defective design. The insurer also claimed that the damage was not a "collapse" since the framing of the roof remained intact and functioning. The appellate court found that the term "collapse" was not defined in the policy. The modern trend was to hold that collapse coverage provided coverage if there was substantial impairment of the structural integrity of the building or a part of a building. Here, however, an adjuster testified that the sag in the roof was not a collapse. There was evidence that the weight of rain and the design of the roof caused the damage. Photos showed that the roof did not fall in, cave in, or lose its shape in any fashion. Most of the roof remained intact. Thus, the trial court's summary judgment was not based on uncontradicted facts as to whether there was a "collapse" within the meaning of the policy. Since there was a genuine fact issue, punitive damages could not have been awarded.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

Frasier v. State


No. 07A01-0207-CR-239


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


794 N.E.2d 449; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1563



August 26, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Frasier v. State, 812 N.E.2d 792, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 63 (Ind., Jan. 14, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE BROWN CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 07C01-0011-DF-0465. The Honorable Judith A. Stewart, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; cause remanded..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought interlocutory review of a decision by the Brown Circuit Court (Indiana). The trial court denied his motion to suppress certain evidence obtained pursuant to a search warrant, which had authorized police officers to enter defendant's home and garage to search for marijuana and items relating to the sale of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: The officer who executed the search warrant found on the desktop of defendant's personal computer an icon labeled "Smoke." The officer opened the file and discovered it contained a letter relating to drug testing. The next file the officer opened had an image of a young, nude female. He opened two or three more files and sought and obtained a warrant to search for evidence of child pornography. Defendant was charged with drug-related offenses and possession of child pornography. The trial court denied his motion to suppress the evidence. The court affirmed. The court declined to determine whether the officer's affidavit was sufficient to establish probable cause; even if it was insufficient, the evidence that defendant sought to suppress was admissible under the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule. The good faith of the police in relying on the search warrant satisfied the first requirement of the plain view doctrine, namely, that the initial intrusion was authorized under the Fourth Amendment. The pornographic images discovered after the issuance of the first warrant but before the second warrant were admissible under the plain view doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the trial court's decision.

May v. State


No. 10A01-0211-CR-441


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


793 N.E.2d 1157; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1527



August 21, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by May v. State, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1975 (Ind. Ct. App., Oct. 16, 2003)
Transfer denied by May v. State, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 69 (Ind., Jan. 14, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CLARK SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 10D01-0205-FC-35. The Honorable Jerome Jacobi, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who had been charged with, among other things, battery and feticide, brought an interlocutory appeal of the denial of his motion for discharge by the Clark Superior Court (Indiana). Both the State and defendant had filed several motions during the contested period.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was initially charged on July 18th. At the initial hearing on July 20th the trial court set a jury trial date of October 23rd and set defendant's bond. Defendant was released on bond that day. After a series of motions, the case was re-docketed on May 6th of the following year. Another series of motions occurred including defendant's motion for discharge. The appellate court noted that when the trial court issued its order of dismissal on August 31st of the first year, the State had not moved to amend. Further, the State's subsequent motion to amend was withdrawn. Therefore, defendant was not entitled to discharge because he remained subject to the pre-trial order pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-34-1-4(d) until September of the following year. At the time the trial court ruled on defendant's motion for discharge based upon his right to a speedy trial, there remained 136 days for the State to try him within the 1-year period. Because none of the Barker factors weighed in defendant's favor, he was not deprived of his right to a speedy trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

658 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Lake Cent. Sch. Corp. v. Hawk Dev. Corp.


No. 45A03-0209-CV-310


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


793 N.E.2d 1080; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1521



August 20, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 45D04-9912-CP-629. The Honorable Gerald N. Svetanoff, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of summary judgment reversed; case remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school corporation sought an interlocutory appeal of a decision by the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment to appellees, a property buyer and two encumbrancers, on the issue of whether the corporation was required to file a lis pendens notice in its condemnation action against appellee developer. Multiple motions for summary judgment had been filed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation started condemnation proceedings against the developer after the developer refused to sell property to the corporation for a new school. The buyer purchased a portion of the subject property from the developer after the corporation had filed its condemnation complaint. Likewise, the encumbrancers took mortgages on the property after the filing of the condemnation complaint. The buyer and the encumbrancers were allowed to intervene in the condemnation action. They asserted that the order of appropriation and subsequent order of immediate possession did not affect their rights because the no lis pendens had been filed. The trial court agreed and granted summary judgment. The appellate court reversed. Although the general rule under the Lis Pendens Act, Ind. Code Ann. §§ 34-34-1-1 to -9 (Supp. 1998-1999) was that a lis pendens was to be filed to give notice to subsequent purchasers, the Eminent Domain Act, Ind. Code Ann. §§ 32-11-1-1 to -11 (1995), was an exception to the general rule. Nothing in the Eminent Domain Act required the filing of a lis pendens in a condemnation proceeding, nor was such a filing required under federal due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the buyer and the encumbrancers. The court remanded for entry of summary judgment in favor of the corporation on it motion for summary judgment.

Poulard v. Lauth


No. 46A03-0209-CV-297


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


793 N.E.2d 1120; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1523; 32 Media L. Rep. 1086



August 20, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAPORTE SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 46D02-0004-CP-80. The Honorable Steven King, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party sued defendants, the newspaper, a source, and others, for libel, slander, and defamation of character. The Laporte Superior Court (Indiana) granted summary judgment for all defendants but denied the source's petition for attorney's fees. The injured party and the source appealed.


OVERVIEW: The injured party argued that the newspaper was not entitled to an award of attorney's fees and costs under the anti strategic lawsuit against public participation (SLAPP) statute on the founds that the statute did not apply. The appellate court concluded that the injured party waived this objection by failing to raise it in response to the summary judgment motion. The source argued that the trial court improperly denied him attorney's fees because the fees and costs were paid by a non-party insurer. The appellate court concluded that the trial court's determination was an abuse of discretion. The appellate court held that the public policy underlying the anti-SLAPP statute dictated an award of attorney's fees to the source even when the source was not obliged to pay the fees. Finally, the source argued that the trial court improperly sanctioned him for a discovery violation without conducting a hearing and without giving him an opportunity to comply with the order compelling discovery. As the source failed to respond to the discovery requests for more than six months and Ind. R. Trial P. 37(D) did not mandate a hearing, the appellate court found no abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The award of attorney's fees to the newspaper and the sanctions imposed on the source for failure to comply with discovery were affirmed. The denial of attorney's fees to the source was reversed and the case was remanded for a determination of the amount to which the source was entitled.

Booth v. Wiley


No. 02A03-0210-CV-355


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


793 N.E.2d 1104; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1524



August 20, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Booth v. Wiley, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 2331 (Ind. Ct. App., Dec. 1, 2003)
Transfer granted by Booth v. Wiley, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 167 (Ind., Feb. 26, 2004)
Superseded by, Remanded by Booth v. Wiley, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 1158 (Ind., Dec. 30, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 02D01-0107-CT-260. The Honorable Nancy Eshcoff Boyer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a patient and his wife, filed a medical malpractice action against defendant doctors after the doctors performed Lasik surgery on the patient despite the fact that he had pre-existing cataracts and glaucoma. The doctors moved for summary judgment. The Allen Superior Court (Indiana) granted the doctors' motions. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient underwent Lasik surgery based on the recommendation of one of the doctors. After undergoing a variety of other procedures and seeing other doctors, the patient became aware that Lasik surgery should not have been performed on him because of his history of pre-existing cataracts and glaucoma. On appeal, plaintiffs argued that the trial court erred in determining that plaintiffs' complaint was filed outside the applicable statute of limitations. The appellate court held that the complaint was filed within the appropriate statute of limitations. The patient's diagnosis of a permanent vision loss, which occurred prior to the patient's becoming aware that Lasik surgery should not have been performed, did not give the patient a basis to reasonably suspect, based on more than mere suspicion or speculation, that malpractice had occurred. In addition, the appellate court noted that a plaintiff had to have a "meaningful opportunity" to pursue a malpractice claim; since only two months remained in the limitation period, it would have been a practical impossibility for plaintiffs to have asserted a timely claim.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

In re Visitation of C.H.


No. 49A02-0303-CV-211


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


792 N.E.2d 608; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1361



July 31, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by In re Visitation of C.H., 2003 Ind. LEXIS 994 (Ind., Nov. 18, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49D05-0210-MI-1770. The Honorable Gary Miller, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, grandparents, appealed a decision by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which denied their petition to establish grandparent visitation with a grandchild.


OVERVIEW: After the grandmother and the mother of the child were involved in an argument, the mother refused to let the grandparents see the grandchild for about two weeks. The mother then relented and allowed further contact with the grandchild. The grandparents petitioned for grandparent visitation, fearing that further disagreements with the mother would cause her to deny access to the grandchild again. Under Ind. Code §§ 31-17-5-1 and 31-17-5-2(a), a court had discretion to grant visitation to grandparents. The trial court in the instant action found that neither parent was unfit. Moreover, the grandparents had substantial access to the child after the argument with the mother was resolved. The mother expressed no hesitation at allowing the grandparents to see the grandchild. The trial court found that the grandparents sought to have a relationship on their terms, without regard to the wishes of grandchild's parents. The appellate court held that the trial court acted within its discretion in declining to order visitation between the grandparents and the grandchild under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

662 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Cushenberry v. State


No. 49A04-0210-PC-487


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


792 N.E.2d 571; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1370



July 30, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Cushenberry v. State, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 877 (Ind., Oct. 22, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G05-0108-CF-170418. The Honorable Grant Hawkins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to possession of a firearm by a serious violent felon, aggravated battery, and being a habitual offender. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) sentenced him to 10 years for each of the B felonies, and enhanced the sentence for aggravated battery by 10 years. The trial court suspended four years of the enhanced 20-year sentence. The trial court denied defendant's motion to correct sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the sentence for aggravated battery was enhanced twice, first by operation of the aggravated battery statute, Ind. Code § 35-42-2-1.5 (2002), and then by application of the general habitual offender statute, Ind. Code § 35-50-2-8 (2002). The appellate court ruled that, unlike the habitual traffic offender scheme and the handgun statute, Ind. Code § 35-47-2-3, the aggravated battery statute was a discrete and separate statute defining a single offense. Aggravated battery was, by definition, a Class B felony. Thus, defendant's conviction of aggravated battery as a Class B felony did not represent an elevation of a lesser classification of aggravated battery. There was no such offense. As a result, the imposition of a habitual offender enhancement did not represent a second enhancement of the aggravated battery offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

663 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


N. Ind. Pub. Serv. Co. v. LaPorte


No. 93A02-0205-EX-369 and No. 46A05-0203-CV-137


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


791 N.E.2d 271; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1249



July 15, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA UTILITY REGULATORY COMMISSION FROM THE LAPORTE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable William D. McCarty, Chairman. The Honorable Steven King, Judge. Cause No. 42194 and Cause No. 46D02-0203-PL-47.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, LaPorte County (Indiana) Board of Commissioners and the City of Michigan City (Indiana) filed an emergency petition with the Indiana Utility Regulatory Commission (IURC) and an action in the LaPorte County Superior Court (Indiana), seeking orders prohibiting respondent utility from acting on a plan to consolidate its operations. The IURC and the trial court ordered the utility not to proceed with its plan, and the utility appealed.


OVERVIEW: After a public utility announced plans to close several operating areas as a cost-savings measure, the LaPorte County Board of Commissioners and the City of Michigan City filed an emergency petition with the IURC asking it to prohibit the utility from implementing its plan and to conduct an investigation, and also sued the utility seeking an order enjoining it from implementing its plan. The IURC issued an order prohibiting the utility from acting on its plan and scheduled a hearing, and the trial court issued a temporary injunction prohibiting the utility for acting on its plan until the IURC issued its ruling. The utility appealed the IURC's ruling and the trial court's order, and both appeals were consolidated for review by the appellate court. The appellate court held that (1) the Board of Commissioners and the City had standing, pursuant to Ind. Code § 8-1-2-54, to challenge the utility's plan; (2) the IURC had authority, pursuant to Ind. Code § 8-1-2-113, to issue an order temporarily enjoining the utility from implementing its plan; and (3) the trial court had jurisdiction to issue a preliminary injunction in favor of the IURC's order.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the IURC's order prohibiting the utility from taking any action on its plan to consolidate operations until the IURC could review the plan, and also affirmed the trial court's order temporarily enjoining the utility from implementing its plan.

 

664 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Cornell v. Hamilton


No. 49A02-0208-CV-635


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


791 N.E.2d 214; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1206; 20 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 197



July 8, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49D04-0002-CP-180. The Honorable Cynthia Ayres, Judge.
Cornell v. Humphreys, 742 N.E.2d 1042, 2001 Ind. App. LEXIS 433 (Ind. Ct. App., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state employee appealed a decision of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment to defendants, the Secretary of the Indiana Family and Social Services Administration and the Indiana State Personnel Director, and denied the employee's motion for summary judgment in her action alleging that Indiana's state employee funeral leave policy violated the Privileges and Immunities Clause, Ind. Const. art. I, § 23.


OVERVIEW: The employee was a lesbian involved in a committed, five-year relationship with her domestic partner. When the domestic partner's father died, the employee requested three days of funeral leave pursuant to Ind. Admin. Code tit. 31, r. 1-9-7(B). The request was denied because the domestic partner was not the employee's spouse. The employee sued and after an initial reversal and remand, the trial court concluded that the policy did not violate the Privileges and Immunities Clause because it treated all unmarried persons the same. On appeal, the court held that Indiana's paid leave policy created a classification because it extended a privilege only to married employees. The employee, however, conceded that the policy was rationally related to marriage. Therefore, the court was not faced with the close question of whether the policy's marital status distinction was rational, but whether the privilege was equally available to all persons similarly situated. Although Ind. Code § 31-11-1-1 prevented the employee from attaining privileged class status by prohibiting her from marrying her partner, she was not "similarly situated" to other married employees in the privileged class.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

665 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Cole v. State


No. 58A04-0207-CR-311


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


790 N.E.2d 1049; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1201



July 2, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Cole v. State, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 761 (Ind., Sept. 19, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE OHIO CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 58C01-0106-CF-004. The Honorable James Humphrey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Ohio County Circuit Court (Indiana) of knowing failure to deposit public funds, in violation of Ind. Code § 5-13-14-3, and obstruction of justice. She appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, as treasurer of a county tourism bureau, controlled the check ledger and was responsible for depositing the bureau's funds. She failed to deposit $ 35,305 in cash receipts, and told an auditor she did not have or could not find documents the auditor requested. Police, after executing a search warrant, found some of these documents in her house. She argued that the penalty for the knowing failure to deposit public funds -- 10 years -- violated the proportionality clause of Ind. Const. art. I, § 16. The appellate court disagreed. Classifying a knowing failure to deposit public funds as a Class B felony did not violate the Indiana Constitution's proportionality requirement, as the penalty for this offense did not shock public sentiment or violate the judgment of a reasonable people. The trial court did not err in failing to instruct the jury that it had a constitutional right to disregard the law, as it had no such right under Ind. Const. art. 1, § 19. Defendant failed to object to the trial court's decision requiring the jury to continue deliberating or be sequestered, and even if she had preserved this point for appeal the trial court's decision was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

666 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Ross v. Ind. State Bd. of Nursing


No. 49A05-0206-CV-293


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


790 N.E.2d 110; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1041



June 13, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable S.K. Reid, Judge. Cause No. 49D13-0001-CP-000127.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In connection with a complaint alleging that appellant nurse was unfit to practice due to a mental disability, appellee Indiana State Board of Nursing ordered him to submit to and pay for a psychiatric evaluation. The nurse filed suit under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The Marion County Court (Indiana) granted him summary judgment, but denied his request for attorney's fees. The Board appealed; the nurse appealed the denial of attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: The State's complaint was based on errors the nurse made, his falsification of a report, and his alleged statement that his errors might have been due to his reducing or discontinuing the use of his medications. Under Ind. Code § 25-1-9-7, the Board could order him to submit to a mental exam if his mental capacity to practice safely was at issue in a disciplinary action. The appellate court held that, as the burden of proof rested with the State, and the Board could recoup the costs of the exam under Ind. Code § 25-1-9-15 after disciplinary sanctions were imposed, but the nurse could not do so if he prevailed, the Board did not have statutory authority to impose costs before any determination of misconduct. Further, as the nurse had the right not to be sanctioned before it was determined that sanctions were appropriate, and the order requiring him to pay the costs of the exam was basically a sanction, such a requirement violated his due process rights. The trial court erred in ruling that immunity precluded assessing attorney's fees against the Board, as Congress intended for attorney's fees to be available in a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action even if damages were barred by immunity.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment in favor of the nurse was affirmed. The trial court's order denying the nurse's request for attorney's fees was reversed and the cause was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

667 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Hannoy v. State


No. 49A05-0206-CR-282


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


789 N.E.2d 977; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 962



June 10, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On rehearing at, Reaffirmed Hannoy v. State, 793 N.E.2d 1109, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1519 (Ind. Ct. App., 2003)
Rehearing granted by Hannoy v. State, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1533 (Ind. Ct. App., Aug. 20, 2003)
Transfer denied by Hannoy v. State, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 868 (Ind., Oct. 22, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G01-0008-CF-139836. The Honorable Tanya Walton Pratt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him after trial to the court on two counts of operating a motor vehicle with a blood alcohol content of .10 percent or greater and causing death. He challenged the admissibility of blood alcohol evidence gathered in two different tests, one ordered by police and the other performed after hospital admission.


OVERVIEW: The first officers at the scene of a fatal accident ordered blood alcohol tests immediately, even before they had probable cause to suspect defendant was drunk. The sample was taken without his consent. The appellate court held that the statutory scheme of which the implied consent statute relating to fatal accidents was a part, at Ind. Code § 9-30-7-2, provided civil penalties for refusal to consent to testing, but it did not authorize police to take a blood sample without obtaining a driver's consent, and the taking of a sample did not fall within the special needs administrative exception to the Fourth Amendment. The results of that first test were relied on to the exclusion of the results of the second test, taken by the hospital for diagnostic purposes after defendant's admission, so their admission was not harmless error. As Indiana drivers had no reasonable expectation of privacy in their blood alcohol results, however, the results of defendant's second test, to which he consented in obtaining treatment, were subject to disclosure under Ind. Code § 9-30-6-6.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction and remanded the matter for retrial, holding, for the trial court's guidance, that results of the second blood test would be admissible at the second trial.

 

668 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Young v. Ind. Dep't of Natural Res.


No. 20A03-0205-CV-161


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


789 N.E.2d 550; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 925



June 9, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Young v. Ind. Dep't of Natural Res., 2003 Ind. LEXIS 856 (Ind., Oct. 22, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 20C01-9803-CP-070. The Honorable Terry C. Shewmaker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; matter remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sued defendants, the employer and several of its officers, in the Elkhart Circuit Court (Indiana) alleging the termination of his employment violated his state and federal constitutional rights. The jury found in favor of the employee, but only awarded damages as to his state law claims. The employee and defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The jury found the employer and officers violated the employee's state and federal constitutional rights, but only awarded damages against the employer as to the state constitutional claims. The appellate court held the employee waived any inconsistency in the jury's verdict when it did not find the employer's liability as to the federal claims, as he did not object before the jury's discharge, despite an opportunity, and alleged an inconsistent, not inadequate, verdict. While his complaint stated constitutional issues, he challenged his termination's constitutionality, rather than the termination procedure's constitutionality, raising fact issues which might have been resolved by the employer's administrative procedures, which he had to exhaust. Failing to do so deprived the trial court of jurisdiction over his state law claims. As he waived objections to the verdict, the trial court had no jurisdiction over his state law claims, no damages were awarded for the federal violations, and his motion for reinstatement was denied, his legal relationship with the employer and the officers was not changed, so he did not prevail for purposes of attorney fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of the employee's motion to correct errors as to the jury's verdict, and motion for attorney fees, was affirmed. The employee's state law claims were dismissed, and the jury's award thereon was vacated.

Ziebell v. State


No. 82A01-0206-CR-229


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


788 N.E.2d 902; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 878



May 27, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at, in part, Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Remanded by Ziebell v. State, 2011 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1413 (Ind. Ct. App., Oct. 19, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 82D02-0109-CF-652. The Honorable Scott R. Bowers, Judge.
Ziebell v. State, 770 N.E.2d 427, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1041 (Ind. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, the Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana) convicted defendant of murder, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-1-1 (1998); conspiracy to commit murder, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-41-5-2 (1998); confinement, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-3-3 (1998); and battery, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-2-1 (Supp. 2000), and sentenced defendant as a habitual offender to 123 years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder, conspiracy to commit murder, confinement, battery, and being a habitual offender after he offered to pay two other men to kill a third man (the victim) and was present when the victim was killed. During defendant's trial, the trial court admitted photographs of the crime scene and the victim over defendant's objection. The appellate court held that (1) photographs which depicted injuries to the victim, damage to his clothing, and the condition of the crime scene where his body was found were relevant to material issues in the case and to the testimony of a pathologist and the officer who found the victim's body; (2) testimony about defendant's prior involvement with drug dealing was relevant to show defendant's motive for wanting the victim killed; (3) the trial court did not err by requiring defendant to be present during the habitual offender phase of his trial or by allowing the State to call an attorney who represented defendant in a previous trial to identify him; and (4) Indiana's habitual offender statute, Ind. Code § 35-50-2-8 (1998), was constitutional, and the trial court did not err by imposing an enhanced sentence under that statute.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Beauchamp v. State


No. 41A05-0110-CR-467


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


788 N.E.2d 881; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 867



May 21, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE JOHNSON SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 41D01-9809-CF-129. The Honorable Kevin M. Barton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of battery resulting in serious bodily injury in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-2-1(a)(4). The Johnson Superior Court (Indiana) sentenced defendant to a 20-year term of imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the denial of his access to medical experts and the trial court's determination that several witnesses called by the State could testify. Defendant also urged that certain evidence was improperly admitted because the State had violated the trial court's discovery order and challenged the propriety of his sentence. In reversing defendant's conviction, the appellate court held that the trial court erred in allowing a doctor to testify as a rebuttal witness for the State because the opinions and the substance of the testimony, which differed dramatically from the doctor's deposition testimony, were known to the State before trial and had not been supplied to defendant. The appellate court also addressed defendant's other issues for purposes of remand and concluded, inter alia, that denying defendant's requests for court-appointed experts was in error since defendant satisfied the Scott requirements for such appointment, and that the trial court erred when it permitted an expert, who had previously consulted with defense counsel to evaluate the case, to testify for the State.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

McKibben Constr., Inc. v. Longshore


No. 34A02-0210-CV-867


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


788 N.E.2d 452; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 794



May 12, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by McKibben Constr. v. Longshore, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 857 (Ind., Oct. 22, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HOWARD CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 34C01-9905-CP-300. The Honorable Lynn Murray, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a construction contractor and realtor, appealed from an order of the Howard Superior Court (Indiana), which denied their motion for summary judgment dismissing an action by plaintiff homeowner seeking damages for misrepresentation, fraud, and breach of implied warranty of habitability.


OVERVIEW: The homeowner bought a four-bedroom house from the realtor associated with the contractor, in which, unknown to the homeowner, the contractor installed a septic system certified for a three-bedroom house. Years later, when problems occurred, he sued the contractor and realtor for fraud, misrepresentation, and breach of warranty. The appellate court held that the applicable septic system ordinance was not vague, overbroad, or lacking in rational basis. The homeowner had a private right of action, as he was suing for intentional wrongs, not for negligent noncompliance with the ordinance. The six-year statute of limitations was tolled until the homeowner actually discovered the system was nonconforming, and the fact that his fiancee had seen a copy of the original septic permit when she applied for a pool permit was not knowledge imputed to the homeowner. A purported disclaimer of warranty that did not comply with Ind. Code § 32-27-2-9 was ineffective. Finally, even though one of five proffered experts who submitted affidavits in opposition to summary judgment was not shown to be qualified, there was still plenty of evidence supporting a finding of triable issues.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of summary judgment and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Groves v. State


No. 20A03-0207-PC-231


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


787 N.E.2d 401; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 738



April 29, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Groves v. State, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 593 (Ind., July 15, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART SUPERIOR COURT NO. 1. Cause No. 5954B. The Honorable L. Benjamin Pfaff, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed an information, alleging that defendant committed murder. It then filed a second murder count, seeking the death penalty. Defendant moved to dismiss the death penalty count, which was granted. An interlocutory appeal was pending when defendant entered a guilty plea to one murder charge, and was sentenced. He petitioned for post-conviction relief, which was denied by the Elkhart Superior Court No. 1 (Indiana). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: At the post-conviction hearing, defendant sought to prove that he was induced to plead guilty by the dismissal of an illusory death penalty charge. In rejecting this argument, the appellate court found that the State was entitled to appeal the trial court's granting of defendant's motion to dismiss the death penalty count. In light of a strong dissent in the controlling case, and another state's refusal to follow the controlling case, the appellate court could not state that the State's appeal was frivolous. Therefore, defendant's guilty plea was not motivated by an improper or illusory threat. The prosecutor properly tested the applicability of a generally adverse precedent. The execution style and particularly callous nature of the killing, coupled with defendant's complete lack of remorse, his allegiance to a gang "code" over societal restraints, his juvenile record, and the likelihood that he would kill again, led the appellate court to the conclusion that the imposition of the maximum term of years was appropriate, and would have been imposed even in the absence of an impermissible aggravator. Even one valid aggravating circumstance was sufficient to support an enhancement.


OUTCOME: The denial of the petition for post-conviction relief was affirmed.

 

673 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Burns v. Hatchett


No. 82A05-0212-CV-576


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


786 N.E.2d 1178; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 681



April 24, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Burns v. Hatchett, 804 N.E.2d 748, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 709 (Ind., Aug. 28, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 82D03-0008-CP-2654. The Honorable J. Douglas Knight, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a patient and her spouse, sued appellee orthodontist in the Vandenburgh Superior Court (Indiana) for medical malpractice. The trial court granted the orthodontist's summary judgment motion dismissing appellants' claims, and they sought review.


OVERVIEW: The patient said the orthodontist's treatment injured her, but her complaint was not filed within two years of treatment, under Ind. Code § 34-18-7-1. The appellate court held § 34-18-7-1 was an occurrence-based, not discovery-based, limitations statute. It imposed no impossible condition on the patient's access to the courts or ability to pursue a valid claim, so it was not unconstitutional as to her, nor did it shorten her time to file a claim so unreasonably that it was impractical to file a claim. Her position that the law was unsettled as to when the limitations period began was unsupported, and she had 9 to 11 months after discovery of the malpractice to file. Disagreement between the Indiana Department of Insurance and the orthodontist's insurer as to his status as a "qualified health care provider" did not justify a delay in filing. The orthodontist's alleged fraudulent concealment did not save the claim as it was untimely if concealment was passive. Additionally, no triable issue as to active concealment was shown as a trier of fact could not reasonably infer the orthodontist actually knew of the injury, concealed it, or prevented the patient's inquiry or misled her.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Sisk v. State


No. 49A02-0205-CR-394


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


785 N.E.2d 271; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 410



March 18, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Certificate of appealability denied Sisk v. Superintendent, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 36528 (S.D. Ind., Mar. 22, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G20-0008-CF-133317. The Honorable David Shaheed, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Marion Superior Court, Indiana, which denied his motion to suppress evidence of his possession of crack cocaine.


OVERVIEW: During a search at a residence, defendant tossed something away that contained crack cocaine. A confidential informant advised an officer that he had purchased cocaine at a residence within the preceding 72 hours. The informant described the seller. The officer testified that he knew the seller's name, and the officer used that name in his affidavit to procure a search warrant. The seller testified that his permanent residence was not the particular residence that was searched. Thus, defendant challenged the warrant as unsupported by probable cause. The appellate court held that the place to be searched was described by address and by its physical appearance. The items to be seized were clearly specified. The officers were authorized to search the premises and curtilage of the particular address and to seize cocaine and related items. They conducted their search accordingly. Defendant was arrested not due to misapprehension that he was the seller. Thus, the trial court did not err in denying the motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

City of Hobart Common Council v. Behavioral Inst. of Ind., LLC


No. 45A03-0201-CV-33


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


785 N.E.2d 238; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 402



March 17, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Behavioral Inst. of Ind. v. Hobart Common Council, 406 F.3d 926, 2005 U.S. App. LEXIS 8065 (7th Cir. Ind., May 9, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT, CIVIL DIVISION, ROOM ONE. Cause No. 45D01-0105-MI-11. The Honorable Diane Kavadias Schneider, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee property owner sought a land use variance from appellant city to operate a residential treatment facility in an area zoned as single-family residential. The city's common council denied the request. The owner sought review from the Lake Superior Court, Civil Division (Indiana), which reversed and ordered approval of the variance. The city and appellants, a school city and public schools, sought review.


OVERVIEW: The board of zoning appeals (BZA) conducted a hearing on the owner's proposed variance, and recommended that the council approve it. The council conducted a hearing and denied the request. The trial court held there was substantial evidence to meet the requirements for a land use variance set forth in Ind. Code § 36-7-4-918.4, and that the council's hearing violated the owner's due process and equal protection rights. The appellate court held that the due process protections applied to BZA hearings by case law and Ind. Code § 36-7-4-920 also had to apply to land use variance proceedings pursuant to Ind. Code § 36-7-4-918.6 (which applied only to two, populous, Indiana counties), in order to avoid a violation of Equal Protection and the Privileges and Immunities Clause of Ind. Const. art. I, § 23. The owner's due process rights were violated by an engineer's ex parte contact with the council and the failure of a council member (who worked for appellant public schools and had been pressured by her principal to deny the variance) to recuse herself. However, by granting the variance, the trial court gave insufficient deference to the council; it should have remanded for a new hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

M-Plan, Inc. v. Ind. Comprehensive Health Ins. Ass'n


No. 49A02-0209-CV-759


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


784 N.E.2d 546; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 353



March 7, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by M-Plan, Inc. v. Ind. Comprehensive Health Ins. Ass'n, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 837 (Ind. Ct. App., May 13, 2003)
Transfer granted by M-Plan, Inc. v. Ind. Comprehensive Health Ins. Assoc., 804 N.E.2d 760, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 1063 (Ind., 2003)
Superseded by M-Plan, Inc. v. Ind. Comprehensive Health Ins. Ass'n, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 530 (Ind., June 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49D07-0207-PL-1136. The Honorable Gerald S. Zore, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant health maintenance organizations (HMOs) sought declaratory relief, challenging the assessment methodology used by appellees, the Indiana Comprehensive Health Insurance Association (ICHIA) and the Indiana Insurance Commissioner. Appellees filed a motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The HMOs appealed the decision of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which dismissed their complaint.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issues were whether the trial court properly dismissed the complaint for lack of subject matter jurisdiction due to a failure to exhaust administrative remedies, and whether the ICHIA was an administrative agency within the province of the Indiana Administrative Orders and Procedures Act, Ind. Code § 4-21.5-1-1 et seq. The appellate court concluded that the hallmarks of an administrative agency were absent. The ICHIA was a nonprofit legal entity to be referred to as the comprehensive health insurance association. This definition was inconsistent with that of an administrative agency--an entity that was responsible for any stage of a proceeding under the Act. The creation of the ICHIA was not accompanied by a regulatory scheme whereby the association was entrusted with enforcement of law. Rather, its purpose was to ensure health insurance availability for the otherwise uninsurable. Its essential function was cost allocation. The statutory scheme under which the ICHIA operated did not provide an exclusive administrative remedy. As such, the HMOs were not required to exhaust a statutory administrative remedy before filing their complaint for declaratory relief.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the dismissal of the complaint against the ICHIA.
