Szpunar v. State


No. 49A04-0202-CR-97


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


783 N.E.2d 1213; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 298



February 27, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Szpunar v. State, 2009 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1313 (Ind. Ct. App., July 16, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G03-0106-CF-126676. The Honorable William T. Robinette, Master Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) convicted defendant of sale of an unregistered security, and sale by an unregistered broker-dealer. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charges arose out of defendant's sale of a telephone services agreement. Defendant argued that the trial court erred when it found that his employment manual was inadmissible after a motion in limine. Defendant never tried to introduce the manual at trial and did not ask the trial court to revisit its ruling during trial. The appellate court ruled that in order to preserve error for appellate review, excluded evidence needed to be offered at trial. Defendant thus waived this issue. Defendant also argued that his right to confrontation was violated when a witness testified about an investigation performed by an investigator who was not called as a witness. However, since defendant elicited that testimony, it was invited error and he was not allowed to argue that it was reversible error. The jury was properly instructed. Ind. Code § 23-2-1-3 was not unconstitutionally vague. The fact that the Indiana Securities Commissioner filed a cease and desist order against defendant before criminal charges were filed against him did not render the State's decision to prosecute defendant for previous conduct a post hoc rationalization.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

678 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Higgins v. State


No. 82A04-0203-CR-109


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


783 N.E.2d 1180; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 263



February 21, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Higgins v. State, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 379 (Ind., May 1, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Carl A. Heldt, Judge. Cause No. 82C01-0009-CF-1094.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana) convicted defendant of residential entry. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in instructing the jury that the opening of a locked or unlocked door was sufficient to establish a breaking. The appellate court ruled that an instruction relating a mandatory presumption violated the Due Process Clause if it relieved the State of the burden of persuasion on a criminal element. The instruction here created a permissive inference, not a mandatory presumption. The giving of an impermissible mandatory instruction did not necessarily amount to reversible error where it was accompanied by an instruction informing the jury that it was the judge of the law and the facts. Instructions stating that certain evidence "is" sufficient to establish a criminal element should have been avoided, but, here, the jury was informed that it was the judge of the law and the facts, so there was no reversible error. Criminal trespass was a factually included lesser offense of residential entry here since the State alleged that defendant did knowingly break and enter his victim's dwelling, but all of the evidence pointed to a breaking, and so the trial court properly refused to give a jury instruction and verdict form on criminal trespass.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

679 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


McCune v. Frey


No. 40A05-0209-CV-449


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


783 N.E.2d 752; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 221



February 20, 2003, Decided  
February 20, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE JENNINGS CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 40C01-0109-MI-237. The Honorable Jon W. Webster, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, grandparents of a minor child, filed a petition for grandparent visitation in the Jennings Circuit Court (Indiana) requesting a set visitation schedule with their grandson. The trial court granted the petition. Respondent mother appealed, raising two issues. She argued that the trial court abused its discretion in awarding visitation, and the Indiana Grandparent Visitation Act, Ind. Code § 31-17-5-1 et seq., was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The mother gave birth to her son when she was 14 years old. Although the marriage dissolved, she and her son continued to have a good relationship with the grandparents, the father's parents. Visitation with the grandparents ceased after the child told his mother that he had been struck by the grandfather. After the grandparents filed a petition for visitation, the mother testified that her son consistently alleged that there was abuse at his grandparents' home. The special advocate's report recommended that visitation at the grandparents' home be continued, but that the grandfather should not be left alone with the child. After the trial court issued its order granting visitation, the appellate court found that the trial court failed to enter a decree setting forth its findings of fact and conclusions of law. The trial court also failed to find that visitation was in the minor child's best interests. As such, the appellate court was unable to determine whether the trial court gave any weight to the notion that a fit parent would have acted in her child's best interests. Finally, the appellate court found that the Indiana Grandparent Visitation Act was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

680 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Dora v. State


No. 07A01-0112-CR-482


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


783 N.E.2d 322; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 176



February 12, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Dora v. State, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 303 (Ind., Apr. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE BROWN CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 07C01-9912-CM-490. The Honorable Judith A. Stewart, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with resisting law enforcement, operating a vehicle while intoxicated, and failure to reduce speed for an emergency vehicle. The State filed a motion in limine to limit defendant's testimony concerning his knowledge of law enforcement misconduct. The court allowed defendant to testify, but limited the scope of his testimony. A jury in the Brown Circuit Court (Indiana) found defendant guilty as charged. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that he was prejudiced during jury selection because the trial court permitted the State to exercise a peremptory strike after it had passed on a juror. The court of appeals found no abuse of discretion in permitting the State to exercise its second peremptory strike since the facts and inferences showed that the request stemmed from an honest mistake, not from a mere change in choice. Defendant also challenged the trial court's resisting law enforcement jury instruction, alleging that it was contrary to law. The court of appeals found no error, noting that a lawful arrest was not a prerequisite to a conviction for resisting law enforcement. Finally, defendant challenged his conviction for driving while intoxicated, contending that there was scant objective evidence of intoxication and that the trial court unconstitutionally limited his ability to present his defense when it limited the scope of his testimony concerning his knowledge of police misconduct. The court of appeals concluded that the trial court properly balanced the probative value of the sought testimony with the potential prejudicial effect when it limited the scope of defendant's testimony.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

Stytle v. Angl. Die Casting Co.


No. 93A02-0210-EX-827


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


783 N.E.2d 316; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 174



February 12, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Stytle v. Angola Die Casting Co., 2004 Ind. App. LEXIS 681 (Ind. Ct. App., Apr. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE WORKER'S COMPENSATION BOARD OF INDIANA. The Honorable G. Terrence Coriden, Chairman. Case No. C-154593.



DISPOSITION: Worker's Compensation Board's decision was reversed and case was remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a workers' compensation proceeding by plaintiff former employee against defendants, the former employer and its successor, the employee appealed from an order of the Indiana Worker's Compensation Board that dismissed for lack of jurisdiction his application for adjustment of claim.


OVERVIEW: The employee's psychiatrist opined that the employee's years of work with aluminum caused his early onset Alzheimer's. The employee therefore commenced a workers' compensation proceeding against his employer and the employer's successor. They argued various points in defense, such as, that the employee never worked for the successor, that his claim was time-barred, and that their insurance carrier was not responsible for benefits awarded. The Indiana workers' compensation agency dismissed the claim for lack of jurisdiction, but did not append any factual findings. The appellate court held that unless the only question for it was a question of law, it could not review an order without the factual findings on which the order was based. There would be nothing to review. It therefore remanded the matter to the agency for the insertion of factual findings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision and remanded the matter for further proceedings, with instructions.

 

682 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Hevenor v. State


No. 34A02-0203-CR-240


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


784 N.E.2d 937; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 169



February 11, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HOWARD SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 34D01-0011-CM-301. The Honorable Dennis Parry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Howard Superior Court (Indiana) of dealing in paraphernalia, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-8.5(c). He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said Ind. Code § 35-48-4-8.5 improperly imposed a harsher penalty for reckless dealing in paraphernalia under Ind. Code § 35-48-4-8.5(c) than for knowing or intentional dealing in paraphernalia under Ind. Code § 35-48-4-8.5(a). The appellate court held Ind. Const. art. I, § 16 required penalties to be proportional to the nature of the offense and prohibited the penalty for a lesser-included offense from being greater than that for the greater offense. While a misdemeanor conviction under Ind. Code § 35-48-4-8.5(c) required proof of a reckless mental state, there was not a proportionality problem when the offense was compared to Ind. Code § 35-48-4-8.5(a), creating an infraction with a lesser penalty, because a mental state of "knowingly" or "intentionally" was not required as this was a strict-liability infraction not requiring proof of a mental state. The word "intended" in § 35-48-4-8.5(a) did not define a culpable mental state required to prove a violation but, rather, modified "raw material, an instrument, a device, or other object." Therefore, the penalties under § 35-48-4-8.5 were constitutional because they were proportional to the nature of the offense.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

683 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. State


No. 49A02-0201-CR-96


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


782 N.E.2d 1039; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 134



February 7, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Williams v. State, 792 N.E.2d 43, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 325 (Ind., 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Williams v. State, 2011 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1246 (Ind. Ct. App., Aug. 8, 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by, As moot Williams v. Superintendent, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 969 (N.D. Ind., Jan. 6, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G03-0003-CF-53499. The Honorable Cale Bradford, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) for murder, attempted robbery, and carrying a handgun without a license, after a jury trial. Defendant raised a number of evidentiary issues, including the admission of hearsay evidence.


OVERVIEW: The victim was providing taxi services when he was shot by defendant and another man as they attempted to rob him. Afterwards, at the hospital, the victim told an officer and his wife what had happened. A couple of months later, the victim's trach tube became blocked by mucous and he subsequently died. Defendant asserted an intervening cause, hospital negligence, killed the victim. The appellate court held the victim had been subjected to a startling event. Thus, the statements were excited utterances and admissible. Because defendant suggested the victim's death was due to an intervening cause, the cause of death was relevant and the statements by the medical examiner as to why some of the victim's organs were not able to be harvested due to gunshots were relevant. The jury instructions, when read together, required that intent to participate had to be proven. Any problems that occurred with the trach tube were the result of the hospitalization and treatment necessitated by the gunshot injuries. Thus, the use of the trach tube was not extraordinary and not an intervening cause. Defendant's sentence of 65 years was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Dorman v. Osmose, Inc.


No. 53A05-0206-CV-284


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


782 N.E.2d 463; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 122; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P16,494



January 31, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Dorman v. Osmose, Inc., 792 N.E.2d 46, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 906 (Ind., 2003)
Appeal after remand at Dorman v. Osmose, Inc., 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2184 (Ind. Ct. App., Sept. 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MONROE CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 53C01-0006-CT-953. The Honorable E. Michael Hoff, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed and case was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an independent contractor and his spouse, appealed from a judgment of the Monroe Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendant lumber companies in plaintiffs' product liability and negligence action.


OVERVIEW: The independent contractor cut himself against the edge of the wood, which had been treated with a heavy metal compound that included arsenic. The contractor suffered various incidents of cellulitis, some requiring hospitalization and medication, over a period of years. After speaking with an attorney and a doctor, the contractor determined that the treated wood caused the health problems. The contractor and his wife commenced an action, which was resolved by summary judgment in favor of defendants upon a finding that the claims were time-barred. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the action was timely filed under Ind. Code § 34-20-3-1 because it was filed within two years of being told of the proximate cause of the product to his injury. The court noted that the contractor's prior mere suspicion that the wood may have caused the health problems was not sufficient to start the running of the limitations period. His prior doctors never informed him that the wood caused the problem, only that there were chemicals in there, and his treatment with antibiotics would not have caused a reasonable person to further investigate if there was a viable cause of action at that time.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

685 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


C.T.S. v. State


No. 49A02-0206-JV-439


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


781 N.E.2d 1193; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 94



January 29, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by C.T.S. v. State, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 394 (Ind., May 8, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No.49D09-0111-JD-4964 & 49D09-0111-JD-4965. The Honorable James Payne, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in par and reversed in part; remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, was charged with battery and pointing a gun. Defendant entered a denial as to the charges. Defendant filed a notice of alibi defense and a request for visitation by an investigator and polygraph examiner. Access was granted for the investigator only. Defendant was found guilty. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) granted wardship to the department of corrections and recommended commitment for 12 months. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court lacked jurisdiction over him because a summons was not issued pursuant to Ind. Code § 31-37-12-2(b). The appellate court found no error since defendant and his parents fully submitted themselves to the authority of the court. Defendant also argued that the trial court improperly denied his request for access to a polygraph examiner. The appellate court found no error, noting that defendant failed to demonstrate how lack of access to such an examination prejudiced his defense. Defendant argued that the trial court abused its discretion when it detained him for over four months during the pendency of the proceedings. The appellate court agreed, after finding ample evidence demonstrating that defendant's parents were willing to go to great lengths so that defendant could be released to their care. Defendant also argued that the evidence was insufficient to support his finding of delinquency. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the testimony was sufficient to support the trial court's findings. Finally, the appellate court upheld the trial court's sentence since, inter alia, there was evidence of defendant's increasingly violent nature.


OUTCOME: The finding that defendant was delinquent was affirmed. The case was remanded for a clarification of the dispositional order to reflect that defendant would be given credit for his time served prior to the disposition hearing against his recommended period of commitment.

Vaughn v. State


No. 49A04-0204-CR-158


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


782 N.E.2d 417; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 91



January 28, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Vaughn v. State, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 345 (Ind., Apr. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G16-0201-DF-002465. CRIMINAL DIVISION 16 The Honorable Clark Rogers, Judge. The Honorable Julie Pitzer, Master Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of domestic battery, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-2-1.3 (2002). Following the entry of judgment, by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), defendant appealed, arguing that Ind. Code § 35-42-2-1.3 (2002) was unconstitutionally vague and that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of that portion of the domestic battery statute, Ind. Code § 35-42-2-1.3 (2002), that required him to live or to have lived "as if a spouse" of the victim. He argued that the statute was unconstitutionally vague because the statute did not define what that phrase meant, and no one could know with any reasonable degree of confidence whether they were or had lived with another "as if a spouse." The appellate court addressed the statute's constitutionality, even though defendant did not file a motion to dismiss prior to trial, under Ind. Code §§ 35-34-1-6, 35-34-1-4 (1998). In addressing the constitutionality issue, the appellate court found that the only evidence presented on the matter of living "as if a spouse" was that defendant and the victim had lived together in the past and had a sexual relationship. Only living in the same home and having a sexual relationship did not equate one to being a spouse. Therefore, the challenged portion of the domestic battery statute was unconstitutionally vague, as applied to defendant. On remand, the trial court was not precluded from entering a conviction and judgment on a charge of battery.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Byrd v. Afscme


No. 49A02-0202-CV-165


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


781 N.E.2d 713; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 16; 171 L.R.R.M. 3000



January 14, 2003, Decided  
January 14, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Byrd v. AFSCME, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 503 (Ind., June 13, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT, ROOM 11. Cause No. 49D11-9805-CP-675. The Honorable John F. Hanley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, reversed, in part, and the cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant non-member employees appealed from an order of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiff public employees' union in an action to recover fair share dues. The employees argued that Ind. Exec. Order No. 90-6 and the First Amendment precluded collection of such dues from them.


OVERVIEW: Although Ind. Exec. Order No. 90-6 contained general right-to-work language regarding the rights of state employees who decided not to join a union, Ind. Exec. Order No. 97-29 specifically incorporated a settlement between the state and the union that provided for fair share dues. The appellate court held that since the earlier executive order did not explicitly forbid fair share dues, they were permissible. The appellate court then looked to whether the union had satisfied its burden, under the First Amendment, to establish that the fair share amount accurately reflected those types of expenses that were properly chargeable to non-members. Even though the union had not presented documentary evidence in the form of its officials' and employees' time cards, the appellate court held that the union had carried its burden as to most expenses. It had not, however, established the chargeability of the proportion of administrative expenses that it imposed on non-members, nor of the proportion of contributions to the international union that it passed on.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in part, but remanded the matter for further proceedings regarding the proportion of administrative expenses and funds passed on to the union international that were properly chargeable to non-members.

 

688 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Gyn-Ob Consultants v. Schopp


No. 02A03-0203-CV-73


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


780 N.E.2d 1206; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 8



January 13, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Gyn-Ob Consultants, L.L.C. v. Schopp, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 369 (Ind., May 1, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 02C01-0011-CT-127. The Honorable David J. Avery, Special Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a patient and her husband, sued defendant doctor alleging sexually battery and genital mutilation. The doctor moved for summary judgment, asserting that the claim was barred by the statute of limitations. The doctor's motion was denied, but the Allen Circuit Court (Indiana) granted summary judgment for the doctor on the issue of negligence. The doctor appealed. The patient cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The doctor performed a hysterectomy on the patient. During surgery, the doctor also removed skin tags from her vaginal area, without her consent. The surgery occurred near the patient's clitoris. The doctor denied operating near her clitoris. The patient did not find out until two years later that the doctor had operated near her clitoris. On appeal, the doctor argued that the trial court erred when it determined that there was an issue of fact regarding whether the doctor had fraudulently concealed the fact that he had performed surgery near the patient's clitoris. In her complaint, the patient had alleged both active and constructive concealment because the doctor denied cutting anywhere near her clitoris, the location of the discomfort. The court of appeals concluded that despite the evidence of concealment, the patient did not timely bring the action because she experienced, almost immediately after the surgery, symptoms that should have led to the discovery of the removal of the skin tags. The doctor's denial that he operated near the patient's clitoris did not change the fact that the patient experienced discernible symptoms. Thus, the statute of limitations was not tolled.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of the doctor's motion for summary judgment was reversed. The trial court's grant of the doctor's motion with respect to the patient's negligence claim was affirmed.

 

689 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Poyser v. Flora


No. 43A03-0207-CV-232


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


780 N.E.2d 1191; 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 6



January 10, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE KOSCIUSKO CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 43C01-0107-CP-464. The Honorable Rex A. Reed, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an insurance agent, appealed the judgment of the Kosciusko Circuit Court (Indiana) that granted the motion of plaintiffs, two investors who were husband and wife, for summary judgment in an action for rescission of a contract. The investors filed suit to recover the money paid to an investment group, contending that the sale of viatical settlement contracts (VSC) violated the Indiana Securities Act, Ind. Code §§ 23-2-1-1 to -24.


OVERVIEW: The investors contended that the agent violated Ind. Code § 23-2-1-19 by selling securities without following the requirements of the Act, specifically that the VSCs were not registered as securities, and the agent was not a registered seller of securities. The appellate court found that a VSC was, at the time, considered to be a security under Ind. Code § 23-2-1-1(k), but was not included in the earlier statutory definition of "security" at the time of the sale to the investors. The appellate court found, however, that there was no dispute that the agent's viatical settlement sales involved the investment of money in a common enterprise, or that the investors invested their money with the reasonable expectation of profits. It was the activities by the capital group and the agent that affected the success or failure of the enterprise, even if those activities may have been pre-purchase. Further, the agent did not contend that he was unaware of the facts surrounding the transaction, merely that he was unaware that the law attached any regulations to the facts as they existed. The appellate court found that this did not constitute an affirmative defense under Ind. Code § 23-2-1-19.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Parks v. Madison County


No. 77A04-0106-CV-257


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


783 N.E.2d 711; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 2197



December 31, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Counsel Corrected January 7, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Parks v. Madison County, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 518 (Ind. Ct. App., Mar. 10, 2003)
Related proceeding at Parks v. State, 789 N.E.2d 40, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 895 (Ind. Ct. App., 2003)
Transfer denied by Parks v. Madison County, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 562 (Ind., June 25, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SULLIVAN SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 77D01-0012-CP-374. The Honorable R. Paulette Stagg, Judge.
Parks v. State, 657 N.E.2d 207, 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 1857 (Ind. Ct. App., 1995)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner sued defendants, a judge, a deputy prosecuting attorney, a county sheriff, a probation officer, and an attorney, alleging civil rights violations under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 based upon, inter alia, the issuance of an arrest warrant. The Sullivan Superior Court (Indiana) granted defendants' motions to dismiss and denied the prisoner's motion to correct error. The prisoner appealed from the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was arrested for violating his probation and his probation was revoked. The court affirmed the revocation of probation. A federal court dismissed the prisoner's civil rights claims for failure to comply with the federal pleading rules. A second federal case was dismissed for untimeliness. In the instant case, the appellate court determined that the relevant statute of limitations barred the prisoner's civil rights action and the "continuing wrong" and "fraudulent concealment" doctrines did not make the action timely. Also, Indiana's Journeys Account Statute did not save the late-filed state complaint, because the federal claims failed due to the prisoner's negligence. In addition, the appellate court determined that Ind. Code Ann. § 35-50-6-5(a)(4) (West 2002), which deprived the prisoner of credit time due to the frivolous lawsuit, was not vague or overbroad, and it did not violate due process or equal protection principles. Also, the trial court did not err in finding that the prisoner's claims were frivolous. Finally, the trial court did not err in declining to appoint counsel to represent the prisoner on the frivolous claims.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

692 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Worman Enters. v. Boone County Solid Waste Mgmt. Dist.


No. 06A01-0206-CV-202


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


779 N.E.2d 565; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 2043



December 5, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reaffirmed, Clarified by, On rehearing at Worman Enters. v. Boone County Solid Waste Mgmt. Dist., 783 N.E.2d 353, 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 211 (Ind. Ct. App., 2003)
Affirmed by Worman Enters. v. Boone County Solid Waste Mgmt. Dist., 2004 Ind. LEXIS 227 (Ind., Mar. 9, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE BOONE SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 06D01-0011-CP-390. The Honorable Ora A. Kincaid, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant recycling facility sued appellee waste management district, seeking a declaratory judgment that certain terms contained in a permit were unlawfully imposed by the district and that the district did not have the authority to issue the permit. The Boone Superior Court (Indiana) entered summary judgment in favor of the district. The recycling facility appealed.


OVERVIEW: The recycling facility argued that under the Home Rule Act, Ind. Code ch. 36-1-3, the district's power to regulate its facility was preempted by state law. The appellate court found that the district had the power to prescribe requirements for the permitting and operation of solid waste facilities. Also, the general assembly did not place any limits on a district's power that would have prevented it from creating a permit system. The permit system did not violate Ind. Code § 13-21-3-14 and the district's authority to establish a permit system was not preempted. The district had the authority to institute a permit system and to regulate solid waste facilities. It was a denial of due process if an agency received ex parte evidence. There was evidence of ex parte communication from the public. There was no evidence that the recycling facility was made aware of the ex parte communications. The district also needed to show that its decision was not based on the ex parte evidence, and summary judgment was improper where resolution hinged on state of mind, credibility of witnesses, and weight of the testimony. Therefore, summary judgment was improper.


OUTCOME: The judgment that the district had the authority to issue permits for the operation of solid waste facilities was affirmed. The judgment was otherwise reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings to determine whether the receipt of ex parte communications during the application process resulted in prejudicial error and to consider the recycling facility's challenges to the permit provisions.

 

693 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


No. 49A02-0110-CR-657


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


779 N.E.2d 111; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1964



November 27, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Transfer February 20, 2003, Reported at: 2003 Ind. LEXIS 140.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G01-9911-CF-204100. The Honorable Tonya Walton Pratt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed; remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), defendant was convicted of child molesting, as a Class A felony. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of molesting a six-year-old girl. Defendant argued that the child's testimony, without more, was insufficient to support the conviction. Defendant argued that the "incredible dubiosity rule" should have been invoked to reverse the conviction. The appellate court ruled that the "incredible dubiosity rule" allowed a reversal when a sole witness gave contradictory testimony that was equivocal, or the result of coercion, and there was a lack of circumstantial evidence of guilt. A conviction was allowed to stand on a minor's uncorroborated testimony. A conviction for child molesting was to be sustained when it was apparent that the child victim described an act of sexual penetration. A child's inconsistent statements did not make her testimony inherently improbable or incredibly dubious. The incredible dubiosity rule did not apply, and there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction. Probation restrictions on defendant's contact with children, his use of a computer, and the requirement that he report any dating or sexual relationships were proper. The restriction on possession of pornography, however, was unreasonably vague.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed but the case was remanded with instructions to set out any prohibition against "pornographic or sexually explicit materials" with more specificity.

 

694 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Avant v. State


No. 49A02-0111-CR-783


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


779 N.E.2d 538; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1928



November 20, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Z. Mae Jimison, Judge. Cause No. 49F10-0110-CM-203059.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an interlocutory appeal from an order of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which denied his motion to dismiss a criminal information against him alleging reckless possession of paraphernalia under Ind. Code Ann. § 35-48-4-8.3 (West 1998), based on his challenge to its constitutionality due to his claim of disproportionality of the penalties.


OVERVIEW: A police officer saw defendant fighting with another individual. Defendant appeared intoxicated and a search incident to the arrest revealed a crack pipe which tested positive for cocaine residue. Defendant sought dismissal of the information against him, alleging that § 35-48-4-8.3 was unconstitutional. The trial court denied his motion and on appeal, the court affirmed that denial, holding that although the term "recklessly" as used in § 35-48-4-8.3(c) was ambiguous, it was interpreted within constitutional limits. The court differentiated the offenses described in § 35-48-4-8.3(a), (c), in their character of the possession and in the nature of the object possessed. In § 35-48-4-8.3(a), the person's intent was the critical element of the offense, whereas in § 35-48-4-8.3(c), the focus was on the nature of the object itself. Likening the interpretation of "recklessly" to that given to the term in Ind. Code Ann. § 35-41-2-2, the court held that "recklessly" possessing an object was more culpable than possessing it "intentionally." The court concluded that § 35-48-3-8.3(a) was a lesser-included offense of § 35-48-3-8.3(c) and that there was no violation of Ind. Const. art. 1, § 16.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

695 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Hensley v. State


No. 40A01-0204-CR-120


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


778 N.E.2d 484; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1901



November 15, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE JENNINGS CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Jon W. Webster, Judge. Cause No. 40C01-0108-DF-135.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with possession of a schedule II controlled substance. Defendant filed a motion to suppress evidence. The Jennings Circuit Court (Indiana) denied the motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court should have granted her motion to suppress because the affidavit did not connect the drugs purchased to the premises to be searched; thus, there was insufficient information to establish probable cause to search defendant's house. In reversing the trial court's judgment, the court of appeals found that the affidavit did not sufficiently set forth facts then in the affiant's knowledge to constitute probable cause to search the house. The affidavit did not link defendant's alleged purchase with the premises, and there was no evidence that she had any connection with the described premises. Thus, there was no basis for a reasonably prudent person to believe that a search of the premises would uncover evidence of a crime. The State argued that defendant's motion was properly denied because the evidence was admissible under the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule. The court of appeals concluded that no reasonable officer could have relied on the search warrant affidavit in good faith. The affidavit on which the search warrant was based was so facially lacking in indicia of probable cause that the good faith exception did not apply.


OUTCOME: The denial of defendant's motion to suppress was reversed.

Borgman v. Sugar Creek Animal Hosp.


No. 93A02-0201-EX-16


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


782 N.E.2d 993; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 2208



November 6, 2002, Decided  
November 6, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Transfer Denied January 14, 2003, Reported at: 2003 Ind. LEXIS 48. Ordered published: Borgman v. Sugar Creek Animal Hosp., 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 2196 (Ind. Ct. App. Dec. 19, 2002).
Transfer denied by Borgman v. Sugar Creek Animal Hosp., 2003 Ind. LEXIS 370 (Ind., May 1, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA WORKER'S COMPENSATION BOARD. The Honorable G. Terrence Coriden, Chairman. Application Number: C140512.
Borgman v. Sugar Creek Animal Hosp., 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1908 (Ind. Ct. App., Nov. 6, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant was injured while working for defendant employer. She left employment because of personal difficulties with a co-worker. Following various workers' compensation and civil proceedings, a hearing was held before a hearing member. Limited disability benefits were awarded and no bad faith was found. The claimant appealed, and the decision was affirmed by judgment of the Indiana Workers' Compensation Board. The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant asserted that she was entitled to temporary partial disability benefits (TPD) because her employer did not offer her any work in accordance with her ability to perform sedentary work. The appellate court found that the issue had not been preserved. Also, because the claimant voluntarily terminated her employment due to reasons unrelated to her work injury, the employer did not have a duty to offer her work according to medical restrictions or to remit any TPD benefits to her. Thus, the Board properly determined that the claimant was unavailable for work for reasons that were not related to her work injury. The medical report of the insurer's doctor was properly admitted into evidence, even though the doctor did not physically examine the claimant. The report met the requirements of Ind. Code § 22-3-2-6(e). There was no need for the insurer's doctor to comment on any impairment, for he determined that the claimant's injuries were not related to her work. There was absolutely no evidence that the insurer acted in bad faith when denying certain benefits. There was substantial competent evidence of probative value to support the Board's decision.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Baugh v. State


No. 29A02-0202-CR-167


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


781 N.E.2d 1141; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 2194



October 28, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Ordered published: Baugh v. State, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 2195 (Ind. Ct. App. Dec. 19, 2002).
Reversed by Baugh v. State, 801 N.E.2d 629, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 40 (Ind., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE HAMILTON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable J. Richard Campbell, Judge. Cause No. 29D04-0102-DF-858.
Baugh v. State, 778 N.E.2d 498, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1840 (Ind. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for operating a vehicle while intoxicated, a class D felony, challenging the constitutionality of Ind. Code § 35-32-2-1(i) as applied to him, arguing that the Hamilton Superior Court (Indiana) deprived him of his constitutional right to be tried in the county where the offense occurred.


OVERVIEW: At the close of the State's evidence, defendant moved for judgment on the evidence, alleging that the State failed to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that venue properly lay in Hamilton County and that a trial in Hamilton County violated his constitutional right to be tried in the county where the offense occurred, as provided in Ind. Const. art. 1, § 13(a). Defendant argued that the State was required to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that venue resided in Hamilton County. The appeals court held that the uncontroverted evidence showed that defendant's offenses occurred wholly in Marion County because the two eastbound lanes of 96th Street were fully in Marion County, and defendant never left the eastbound lanes and never even fully crossed into the northern eastbound lane. Thus, the State failed to prove that venue properly resided in Hamilton County, and the trial court erred by failing to grant defendant's motion for judgment on the evidence at the end of the State's case-in-chief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

698 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Little Bev. Co. v. DePrez


No. 49A02-0203-CV-232


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


777 N.E.2d 74; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1758



October 25, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer denied by Little Bev. Co. v. Deprez, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 284 (Ind., Mar. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable S. K. Reid, Judge. Cause No. 49D13-0111-CP-1902.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff beer distributors appealed from a Marion Superior Court (Indiana) summary judgment in favor of defendants, the Indiana Alcohol and Tobacco Commission (ATC) and a brewing company, declaring that a rule of the Commission had expired under the Indiana Sunset Law, Ind. Code § 4-22-2.5-2 (2002), and that if the distributors shipped outside their contractual territories, they would be in breach of contract.


OVERVIEW: Former Ind. Admin. Code tit. 905, r. 1-28-1(3) (1979) (Rule 28) prohibited beer distributors in Indiana from having exclusive territories. Therefore, even though distributors' contracts with brewers assigned particular territories, they engaged in a practice called transshipping, under which they also distributed beer in other wholesalers' territories. When Rule 28 expired under the Sunset Law, after the ATC declined to readopt it, a brewer notified certain distributors that they would have to stick to their own territories in future. The appellate court held that Rule 28 had indeed expired by operation of law. Therefore, no administrative action was required to repeal it, and the expiration did not amount to revocation of the distributors' permits without proper procedures. Further, in the interests of judicial economy, the trial court had not erred in declaring that the distributors would be in breach of contract if they were to continue transshipping.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Sons v. Lake County Office of Family & Children (In re R.S.)


No. 45A03-0202-JV-46


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


774 N.E.2d 927; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1490



September 10, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Transfer Denied January 2, 2003, Reported at: 2003 Ind. LEXIS 29.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. Cause Nos. 45D06-0012-JT-191, 45D06-0012-JT-189, 45D06-0012-JT-192, &. The Honorable Mary Beth Bonaventura, Judge 45D06-0012-JT-190.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: From the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), appellant mother challenged an order terminating her parental rights upon the petition of appellee Lake County Office of Family and Children (OFC).


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the mother failed to properly challenge the constitutionality of Ind. Code § 31-35-2-4. The mother did not challenge the right of the OFC to offer evidence of the children's best interests on constitutional grounds at the trial court, and waived appellate review of her constitutional claim. The OFC established by clear and convincing evidence the requisite elements to support the termination of the mother's parental rights. The evidence most favorable to the judgment disclosed that the mother was historically unable to provide adequate housing and supervision for her children. One of the children, aged 10, had contracted gonorrhea after sexual involvement with another child. The mother had sporadically resided with a relative, with the father, in shelters, motels, a vehicle, and jail and was chronically unemployed. The conditions leading to the children's removal were probably not going to change, and termination was in the children's best interests. Under Ind. R. Trial P. 59(J)(7), the trial court's order on its sua sponte motion to correct error was proper.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was affirmed.

Sharp v. Fields (In re Baby W)


No. 11A05-0203-JV-00110


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


774 N.E.2d 570; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1484



September 6, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected September 6, 2002. Petition to Transfer Denied January 2, 2003, Reported at: 2003 Ind. LEXIS 46.
Transfer denied by Sharp v. Fields (In re Baby W.), 792 N.E.2d 33, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 46 (Ind., 2003)
Subsequent appeal at Sharp v. Fields (In re Sharp), 2003 Ind. App. LEXIS 1814 (Ind. Ct. App., Sept. 26, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CLAY C75CUIT COURT. Cause No. 11C01-0112-JP-270. The Honorable Ernest E. Yelton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner putative father appealed from a judgment of the Clay Circuit Court (Indiana) granting a motion by respondent prospective adoptive parents to dismiss his paternity action for lack of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The attorney for the prospective adoptive parents wrote a letter to the putative father. Although it was not strictly compliant with the Indiana pre-birth notice statute, Ind. Code § 31-19-3-4, the letter told the father of the mother's hope that the parents would adopt the expected child, enclosed a copy of Ind. Code § 31-19-9-15, which explained what the father needed to do to avoid an implication of consent to adoption, and warned him to rely only on the statute. The appellate court held that the letter substantially complied with the notice statute, because it told the father exactly what he needed to do and what the consequences of inaction would be. Instead of filing a paternity action within 30 days, as the statute directed, the father commenced DNA testing, without indicating any desire to be involved with the child. The appellate court held that the implied consent statute was a nonclaim statute, not subject to equitable defenses, and noted that it had already been held not to violate due process. Therefore, since the father had not acted to timely preserve his paternity claim, Indiana's courts were without jurisdiction to hear it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Kirby v. State


No. 55A01-0109-CR-335


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


774 N.E.2d 523; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1437



August 29, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Transfer Denied January 2, 2003, Reported at: 2003 Ind. LEXIS 37. Petition for Rehearing Denied October 30, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 2266.
Rehearing denied by Kirby v. State, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 2266 (Ind. Ct. App., Oct. 30, 2002)
Transfer denied by Kirby v. State, 792 N.E.2d 33, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 37 (Ind., 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Kirby v. State, 2015 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1382 (Ind. Ct. App., Dec. 10, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MORGAN SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 55D03-0004-CF-105. The Honorable Jane Spencer Craney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appellant-defendant's convictions and sentence were affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of seven counts of murder as felonies, four counts of neglect of a dependent resulting in serious bodily injury as Class B felonies, and one count of aggravated battery as a Class B felony. At sentencing the four convictions of neglect of a dependent were merged into the murder convictions of the children, and she was sentenced to 215 years by the Morgan Superior Court (Indiana). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State's theory was that defendant was attempting to commit suicide when she drove her vehicle down the wrong side of a highway at over 90 miles per hour. Defendant argued that the State's action of amending its witness list to include 22 new witness three weeks prior to the scheduled trial forced her to request a continuance. In rejecting defendant's speedy trial claim, the appellate court found that the State did not delay in providing its amended witness list. Rather, it timely disclosed the amended list in accordance with the trial court's deadline. The appellate court would not say that the trial court abused its discretion by finding that defendant could have been prepared for trial without the continuance and by attributing the delay resulting from the continuance to defendant. Evidence of defendant's prior drug dealing was highly relevant to the issue of defendant's state of mind. The State theorized that this provided motivation to commit suicide, as she was afraid she was under investigation and would be arrested. No circumstantial evidence instruction was necessary because there was direct as well as circumstantial evidence linking defendant to the crimes.


OUTCOME: The convictions and the 215-year sentence were affirmed.

Estate of Foleno v. Estate of Foleno


No. 76A05-0111-CV-496


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


772 N.E.2d 490; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1204



July 30, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Transfer Denied November 13, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Ind. LEXIS 875.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE STEUBEN CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Allen N. Wheat, Judge. Cause No. 76C01-0007-ES-0059.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff executor of the estate of the decedent insured's wife appealed from a summary judgment of the Steuben Circuit Court (Indiana), declaring that defendant contingent beneficiaries under the decedent's life insurance policy were entitled to the proceeds that defendant insurer placed in escrow.


OVERVIEW: The decedent's wife was the primary beneficiary under the insured's life insurance policy, and his brothers were the contingent beneficiaries. The decedent killed his wife and then killed himself. The appellate court upheld the right of the contingent beneficiaries under the policy against a challenge by the wife's estate, holding that no constructive trust could be imposed under Ind. Code § 29-1-2-12.1, because the insured could never be convicted of his wife's murder, and, further, no constructive trust arose under equitable principles either, because the policy always belonged to the insured, and he acquired no new right by killing his wife. Thus, the slayer's rule of case law had no application. As the contingent beneficiaries had not committed any wrongful act in connection with the death, their right was clear.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment.

Crowe, Chizek & Co., L.L.P. v. Oil Tech., Inc.


No. 45A05-0110-CV-458


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


771 N.E.2d 1203; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1165



July 23, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Transfer Denied February 20, 2003, Reported at: 2003 Ind. LEXIS 160. Application for Rehearing Denied October 23, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 2268.
Rehearing denied by Crowe, Chizek, & Co. v. Oil Tech., 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 2268 (Ind. Ct. App., Oct. 23, 2002)
Transfer denied by Oil Tech., Inc. v. Crowe, Chizek, & Co., LLP, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 160 (Ind., Feb. 20, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable George S. Ivancevich, Magistrate. Cause No. 45C01-9709-CT-02244.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; matter remanded to the trial court with instructions to Crowe's motion for summary judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation filed an action against defendant accounting firm, alleging negligence. The accounting firm filed a motion for summary judgment, arguing that the action was barred by the statute of limitations set forth in Indiana's Accountancy Act, codified at Ind. Code § 25-2.1-15-2. The Lake Circuit Court (Indiana) denied the accounting firm's motion, and the accounting firm appealed.


OVERVIEW: A corporation hired an accounting firm to prepare its tax returns. The firm prepared the corporation's state personal property tax returns from 1987 through 1992, and although it did not complete state personal property tax returns after 1992, it provided other services, including the preparation of federal and state income tax returns, until May 1995. While preparing the corporation's state personal property tax returns, the accounting firm failed to note that the corporation was entitled to take a tax exemption on an industrial waste control facility it operated, and, as the exemption was not claimed, the corporation paid approximately $ 168,000 in personal property taxes it could have avoided. In 1997, the corporation sued the accounting firm, alleging negligence. The appellate court held that: (1) the statute of limitations set forth in Indiana's Accountancy Act, codified at Ind. Code § 25-2.1-15-2, was not unconstitutional; (2) the facts did not establish constructive fraud, a continuing wrong, or fraudulent concealment, and the corporation could not use those doctrines to toll the statute of limitations; and (3) the corporation's action was untimely under § 25-2.1-15-2.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with instructions that final judgment be entered for the accounting firm.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with driving while intoxicated, and filed a motion to suppress his chemical test results. The Porter Superior Court (Indiana) denied defendant's motion to suppress. The trial court certified issues for interlocutory appeal. Defendant appealed.

Mishler v. MAC Sys.


No. 27A02-0111-CV-778


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


771 N.E.2d 92; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1127



July 16, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Counsel Corrected July 24, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE GRANT SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Randall Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 27D02-0111-CP-222.



DISPOSITION:  [**2] Trial court's judgment was reversed and case was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sued defendant contractor, alleging breach of a contract. The contractor filed a counterclaim alleging defamation and petitioned the court to enjoin the property owners from making verbal or written statements regarding the contractor's character, qualifications, or reputation. The Grant Superior Court (Indiana) granted the contractor's petition in part and issued an injunction. The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owners hired a contractor to perform fire restoration and construction services on a building they owned. After a dispute arose between the property owners and the contractor and a stop-work order was issued by a county building department, the property owners posted a sign on their building which expressed their concerns about the quality of the contractor's work. When the property owners sued the contractor for breach of contract, the contractor filed a counterclaim alleging defamation and asked the trial court to enjoin the property owners from making verbal or written statements that criticized the contractor's character, qualifications, or reputation. The trial court granted the contractor's petition in part and ordered the property owners to remove their sign and not to replace it. The appellate court held that (1) Ind. Const. art. I, § 9 was intended to prohibit Indiana courts, as well as the Indiana General Assembly, from abridging the free speech rights of Indiana citizens; and (2) the trial court's order was an impermissible prior restraint on speech that violated the property owners' rights under Ind. Const. art. I, § 9.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's order and remanded the case with instructions that the trial court dissolve the injunction.

Wright v. State


No. 49A04-0108-CR-341


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


772 N.E.2d 449; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1112



July 11, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Wright v. Premier Sec., Inc., 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 27708 (S.D. Ind., Sept. 28, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Israel Nunez Cruz, Master Commissioner. Cause No. 49F19-0101-CM-5626.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) convicted defendant of public intoxication. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was detained by a private security guard in a hotel hallway after he became unruly while intoxicated. On appeal, defendant argued that because he was not in a public place at the time of his arrest, he did not commit the offense of public intoxication. The appellate court ruled that a public place included a place open to common and general use and accessible to the public. The hotel hallway was a public place for purposes of Ind. Code § 7.1-5-1-3. Also, that statute adequately advised the public of the proscribed conduct and was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad as applied. Defendant's challenge to the special deputy statute, Ind. Code § 36-8-10-10.6(a), was not clear and was unsupported by authority. Defendant was not unlawfully detained nor evicted. While the cost of transcript preparation was high, the cost did not infringe upon defendant's right to appeal. The court reporter's failure to transcribe voir dire and opening and closing statements was reasonable and did not infringe on defendant's constitutional right to appeal. There was sufficient evidence to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Hochstedler v. St. Joseph County Solid Waste Mgmt. Dist.


No. 71A03-0110-CV-330


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


770 N.E.2d 910; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1054



June 28, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Transfer Denied October 24, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1054.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 71D01-0009-SC-09618. The Honorable Richard McCormick, Magistrate.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee waste management district sued appellant property owner in the St. Joseph Superior Court, Small Claims Division (Indiana), for a mandatory recycling fee. The trial court found in favor of the district, and the owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owner refused to pay a mandatory recycling fee. The appellate court held the fee was a payment for recycling services associated with the costs of the services and was uniformly imposed upon residential property owners. While it was compulsory, it was a fee and not a tax. The resolution adopting the fee did not violate Ind. Const. art. I, § 23 due to the fact that, under Ind. Code § 13-21-3-12(17), it did not apply to a municipality unless the municipality adopted it. The resolution applied equally to all citizens living in the municipality and was rationally related to the legitimate purpose of the policy of home rule. The resolution's exemption of certain property owners did not violate Ind. Const. art. I, § 23 because it was uniformly applicable to all property owners and was a legitimate exercise of legislative line-drawing based on the fiscal considerations of the difficulty of implementing a program applicable to rental complexes over four units. The resolution was authorized by the district's broad power under Ind. Code § 13-21-3-12 to do all things necessary for the reduction, management, and disposal of solid waste.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

709 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Laughner v. State


No. 82A01-0104-CR-141


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


769 N.E.2d 1147; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 918



June 12, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied August 9, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1446. Petition to Transfer Denied October 31, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Ind. LEXIS 828.
Rehearing denied by Laughner v. State, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1446 (Ind. Ct. App., Aug. 9, 2002)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Laughner v. Indiana, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 3485 (U.S., May 5, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Robert Pigman, Judge. Cause No. 82D02-0008-CF-710.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, reversed, in part, and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana) after his jury conviction of one count of attempted child solicitation. Defendant asserted numerous errors including impossibility of committing the crime of child solicitation as well as sentencing error.


OVERVIEW: A police officer had "entered" computer chat rooms on the internet and portrayed himself as a child, available to be solicited for sex by adults. Defendant engaged in internet conversation with the officer and ultimately made inquiries indicative of whether the officer would like to have sex. When defendant arrived at a location to meet the officer he was arrested. The appellate court held the fact that it was not actually possible for defendant to solicit a child because the officer was not a child, did not bar his conviction for an attempted child solicitation. The appellate court did not find that the trial court committed reversible error in allowing the State to amend the information six days before trial of a charge that had been pending for over six months. The admission of a printout of the internet conversations was not an abuse of discretion. The trial court's instruction implicitly covered the substance of defendant's proposed instruction. Defendant's sentence required remand since that which could not be used to enhance a sentence could not be used to balance circumstances that could properly serve to reduce the sentence as mitigators.


OUTCOME: The defendant's conviction was affirmed, but his sentence was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for resentencing of defendant to less than the presumptive sentence.

Jacobs v. Manhart


No. 20A03-0107-CV-238


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


770 N.E.2d 344; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 892



June 5, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Transfer Denied November 1, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Ind. LEXIS 832.
Petition for Rehearing Denied July 15, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1147.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 20D02-0005-CP-00326. The Honorable Stephen E. Platt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee patient and husband sued appellant doctor and foundation for malpractice, alleging that the patient suffered permanent injuries, suffered great pain, emotional distress, and mental trauma, and that the husband lost consortium, society, and services of the patient. The Elkhart Superior Court (Indiana) denied appellants' motion for preliminary determination as to the statute of limitations. The doctor and the foundation appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued that the trial court erred by not finding in their favor on their motion for a preliminary determination as to the malpractice statute of limitations. Appellees argued that the malpractice statute of limitations was unconstitutional as applied to them. The court of appeals concluded that, looking at the totality of the circumstances giving rise to this claim, it was a practical impossibility for the patient to assert her claim before the expiration of the limitation period and that rigid application of the occurrence-based statute would deny her the meaningful opportunity to pursue her claim. The court of appeals noted that the patient did not have the requisite information to determine that she had a medical malpractice claim until she received the news that she had cancer, which was more than two years after the alleged malpractice occurred. Accordingly, the court of appeals agreed with the trial court that that patient's claim was not barred by the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

711 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Aguilera v. City of E. Chicago


No. 45A05-0106-CV-270


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


768 N.E.2d 978; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 805



May 30, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition to Transfer Denied November 13, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Ind. LEXIS 878. Petition for Rehearing Denied August 2, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT CIVIL DIVISION ROOM THREE. The Honorable Roger Bradford, Special Judge. Cause No. 56D01-0003-MI-21.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner firefighter appealed from a decision of the Lake Superior Court, Civil Division (Indiana), upholding an order of respondent civil service commission discharging him from employment after he failed two drug tests.


OVERVIEW: When a firefighter initially flunked a random drug test, he elected to participate in an employee assistance program that enabled him to remain employed. Because of procedural irregularities, he successfully challenged much of the outcome of the initial proceeding against him, but his record was not expunged. When he failed a follow-up test, administered as part of the voluntary program, he was fired. The appellate court upheld the action, finding no arbitrariness and no constitutional violations, given the safety-sensitive nature of his job. Expungement of employee records was a discretionary remedy, narrowly applied. The firefighter was granted all the other relief he sought from the original determination, but he elected to become subject to further testing when he enrolled in the program. When he failed the second test, he was not deprived of his position without notice and a hearing, but he was not entitled to relitigate all the circumstances of the original test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

Dvorak v. City of Bloomington


No. 53A01-0105-CV-188


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


768 N.E.2d 490; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 694



May 17, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transfer granted by Dvorak v. City of Bloomington, 783 N.E.2d 695, 2002 Ind. LEXIS 1088 (Ind., 2002)
Superseded by Dvorak v. City of Bloomington, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 791 (Ind., Sept. 23, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MONROE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Elizabeth N. Mann, Judge. Cause No. 53C04-9604-OV-350.
Dvorak v. City of Bloomington, 702 N.E.2d 1121, 1998 Ind. App. LEXIS 2191 (Ind. Ct. App., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff City of Bloomington, Indiana, (city) filed a complaint alleging that defendants, a property owner and five other people who occupied his property, were violating Bloomington, Ind., Mun. Code § 20.02.01.00. Defendants filed a motion for summary judgment, claiming that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The Monroe Circuit Court (Indiana) found that the ordinance was constitutional, and defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: A city passed an ordinance which defined a "family" as an individual or people related by blood, marriage, or legal adoption, and any dependent children of the household and specified that, in designated zones, a family included a group of no more than three adults and their dependent children living together as a single housekeeping unit. In all other zones, a family was defined to include a group of no more than five adults and their dependent children living together as a single housekeeping unit. The city filed a complaint against a property owner and five people who were unrelated to him after it learned they were living together in the same dwelling unit. The appellate court held that (1) the acts of the city through its zoning authority were state action subject to the equal privileges and immunities clause of the Indiana Constitution, Ind. Const. art. I, § 23; and (2) because the ordinance was based on mere planning premises without any documented support in professional literature and there was no evidence showing that the classification created by the ordinance was reasonable or substantial, the ordinance violated art. I, § 23.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment.

Jones v. State


No. 49A02-0108-CR-531


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


766 N.E.2d 1258; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 653



April 30, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied June 18, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1001.
Rehearing denied by Jones v. State, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 1001 (Ind. Ct. App., June 18, 2002)
Transfer denied by Jones v. State, 2002 Ind. LEXIS 1113 (Ind., Sept. 5, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G06-0101-CF-6131. The Honorable Jane Magnus-Stinson, Judge. The Honorable Jane Barker, Master Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction of promoting prostitution and sentence to five years' imprisonment after a bench trial in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), after, on the morning of the trial, the State was permitted to amend the information against him, and he was denied a continuance.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the trial court did not err in permitting the amendment to the charging document, as the State deleted one of the alternate bases for defendant's conviction. The amendment did not affect the availability of defendant's defense or the applicability of evidence that existed under the original information. The evidence was sufficient to convict defendant, as he screened the patron, a police officer, arranged the meeting, allowed the patron to inspect the prostitute prior to striking a deal, accepted part of the money himself, and encouraged a sexual encounter by offering to sell the patron condoms when the patron suggested that he needed them. Defendant's sentence did not violate the state constitution's proportionality clause, even though the range of permitted sentences for a prostitution promoter was longer than the sentencing range for prostitution. There was nothing incongruous or unfair about the legislature's decision to punish the two crimes differently. In light of the presumption of constitutionality of statutes, defendant failed to meet the heavy burden on a party asserting unconstitutionality of the sentencing statute.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

714 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Langman v. Milos


No. 64A03-0109-CV-312


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


765 N.E.2d 227; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 470



March 28, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE PORTER SUPERIOR COURT NO. 2. The Honorable Thomas W. Webber, Presiding Judge. Cause No. 64D02-0008-CP-6482.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, patient and his wife, sued defendant health care providers, alleging medical malpractice. The Porter Superior Court (Indiana) granted summary judgment in favor of the health care providers. The patient and his wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient and his wife claimed that surgery on the patient was done negligently and caused the patient's reflex sympathetic dystrophy to advance. The complaint was filed more than four years after the surgery. The patient and his wife argued that because they did not learn of the possibility of the alleged malpractice until much later, when they met with another doctor, they had two years thereafter to file their complaint. The appellate court held that Ind. Code § 34-18-7-1(b) (1998) required the filing of a malpractice action within two years of the occurrence. The case did not pass the first stage of the Rogers and Shah analysis. The patient's worsened and worsening symptoms would have led a reasonably diligent person to have discovered the alleged malpractice and resulting injury. The patient and his wife were aware within several months after the surgery that the pain had increased and spread. Within two years of his surgery, and clearly within two years of his last visit to the health care providers, the patient and his wife had enough information that a reasonably diligent person should have discovered the alleged malpractice claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee developer moved to dismiss appellant commission's appeal of a judgment by the Floyd Circuit Court (Indiana) that reversed the commission's rejection of the developer's request for preliminary approval of a planned subdivision, claiming that the appeal was moot.


OVERVIEW: Although the developer apparently addressed all of the concerns raised by the commission, it denied his preliminary subdivision application. The trial court accordingly concluded that the commission improperly denied the application. The appellate court found that after the commission appealed, the county commissioners approved the subdivision plat. Therefore, the appeal was moot. The commission was obligated to grant the application when the application satisfied the subdivision control ordinance. The denial of the application on the basis of factors outside the ordinance was erroneous. Speculation about unspecified possibilities did not constitute a factual finding. The commission's findings were either unrelated to the subdivision standards, were too vague and indefinite to give the developer notice as to the nature of the alleged violation, or were unsupported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Duncan v. Duncan


No. 15A04-0111-CV-489


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


764 N.E.2d 763; 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 388



March 13, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied March 22, 2002.
Rehearing denied by Duncan v. Duncan, 2002 Ind. App. LEXIS 794 (Ind. Ct. App., Apr. 22, 2002)
Transfer denied by Duncan v. Duncan, 2002 Ind. LEXIS 1098 (Ind., Sept. 6, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DEARBORN CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 15C01-0012-CT-81. The Honorable James D. Humphrey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of defendant-appellee's motion for summary judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff passenger sued defendant motorist seeking damages for injuries sustained in a traffic accident. The motorist filed a motion for summary judgment. The Dearborn Circuit Court (Indiana) granted the motion for summary judgment. The passenger appealed.


OVERVIEW: The passenger and the motorist were sisters. The motorist argued that the Guest Statute, Ind. Code § 34-30-11-1, barred the passenger's claim. The passenger argued that the Guest Statute was inapplicable, as there was evidence to show the motorist's willful and wanton misconduct. The appellate court found that affidavits presented by the passenger were based on inadmissible statements. Documents attached to the affidavit were inadmissible as well. Summary judgment affidavits needed to be made on personal knowledge. The passenger's injuries resulted from the motorist's mistake in judgment rather than from wanton or willful misconduct. The appellate court declined to review the passenger's claims that the Guest Statute was unconstitutional, as she had the opportunity to raise this issue to the trial court but failed to do so. Challenges to the constitutionality of a civil statute could be waived if they could have been raised to the trial court, but the passenger failed to do so. An appellate court would not hold that an appellant waived his or her right to appeal in situations where doing so would have been fundamentally unjust, but that was not the instant situation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
