Hollen v. State


No. 13A01-0001-CR-6


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


740 N.E.2d 149; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 2034



December 15, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CRAWFORD CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable K. Lynn Lopp, Judge. Cause No. 13C01-9809-DF-51.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of and sentence for battery of a law enforcement officer, a class D felony, and operating a vehicle while intoxicated, a class A misdemeanor, by the Crawford Circuit Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: An officer was dispatched to defendant's residence after defendant was reported to have a gun, and to have threatened to kill persons. The dispatched officer observed defendant driving on the wrong side of the road and other evidence of intoxication. The defendant grabbed the officer by the testicles, and would not let go until the officer struck and choked defendant. After testing defendant's alcohol level at the sheriff's department, defendant struck the officer again at the hospital where defendant was taken for treatment. Defendant's conviction and sentence for battery of a law enforcement officer and operating a vehicle while intoxicated was affirmed after his appeal. The prosecution had agreed, in response to the defendant's in limine motion, for the officer not to testify about the reasons for dispatch to investigate defendant. Admission of the officer's testimony about those matters, and admission of his notes, was error, but not reversible error. There was other cumulative testimony.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed. Admission of the officer's testimony, in violation of an in limine order, and his handwritten notes was not reversible error since there was cumulative evidence. Lack of remorse was not an aggravating factor here, since there was no evidence of defendant's bad faith, but the court was persuaded the original sentencing decision would have remained the same.

 

764 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Poling v. State


No. 14A01-9910-PC-342


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


740 N.E.2d 872; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 2043



December 12, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE DAVIESS CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 14C01-8312-CF-070V. The Honorable R. Joseph Howell, Special Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the Daviess Circuit Court's (Indiana) summary disposition for the state, without a hearing, of his second petition for post-conviction relief as to his murder conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant confessed to murder which the only trial witness testified he committed. Appellant was convicted and given 60 years. That was affirmed. Post-conviction relief was denied. Appeal of the denial was dismissed because of counsel's mistake. Summary disposition without a hearing was granted the state in appellant's second post-conviction relief petition. The court affirmed. The trial court's error in not holding a hearing was not prejudicial in that there was no genuine issue of material fact and the state was entitled to judgment as a matter of law. Counsel's mistake was not prejudicial because the court would have affirmed denial of appellant's first post-conviction petition. Appellant's claims of error were waived, barred by res judicata, or failed on the merits. Although his co-defendant was acquitted, Ind. Code § 35-41-2-3 allowed appellant's conviction as principal whether he was characterized as that or as accessory. Trial court appointment of dermatologist expert for appellant would have been wasteful. Ind. Code § 35-50-6-3.3, on sentence reduction for education in prison earned after appellant had earned his, did not violate his equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. As appellant's claims of error were waived, barred by res judicata, or failed on the merits, counsel's mistake in not filing the record, and post-conviction relief court's error in not holding a summary disposition hearing were not prejudicial.

 

765 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. State


No. 06A05-0004-PC-149


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


740 N.E.2d 137; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 2026



December 11, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Martin v. State, 2001 Ind. App. LEXIS 363 (Ind. Ct. App., Feb. 21, 2001)
Transfer denied by Martin v. State, 753 N.E.2d 13, 2001 Ind. LEXIS 449 (Ind., 2001)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE BOONE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Ora A. Kincaid, III, Judge. Cause No. S6320.
French v. State, 266 Ind. 276, 362 N.E.2d 834, 1977 Ind. LEXIS 396 (1977)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the Boone (Indiana) Superior Court's denial of his petition for post-conviction relief, following his convictions for murder and kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder and kidnapping. He filed a petition for post-conviction relief, contending that the conviction for both crimes constituted double jeopardy, and that collateral estoppel required that his conviction of kidnapping be vacated. The court of appeals affirmed, holding that "occurring in the course of a kidnapping" was not one of the elements of murder under Ind. Code § 35-13-4-1. That the murder occurred in the course of a kidnapping only served to elevate the penalty for the crime of murder to death rather than life imprisonment. When appellant's sentence was commuted from death to life imprisonment, the kidnapping became irrelevant to the murder conviction. Under the Blockburger same elements test, murder in the first degree and kidnapping each required proof of at least one element which the other did not, and thus the two convictions survived double jeopardy scrutiny. Second, nonmutual collateral estoppel was not applicable to a criminal case.


OUTCOME: Trial court judgment affirmed. The State charged and proved that appellant committed intentional murder, and the allegation that the murder occurred in the course of a kidnapping served only to enhance the sentence. Therefore, the convictions for both offenses did not violate double jeopardy. Second, collateral estoppel did not apply.

Executive Builders, Inc. v. Trisler


No. 73A01-0001-CV-30


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


741 N.E.2d 351; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1985



December 6, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Transfer Denied July 18, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Ind. LEXIS 626. As Corrected December 14, 2000. Certiorari Denied January 7, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 259.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SHELBY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Charles O'Connor, Judge. Cause No. 73C01-8803-CP-57.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed judgment entered in favor of defendant awarding compensatory and punitive damages for defamation, invasion of privacy, abuse of process and frivolous litigation by the Shelby Circuit Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sued defendant for intentional interference with business. Defendant counterclaimed alleging defamation, invasion of privacy, abuse of process and frivolous litigation. During the appellate process for plaintiffs' claim, defendant's complaint proceeded to trial whereby a jury returned a verdict in favor of defendant for $ 178,240 in compensatory damages and $ 1.54 million in punitives from which plaintiffs appealed. Plaintiffs alleged seven points of error on appeal. The appellate court found that the trial court did not err in refusing to allow plaintiffs to amend their pleadings to match the evidence because there was nothing in the record to validate plaintiffs' amended affirmative defense. Further, the appellate court found that the trial court did not err in submitting certain issues to the jury because the issues were questions of fact and not of law. Finally, the appellate court found that the trial court was not obligated to provide the jury with written copies of the jury instructions and by re-reading the instructions to the jury, it did not abuse its discretion. As such, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed because the trial court properly denied plaintiff's request to amend its pleadings to conform to the evidence inasmuch as the record did not reflect any evidence which would mandate an amended pleading. Additionally, the trial court properly addressed the questions posed by the jury during the trial.

Burke v. Town of Schererville


No. 45A03-9912-CV-461


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


739 N.E.2d 1086; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1981



December 4, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 45D05-9801-CP-41. The Honorable James J. Richards, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the decision of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) dismissing their declaratory judgment action which alleged that defendant town's sewer and water connection fees were unreasonable, excessive, and illegal impact fees.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff builders brought a declaratory action against defendant town, alleging that defendant's sewer and water connection fees were unreasonable, excessive, and illegal impact fees. The trial court dismissed plaintiffs' action. The court affirmed. Defendant did not violate the Impact Fee Statute in establishing the sewer connection fees. Also, because the Municipal Sewage Works Act provided the exclusive procedure for customers to appeal those fees, which procedure was not followed by plaintiffs, the trial court properly dismissed plaintiffs' sewer connection claims. Also, pursuant to Ind. Code § 8-1-3-1, a party seeking to challenge the Indiana Utility Regulatory Commission's approval of a municipality's water rates and charges had 30 days to appeal such approval to the court. Plaintiffs had forfeited their right to challenge the water connection fees by failing to follow that statutory procedure.


OUTCOME: Trial court's dismissal of plaintiffs' action was affirmed. Plaintiffs forfeited their right to challenge defendant town's water connection fees by failing to follow statutory procedure by appealing Indiana Utility Regulatory Commission's approval of fees within time period provided by statute.

 

768 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gerschoffer


No. 71A05-0003-CR-116


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


738 N.E.2d 713; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1920



November 28, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable R. W. Chamblee, Judge. Cause No. 71D08-9906-DF-686.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged an order of the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana), which suppressed evidence of appellee's intoxication obtained at a sobriety checkpoint as being unconstitutionally obtained.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was pulled over at random at a sobriety roadblock, failed sobriety tests, and was charged with drunk driving. The trial court granted his motion to suppress evidence obtained after he was stopped, and the court affirmed. While U.S. Const. amend. IV had a "sobriety roadblock exception" to the requirement that police may not stop a motorist without reasonable suspicion of wrongdoing, the court held that no such exception existed under the search and seizure provisions of Ind. Const. art. I, § 11. The court refused to balance the state's interests in stopping drunk drivers with the citizens' constitutional rights to be free of unreasonable searches and seizures. Because the use of sobriety checkpoints entailed stopping motorists without reasonable suspicion, such checkpoints were held unconstitutional under Ind. Const. art. I, §11.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed, because under the Indiana Constitution, an investigatory stop without reasonable suspicion of wrongdoing was unconstitutional.

 

769 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Teer v. State


No. 69A01-0006-CR-193


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


738 N.E.2d 283; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1832



November 9, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE RIPLEY SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Carl Taul, Judge. Cause No. 69C01-9912-CF-42.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for unlawful possession of a firearm by a serious felon, Ind. Code § 35-47-4-5(c), and sentence in Ripley County (Indiana) Superior Court, claiming the statute and his conviction were unconstitutional and his sentence was unconstitutionally disproportionate.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of unlawful possession of a firearm by a serious violent felon and sought review. The court affirmed. The conviction was not an ex post facto violation where the statute punished appellant for the crime committed in 1999, when he was found to be in possession of the weapon, not for his 1996 felony conviction. There was no substantive due process violation because appellant failed to show a deprivation in his case that was without a rational basis. The warrantless search of the house was not a constitutional violation. There were five adults in the house where appellant was arrested. Officers heard a barking dog, which was a pit bull. Officer safety justified a protective sweep of the house. Sentence of six to 20 years was not unconstitutionally disproportionate where the presumptive sentence was 10 years with the possible addition of 10 years for aggravating factors and appellant's criminal history was an aggravating factor.


OUTCOME: Conviction and sentence affirmed because the statute and his conviction were not unconstitutional and his sentence was not disproportionate considering the aggravating factor.

 

770 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Phelps v. Sybinsky


No. 49A05-9912-CV-554


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


736 N.E.2d 809; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1663



October 20, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49D11-9907-CP-1016. The Honorable John L. Price, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the Marion County (Indiana) Superior Court decision granting appellees' motion to dismiss, claiming Ind. Code § 31-35-2-4.5 (1998) violated the Adoption Assistance and Child Welfare Act, 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 620-628b, 670-679b, violated the Ind. Const. art. III, § 1 separation of power provision, and violated United States Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses.


OVERVIEW: Appellant class representatives had an autistic child with behavioral problems who was removed from their home. Appellants continued to maintain a close relationship with child. Office of family and children (OFC) created a permanency plan, recommending long term foster or institutional care with regular visitation. Subsequently, Ind. Code § 31-35-2-4.5 (1998) was enacted, which required filing of termination petition in appellants' situation. Thus, OFC initiated termination proceedings. Appellants filed a class action complaint. Trial court granted appellees' motion to dismiss. The court affirmed. The statute did not conflict with 42 U.S.C.S. § 675(5)(E) (Supp. III 1997). The only difference between the two was a trial court's involvement in determining child's best interests. Although statute did curtail executive branch discretion, it did not violate separation of powers provision. The legislative branch was exercising its power to enact laws, merely setting a time period to file a termination petition.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because the state statute did not conflict with federal law, it did not violate the state separation of powers provision and did not violate the United States Due Process or Equal Protection Clauses.

 

771 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Gillespie v. State


No. 49A02-0002-PC-113


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


736 N.E.2d 770; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1652



October 17, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49F16-9508-DF-117346. CRIMINAL DIVISION, ROOM 16. The Honorable Evan Dee Goodman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed Marion Superior Court (Indiana) denial of his petitions for post-conviction relief on grounds of newly discovered evidence, to withdraw his guilty plea on grounds that it was not knowing, intelligent, and voluntary, and for relief from judgment on grounds of surprise under Ind. R. Trial P. 60(B).


OVERVIEW: Defendant police officer pled guilty to misdemeanor domestic violence. His guilty plea cost him his job under a federal statute making it illegal for persons convicted of misdemeanors to possess firearms. He petitioned for a new trial on grounds that the statute was newly discovered evidence, to withdraw his guilty plea, on grounds that it was not knowing, intelligent, and voluntary because no one told him of the pending legislation, and for relief from judgment under Ind. R. Trial P. 60(b), available in cases of mistake, surprise, or excusable neglect. Defendant was not entitled to relief under any theory. The new statute was not newly discovered evidence; it made defendant no less guilty of the underlying offense. His plea was not invalid, because collateral consequences had nothing to do with its integrity. Finally, relief from judgment was only available to defendants who raised a meritorious defense, and defendant had none.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, because collateral effects of defendant's guilty plea did not affect validity of judgment based on his having committed the offense in question. Federal statute that had collateral effect was not newly discovered evidence, nor did it cause the type of surprise entitling defendant to relief from judgment.

Clark v. CSX Transp., Inc.


No. 29A02-9902-CV-139


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


737 N.E.2d 752; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1583



October 12, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Clark v. CSX Transp., Inc., 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 2050 (Ind. Ct. App., Dec. 7, 2000)
Transfer denied by Clark v. CSX Transp., Inc., 783 N.E.2d 691, 2002 Ind. LEXIS 707 (Ind., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HAMILTON COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT NO. 3. Cause No. 29D03-9308-CP-404. The Honorable William J. Hughes, Judge.
CSX Transp. v. Clark, 646 N.E.2d 1003, 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 162 (Ind. Ct. App., 1995)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grantors' successors subclass and defendant railroad sought review of summary declaratory judgment of Hamilton County Superior Court (Indiana) construing 21 deeds of strips of property to defendant; plaintiffs argued they all conveyed easements and defendant argued that they all conveyed estates in fee. Defendant also alleged due process violations.


OVERVIEW: Defendant railroad's predecessor used strips of land acquired from plaintiffs' predecessors for use as railroad rights-of-way. Plaintiffs brought a class action seeking a declaratory judgment that defendant's predecessors acquired only easements that were extinguished upon abandonment, but defendant argued that the deeds conveyed fee interests. The court looked to each of 21 deeds, finding some to convey fee interests and some to convey easements. In determining whether deeds were ambiguous enough to construe them against the original railroad drafters, the court looked primarily to the granting clauses to see whether they contained limiting language. Failure of plaintiffs to provide proof that they had quieted title in themselves did not deprive defendant of due process, because at this stage plaintiffs only sought declaratory relief eliminating defendant as a claimant.


OUTCOME: Looking to granting clauses to determine existence of ambiguities, the court affirmed for all deeds that trial court found had conveyed fee estates, and reversed only one determination that a deed conveyed an easement. There was no due process violation because plaintiffs merely requested declaratory relief, not quieting of title.

 

773 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Shoultz v. State


No. 82A01-9912-CR-436


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


735 N.E.2d 818; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1483



September 22, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Nancy Hankins Long, Magistrate. Cause No. 82D05-9712-CM-8710.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana), convicting him for resisting law enforcement, a class A misdemeanor, and disorderly conduct, a class B misdemeanor, in a suit to determine whether the arresting officer used excessive force against defendant in violation of U.S. Const. amend. IV, and whether defendant's disorderly conduct conviction violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 9.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of resisting law enforcement, a class A misdemeanor, and disorderly conduct, a class B misdemeanor. Defendant appealed his convictions, contending that the arresting officer used excessive force against him in violation of U.S. Const. amend. IV, and that his disorderly conduct conviction violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 9. The court held, first, that the consideration of the Graham factors, the severity of the crime, whether defendant posed an immediate threat to the safety of the arresting officer or others, and whether defendant was actively resisting arrest or attempting to evade arrest by flight, compelled the conclusion that the force the officer used against defendant was objectively unreasonable and unconstitutionally excessive. Second, the speech defendant engaged in prior to his arrest, and which plaintiff relied upon to support his disorderly conduct conviction, was protected political expression. Defendant's speech was directed to the legality and appropriateness of police conduct toward a third party and constituted criticism of an official acting under color of law. Consequently, defendant's convictions were reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions. The force the arresting officer used against defendant was objectively unreasonable and unconstitutionally excessive, and the speech defendant engaged in prior to his arrest was directed to the legality and appropriateness of the arresting officer's conduct toward a third party and constituted criticism of an official acting under color of law.

 

774 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gunn


No. 71A04-9912-CR-543


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


735 N.E.2d 304; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1480; 16 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1300



September 21, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Rehearing January 10, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Ind. App. LEXIS 3.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 71D08-9906-DF-621. The Honorable R.W. Chamblee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a prosecution of defendant for, inter alia, operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated resulting in serious bodily injury to another person, the State appealed an order of the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana), which granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was the South Bend police chief, was involved in a collision with another vehicle while he was driving a city-owned vehicle, and there was more than $ 1,500 in property damages. South Bend had in place a contract between the city and the police department providing for mandatory drug and alcohol testing when there was reasonable cause to believe that an employee operating a city-owned vehicle caused an accident causing $ 1,500 or more in property damages or causing injury to the employee or other individual to determine if drugs, alcohol, or other metabolites were in the employee's system. Defendant was given two breath tests. The first resulted in a blood alcohol content of .101, and the second resulted in a blood alcohol content of .106. Defendant was charged with, inter alia, operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated resulting in serious bodily injury to another person, but trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress the test results. The court affirmed, concluding that the use of the city's workplace drug testing policy to pursue criminal prosecutions against employees was a violation of these employees' rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OUTCOME: Order granting defendant's motion to suppress evidence affirmed; use of city's workplace drug testing policy to pursue criminal prosecutions against employees was a violation of these employees' constitutional rights.

 

775 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Noble v. State


No. 49A02-9902-CR-105


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


734 N.E.2d 1119; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1465



September 14, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49F16-9709-DF-139778. The Honorable Evan D. Goodman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Marion County (Indiana), which convicted defendant for battery in violation of Ind. Code Ann. § 35-42-2-1(a)(1), battery causing serious bodily injury and battery with a deadly weapon in violation of Ind. Code Ann. § 35-42-2-1(a)(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for battery in violation of Ind. Code Ann. § 35-42-2-1(a)(1), battery causing serious bodily injury, and battery with a deadly weapon in violation of Ind. Code Ann. § 35-42-2-1(a)(3). Defendant contended that the prosecution improperly induced defendant to move for a mistrial, and that defendant's convictions for battery causing serious bodily injury and battery with a deadly weapon violated double jeopardy principles. The court found that defendant's retrial did not violate federal double jeopardy because the prosecutor had not intended to force defendant to seek a mistrial. However, the convictions were for the same offense, violating double jeopardy under Ind. Const. art. 1, § 14, since the jury probably used the same evidentiary facts to establish the essential elements of both offenses. Since both battery convictions were of equal length and ran concurrently, the court vacated the sentence for battery with a deadly weapon.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed in part; defendant's retrial did not violate federal double jeopardy; however, defendant's convictions for battery causing serious bodily injury and battery with a deadly weapon were for same offense, violating State double jeopardy principals, because the essential elements of both offenses were established by the same evidentiary facts.

 

776 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


J.A.C. v. Koenig (In re J.A.C.)


No. 49A04-9912-JV-567


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


734 N.E.2d 1057; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1785



August 16, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published September 6, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT, JUVENILE DIVISION. The Honorable Geoffrey Gaither, Magistrate Judge. Cause Nos. 49D09-9810-JP-000284, 49D08-9810-GU-000811.

Originally Reported in Table Case Format at: 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1328.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father appealed Marion County Superior Court (Indiana) custody order to the extent that it granted visitation rights to respondent, child's late mother's sister, on grounds that trial court's findings and conclusions were insufficient to support the order and that such visitation violated Indiana law and U.S. Const. privacy rights.


OVERVIEW: At the time the mother of petitioner's child died, she and the child were in the care of respondent, her sister. Petitioner sought custody, and received it subject to respondent's visitation rights. Petitioner challenged the visitation order as unsupported by the findings of fact and conclusions based on them, and the court agreed. Despite the deference usually shown to the trial court's findings, especially in family law cases, the court found that the trial court failed to make two findings that were absolutely required before making a grant of visitation to a non-parent, non-grandparent third party: existence of a custodial and parental relationship and that visitation would be in the child's best interest. Since these findings were not made, there was no basis for ordering visitation. Petitioner also challenged the order as contrary to Indiana law and violative of family privacy rights, but the court did not reach these issues.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the visitation order, because the trial court had failed to make required findings that a custodial and parental relationship existed between respondent and child and that visitation would be in the child's best interest. There was no need to consider petitioner's other arguments.

Ling v. Stillwell


No. 49A02-0002-CV-119


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


732 N.E.2d 1270; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1218



August 15, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49D12-9909-MI-1363. The Honorable Susan Macey Thompson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hospital appealed the judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) which denied defendant's motion for summary judgment in medical malpractice action brought by plaintiff seeking to recover damages resulting from the death of plaintiff's mother.


OVERVIEW: After becoming aware that his mother's death at defendant hospital was part of a murder investigation, plaintiff filed a complaint for damages. The trial court denied defendant's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, defendant challenged whether: (1) the trial court properly denied defendant's motion for summary judgment on the issue of the statute of limitations; (2) the trial court properly considered plaintiff's designated evidence in ruling on defendant's motion; and (3) the trial court improperly relied on the doctrine of collateral estoppel in ruling on defendant's motion. The court affirmed the judgment, holding the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for summary judgment. The court reasoned that plaintiff did not have reason to know, nor should he have known, that his mother's death was attributable to negligence until after the two-year limitations period had expired, therefore, plaintiff's claim was properly filed. Further, the court concluded that plaintiff's designation of evidence was proper, and the trial court could deny the motion for summary judgment on any theory the evidence supported, and did not improperly rely on collateral estoppel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment because plaintiff's claim was properly filed. Plaintiff did not have reason to know that his mother's death was attributable to negligence until after the two-year limitations period had expired. Further, plaintiff's designation of evidence was proper, and the trial court did not improperly rely on collateral estoppel in ruling on defendant hospital's motion.

Freidline v. Civil S. Bend


No. 71A03-9912-CV-442


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


733 N.E.2d 490; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1203



August 8, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 71C01-9812-CP-017890. The Honorable Terry A. Crone, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant land trust sought review of a summary judgment entered in the St. Joseph Circuit Court (Indiana) in favor of appellee city in appellee's action to recover monetary penalties imposed pursuant to Ind. Code § 36-7-9-7(d) for appellant's failure to make repairs to real property.


OVERVIEW: Appellee city ordered appellant land trust to make repairs to real property because it was in violation of building codes. Appellant did not make the repairs, and appellee imposed penalties pursuant to Ind. Code § 36-7-9-7(d). Appellee filed a record for collection, and both parties filed motions for summary judgment. The trial court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment. Appellants were not entitled to the constitutional protections of a criminal proceeding under Ind. Const. art. I, § 13 and U.S. Const. amend. VI because the penalty provision of Ind. Code § 36-7-9-7(d) was civil. The sanction was civil because the legislature labeled it a civil penalty and the only remedy was monetary. Also, the penalty provision did not subject appellant to affirmative restraint or disability, did not promote the traditional aims of punishment, and did not punish past behavior.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that the penalties were civil, and thus the constitutional protections for criminal proceedings were not applicable.

 

779 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Danks v. State


No. 46A03-9908-PC-330


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


733 N.E.2d 474; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1155



August 3, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAPORTE CIRCUIT COURT, CRIMINAL DIVISION. Cause No. 46C01-8410-CF-5157-C. The Honorable Steven King, Special Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an order by the LaPorte Circuit Court, Criminal Division (Indiana), denying his petition for post-conviction relief in which petitioner claimed that his rights to a speedy trial and effective assistance of counsel violated U.S. Const. amend. VI.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner challenged denial of his post-conviction petition that sought relief from his conviction for felony murder. Petitioner presented two issues for the court's review: 1) whether a delay of nearly six and one-half years constituted a denial of petitioner's right to a speedy trial; 2) whether petitioner received ineffective assistance of counsel. The court balanced four Barker factors; the delay in the case was inordinately long and the court was assuming that the speedy trial issue was timely raised. The reason for most of the delay was attributable to petitioner's incompetency, not inaction by the State, though one year and four months of the delay was fairly attributable to the State's negligence. Given the State's tardiness, petitioner's burden of establishing grounds for relief on his speedy trial claim was less. Petitioner failed to provide the court with indicators of prejudice. As to the claim of ineffective assistance of counsel, petitioner was not prejudiced by defense counsel's failure to file a motion to dismiss on the ground of unconstitutional delay, nor did defense counsel's decision fall below an objectively reasonable level. Judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Petitioner failed to show that he was prejudiced by delay in trial, although part of the delay was caused by the State's negligence. Counsel was not ineffective by failing to file motion to dismiss.

Gordon v. Gordon


No. 43A03-0001-CV-25


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


733 N.E.2d 468; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1145; 16 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 977



July 28, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE KOSCIUSKO CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 43C01-9909-PO-151. The Honorable Richard W. Sand, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent appealed a judgment from the Kosciusko Circuit Court (Indiana), granting petitioner a protective order pursuant to Ind. Code § 34-26-2-12.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the issuance of the protective order because the trial court had jurisdiction to hear the case because respondent's sexual, verbal, and/or mental abuse of petitioner was not an acceptable term or condition of employment under Ind. Code § 22-6-1-2, and thus, was not a "freedom" protected by the Anti-Injunction Act, Ind. Code § 22-6-1-1 et seq. Additionally, the trial court properly issued the protective order once it had decided that petitioner was truthful about respondent's actions, and that the conduct was sufficient to constitute abuse, harassment, or disturbing of the peace. Moreover the protective order was not vague and addressed the specific situation. Finally, the order was no more restrictive than that necessary to accomplish the goal of a broad prohibition on all forms of communication at the workplace between the parties, and although the order limited respondent's U.S. amend. I right to speech and association, it allowed both parties to retain their jobs with their mutual employer.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The trial court had jurisdiction to hear the case because respondent's conduct was not a protected by the Anti-Injunction Act; the order was not vague and it was as restrictive only as necessary to bar communication at work between the parties; and, the order limited respondent's U.S. amend. I right to speech and association, but allowed both parties to keep their employment.

Coffer v. Arndt


No. 49A02-9910-CV-720


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


732 N.E.2d 815; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1082



July 20, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49D01-9901-CT-47. The Honorable David A. Jester, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed summary judgment grant to defendant optometrist, entered by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), in a case where plaintiff filed a medical malpractice suit against defendant, his regular optometrist for several years, after defendant failed to diagnose plaintiff's glaucoma and plaintiff was informed of it by another doctor.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff patient sued defendant optometrist. Plaintiff had been treated by defendant for several years. He stopped seeing or being treated by defendant in October of 1995, because defendant referred plaintiff to another doctor. Plaintiff saw that doctor that November. That doctor referred plaintiff to a glaucoma specialist who informed plaintiff in December of 1995 that plaintiff had glaucoma and had it for several years. Plaintiff waited until December of 1997 to sue. Defendant moved for summary judgment and alleged the two-year statute of limitation period ran out in October of 1997, two years after he last could have missed diagnosing the glaucoma. The trial court granted the motion. Plaintiff appealed. The court affirmed. The court held the medical malpractice statute of limitations was constitutional as applied to patients, such as plaintiff, who discovered the medical malpractice well before the limitations period expired, but after the medical malpractice had occurred.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because suit was not filed within two-year statutory limitations period after plaintiff stopped being treated by defendant, which was the last date failure to diagnose could have occurred, because plaintiff still had 22 months to file when he was informed of the wrong, yet did not timely file.

Schulz v. State


No. 31A01-9907-CV-240


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


731 N.E.2d 1041; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1066



July 14, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HARRISON CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 31C01-9610-CP-214. The Honorable Robert L. Bennett, Special Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners and appellant organization appealed order from the Harrison Circuit Court (Indiana), dismissing their claim, for lack of standing, against appellee State and appellee Indiana Gaming Commission challenging riverboat gambling statute.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowners and appellant organization challenged the dismissal of their claim against the appellee State and appellee Indiana Gaming Commission (Commission). Although they raised several issues for review, the court found one dispositive: whether appellants had standing to challenge a riverboat gambling law. The court affirmed. Appellant landowners, in alleging damage to their aesthetic interests, were in essence claiming damage to their property. This was the only legally protectable injury identified in their complaint. Nevertheless, the harm appellants alleged was too remote. The trial court did not err in determining that appellant landowners lacked standing. The trial court also did not err in determining that appellant organization lacked standing. Appellants also alleged that the enactment of the riverboat gambling law violated the single subject requirement of the Indiana Constitution. Nevertheless, they claimed no particular harm from this violation. Appellants' injury from this alleged violation was the same general injury suffered by the public as a whole. This was insufficient to confer standing on a party. Judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Appellants lacked standing to challenge gaming statute, as their harm was too remote and injury was no different than that that would be suffered by public as a whole.

Burton v. Elskens


No. 79A02-9911-CV-747


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


730 N.E.2d 1281; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 1036



July 6, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 11, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 2246.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 79D01-9904-CT-19. The Honorable David J. Crouse, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the Tippecanoe Superior Court (Indiana) decision granting summary judgment in appellee doctor's favor, finding the doctrine of continuing wrongs did not toll the statute of limitation on their medical malpractice complaint against appellee.


OVERVIEW: In October 1994, appellee doctor performed a craniotomy on appellant woman. Almost immediately after surgery appellant suffered a stroke. Appellee administered postoperative outpatient treatment until May 1995. In May 1997, appellants filed a proposed complaint with appellee department, alleging negligence in treatment and loss of consortium. The court affirmed summary judgment in appellee doctor's favor, finding the complaint was time barred. Injury occurred in October 1994 and appellant woman experienced immediate complications. There was no continuing wrong that would toll the statute of limitations where there was no injury producing conduct of a continuous nature. Appellant did not suffer from a disease with a long latency period and her condition did not manifest pain or symptoms at a later date. Appellants did not present any reason why they could not have discovered their cause of action within the appropriate two-year period.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because the continuing wrong doctrine did not toll the statute of limitations concerning their medical malpractice complaint against appellee doctor.

Sims v. U.S. Fid. & Guar. Co.


No. 49A02-9904-CV-295


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


730 N.E.2d 232; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 906



June 23, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49D12-9904-CT-489. The Honorable Susan Macey-Thompson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed order of Marion Superior Court (Indiana) dismissing for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, under Ind. Code § 22-3-4-12.1, his gross negligence, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and intentional deprivation of statutory rights under Worker's Compensation Act claims.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was injured while working at a construction site. He contacted defendant with respect to scheduling medical care and temporary total disability benefits. Defendant did not respond. A few weeks later, plaintiff again contacted defendant and still did not receive a response. He then filed his complaint. His allegations amounted to independent torts which did not fall within the exclusive jurisdiction of the Indiana Worker's Compensation Board. The portion of Ind. Code § 22-3-4-12.1 which gave the board exclusive jurisdiction to determine whether the employer's worker's compensation insurance carrier committed an independent tort in adjusting or settling the claim was unconstitutional as violative of Ind. Const. art. I, § 12, which guaranteed that courts were open, and Ind. Const. art. I, § 20, which guaranteed the right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, holding plaintiff's right of access to courts was unreasonably denied, and right to jury trial was eviscerated, and thus statute granting exclusive jurisdiction to Indiana Worker's Compensation Board for independent torts committed by insurance carrier was unconstitutional.

Tipton County v. State ex rel. Nash


No. 48A02-9912-CV-810


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


731 N.E.2d 12; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 898



June 21, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MADISON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Carl VanDorn, Senior Judge. Cause No. 48C01-9809-CP-534.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county appealed a summary judgment of Madison County Court (Indiana) that determined that defendant's cessation of paying plaintiff judge voluntary supplemental wages violated Ind. Const. art. VII, § 19; plaintiff cross-appealed summary denial of his claims for liquidated damages and attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: Indiana law permitted counties to contribute up to $ 5,000 to their judges' salaries. After the legislature enacted large judicial salary increases, defendant elected to discontinue supplemental payments. Plaintiff judge sought writ of mandamus and other relief, arguing that this constituted a salary reduction in violation of Ind. Const. art. VII, § 19. Applying traditional principles of statutory construction, the court determined both from plain language and legislative history that the statutory scheme envisioned a single system of judicial salaries, not two separate systems. When the two sources of income were combined for each year, plaintiff's actual salary was never decreased, so defendant's action was not unconstitutional. Since plaintiff had now lost on the merits, his cross-appeal of the trial court's denial of liquidated damages and attorney fees was also unsuccessful.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part, and remanded with instructions to enter summary judgment for defendant, because it construed statutes to mean state and local payments constituted a single salary; thus, plaintiff's pay was never unconstitutionally reduced. The court affirmed damages and fees denial, since plaintiff did not prevail on merits.

Vranicar v. Board of Comm'rs


No. 07A05-9911-CV-493


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIFTH DISTRICT


730 N.E.2d 752; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 895



June 20, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE BROWN CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 07C01-9807-MI-0199. The Honorable Heather M. Mollo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners appealed the decision of the Brown Circuit Court (Indiana) dismissing their action seeking review of decision of respondent Brown County Board of Commissioners which refused to vacate a public right of way.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners' property abutted a county road. The road was used only by the Forest Service, U.S. Department of Agriculture, and petitioners, and their guests. Petitioners attempted to vacate the part of the road abutting their property. Respondent Brown County Board of Commissioners wanted to vacate the whole road, or none of it. The Forest Service did not support vacation of the whole road. Respondent denied the petition since it did not benefit the County. The trial court did not have subject matter jurisdiction of the appeal, since Ind. Code § 36-7-3-12(f) was more specific and more recent than Ind. Code § 36-2-2-27. This case was not the taking of private property involving a constitutional right. Petitioners did not show harm by a governmental act or change in the status quo depriving them of a statutory or constitutional right, and thus there was not a nonstatutory appeal right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that since the status quo was maintained, there was no harm to petitioners, and the trial court did not have statutory subject matter jurisdiction of petitioners' appeal, petitioners did not have the right to appeal the denial of a road vacation.

Marley v. State


No. 49A02-9908-CR-617


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


729 N.E.2d 1011; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 861



June 8, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. Cause No. 49G02-9706-CF-85105. The Honorable Ruth D. Reichard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), entering an interlocutory order requiring defendant to proceed under the effects of battery statute in order to present Battered Women's Syndrome evidence, and excluding a videotape of defendant engaging in sexual acts with the victim.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder, attempted murder, and other offenses. The trial court ordered that defendant present evidence of Battered Women's Syndrome (BWS) under the Effects of Battery statute, Ind. Code § 35-41-3-11, and excluded a videotape offered by defendant showing defendant involved in sexual acts with the victim, who was a relative of defendant who had been convicted of sexually molesting defendant. Defendant filed an interlocutory appeal. The court held the trial court did not abuse its discretion with respect to admission of the BWS evidence. The court found that to the extent involuntary behavior of defendant was contended to result from a mental disease, the state insanity statute applied. Therefore, defendant was not entitled to present evidence as to her mental state without pursuing an insanity defense. The court held the trial court properly excluded the videotape. The court found the videotape's probative value to show dissociative conduct by defendant was minimal, and the potential of the videotape to prejudice the jury against the victim exceeded its probative value.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision, because the trial court did not abuse discretion in ruling defendant could not introduce Battered Women's Syndrome evidence unless she did so pursuant to the Effects of Battery statute, and the probative value of the videotape in question to show dissociative conduct by defendant was minimal.

Eukers v. State


No. 34A02-9907-CR-502


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


728 N.E.2d 219; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 711



May 15, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HOWARD SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable John C. Wood, Judge. Cause No. 34D03-9801-CM-190.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction for violating Ind. Code § 20-8.1-3-34, the Compulsary Attendance Act, in the Howard Superior Court (Indiana), alleging that the authority delegated to local school corporations to establish attendance policies, the violation of which subjected a parent to criminal liability, was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative function.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the mother and custodial parent of an elementary school student. The school corporation's attendance policy provided, inter alia, that after a student accumulated 20 unexcused absences, the county prosecutor was notified by school officials. Upon notification that the student had accumulated 23 absences, the State charged defendant with violating the Compulsory Attendance Act, Ind. Code § 20-8.1-3-34. Following a bench trial, defendant was found guilty and sentenced. Defendant appealed, arguing that the legislature, by permitting Indiana's school districts to establish their own attendance polices, had impermissibly delegated the purely legislative function of defining the elements and acts which constitute criminal activity to the individual school attendance districts. The appellate court affirmed, holding that the General School Powers Act, Ind. Code §§ 25-5-1 to -6, was not unconstitutional because the discretion whether to prosecute a parent lay solely with the prosecutor.


OUTCOME: Conviction of parent for child's non-attendance was affirmed; delegation of authority to school districts to establish attendance policies was not unconstitutional because it was the prosecutor whom the legislature vested with discretion in deciding whether to prosecute a parent, and this discretion operated independently of school's attendance policy.

 

791 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


No. 85A02-9911-CR-753


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


727 N.E.2d 763; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 600



April 27, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE WABASH CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Daniel J. Vanderpool, Judge. Cause No. 85C01-9303-CF-19.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Wabash Circuit Court (Indiana), which revoked defendant's probation.


OVERVIEW: The trial court revoked defendant's probation on the basis that he had had contact with a five-year-old boy. Defendant had been convicted of child molesting and attempted child molesting. On appeal, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to show that there had been substantial contact between defendant and the boy. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in revoking defendant's probation. Defendant contended that Ind. Code § 35-38-2-2.4, the statute that formed the basis for the "no contact" provision of his probation agreement, was unconstitutionally vague and unconstitutionally overbroad. No reasonable person of ordinary intelligence would have had difficulty determining that intentional interaction with and physical touching of the boy was proscribed by § 35-38-2-2.4. It was inherent in § 35-38-2-2.4 that a probationer was not required to avoid inadvertent or unintentional contact with persons less than 16 years of age.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; the trial court did not err in concluding that there was sufficient evidence to support the revocation of defendant's probation, and the statute providing the premise for the no-contact condition of probation was neither vague nor overbroad.

 

792 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Sullivan v. City of Evansville


No. 82A01-9906-CV-191


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


728 N.E.2d 182; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 604



April 27, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Carl A. Heldt, Judge. Cause No. 82C01-9805-CP-167.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer challenged the judgment of the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana) granting summary judgment in favor of appellee city in his appeal of a disciplinary order of the Evansville Police Merit Commission.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was suspended for his misconduct during a traffic stop of a 17-year-old girl. Appellant challenged the decision, and the trial court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment. Because appellant failed to raise the police merit commission's (commission) lack of a legal quorum at the administrative hearing, he failed to preserve the issue for appellate review, and the court affirmed the grant of summary judgment. Appellant also waived his denial of due process claim for lack of proper notice because he reviewed the complaint against him and appeared before the commission. Appellant failed to show that admission of testimony regarding charges of prior misconduct was reversible error because he cross-examined the witnesses and did not allege that the commission was biased or acted in bad faith. The court reversed summary judgment as to the imposition of probation and a mental health examination because neither was provided for under Ind. Code § 36-8-3-4(b).


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed as to appellant's lack of a legal quorum and denial of due process claims because he failed to raise the issues before the administrative hearing and failed to show that admission of testimony was reversible error. Judgment reversed as to the imposition of probation and mental health examination.

 

793 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Metropolitan Dev. Comm'n v. Schroeder


No. 49A04-9901-CV-40


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


727 N.E.2d 742; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 599



April 27, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Richard P. Good, Judge. Cause No. 49F12-9712-CP-4039.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) decision finding appellant was not entitled to an injunction enforcing a variance prohibiting outdoor storage of vehicles.


OVERVIEW: Appellee purchased property in 1979 under a zoning classification that prohibited gasoline stations from storing inoperable vehicles other than those awaiting immediate repair. In 1977, a variance was granted limiting the number of vehicles that could be parked outside, overnight. Appellee was not aware of this because a title search did not reveal it. In 1997, appellant filed a complaint claiming property was being used for outdoor vehicle storage. The court reversed, finding appellant was in violation of the ordinance. Laches, waiver, and acquiescence were not valid defense to a municipality violation. No non-conforming use existed prior to the enactment of the zoning ordinance. Appellee alleged the violation occurred in October 1997 and the complaint was filed December 1997; thus, it was within the statute of limitations. Appellant was not estopped from filing where they had filed a previous complaint. No taking occurred where property still had viable uses.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed because appellee was subject to the variance prohibiting outdoor storage of vehicles where defenses were not applicable to zoning ordinances and property still had viable economic uses.

 

794 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Wiggins v. State


No. 84A01-9905-CR-169


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


727 N.E.2d 1; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 502



April 10, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VIGO SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Michael H. Eldred, Judge. Cause No. 84D01-9802-CF-42.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following his conviction at a jury trial of nonsupport of a dependent, enhanced because of the amount of arrearage, defendant appealed from the Vigo Superior Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from conviction for nonsupport of a dependent. Defendant waived his claim that Ind. Code Ann. § 35-46-1-5(a) was unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous. His ex post facto claim failed. The record showed he provided his children only a few items of clothing and paid minimal support during the relevant time. Defendant earned enough during that time to pay his support obligation. Defendant admitted that he chose not to pay support while the arrearage accumulated, notwithstanding that he was spending significant amounts of money on nonessential items for his children. Defendant acknowledged that support payments were a low priority. He admitted to not filing tax returns because he knew any refund would be intercepted for support. Defendant waived any objections to closing argument by not raising them immediately. There was strong evidence of guilt. The sentencing statement should have explained why less than the presumptive sentence was imposed upon defendant.


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting and sentencing defendant for nonsupport of a dependent was affirmed in part and remanded in part. There was strong evidence of defendant's guilt, including his own testimony. However, the sentencing decision to impose less than the presumptive time on defendant was not adequately explained. Remanded for explanation.

 

795 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Rene v. Reed


No. 49A02-9907-CV-457


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


726 N.E.2d 808; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 443



April 4, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. CIVIL DIVISION, ROOM 12. The Honorable Susan Macey Thompson, Judge. Cause No. 49D12-9805-CP-730.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, disabled students, brought an interlocutory appeal of the Marion Superior Court's (Indiana) decision denying their motion to certify class actions under 42 U.S.C.S § 1983, Individuals with Disabilities Education Act, 20 U.S.C.S. § 1401, alleging defendant violated due process rights by requiring them to take a standardized graduation test.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, disabled students, sought class certification of claims under 42 U.S.C.S § 1983, and the Individuals with Disabilities Education Act, 20 U.S.C.S. § 1401, alleging their due process rights were violated by forcing them to pass a standardized graduation test, while plaintiffs had previously been exempt from standardized testing. The trial court denied class certification, and plaintiff filed an interlocutory appeal. The court held the trial court improperly denied class certification. The court held plaintiffs fulfilled all requirements of Ind. Trial R. 23(A), including numerosity, common questions of law and fact, typical claims and defenses, and fair and adequate protection of the interests of the class. The court held plaintiffs were not required to exhaust administrative remedies. The issues presented were pure questions of law, as plaintiffs argued the administrative agency did not have authority to declare the test invalid, or award a diploma without passing the graduation test.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the denial of class certification, because plaintiffs satisfied all requirements for class certification, and plaintiffs were not required to exhaust administrative remedies prior to bring the action.

 

796 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Balls v. State


No. 49A04-9908-CR-374


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


725 N.E.2d 450; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 315



March 15, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 3, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 2287.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. CRIMINAL DIVISION 6. The Honorable, Jane Magnus-Stinson, Judge. Cause No. 49G06-9806-CF-89219.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed with respect to welfare fraud conviction and restitution order, but matter remanded to trial court with instructions to vacate theft conviction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), for welfare fraud and theft, related to his theft of a box of food stamps.


OVERVIEW: When a clerk took a break from her job issuing food stamps, she left an unopened box containing food stamps unattended. The box was not found anywhere in the office. The numbers on the missing food stamps were reported to retailers. When used, they were traced to appellant. Appellant was convicted of both theft and welfare fraud. On appeal, the judgment was affirmed with respect to the welfare fraud conviction and the restitution order, but the matter was remanded to the trial court with instructions to vacate the theft conviction. The trial court had found appellant guilty of both welfare fraud and theft. While appellant had only been sentenced for welfare fraud, the theft conviction was not vacated. "Merger" of the convictions was inadequate; the "merged" offense had to be vacated. The trial court did not err by ordering restitution in the amount on the face of the food stamps.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed with respect to welfare fraud conviction and restitution order, but remanded to trial court with instructions to vacate the theft conviction. It was clear that the welfare fraud statute was not unconstitutionally vague; it was intended to punish stealing or otherwise dealing in food stamps.

 

797 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Owner-Operator Indep. Drivers Ass'n v. Ind. Dep't of Revenue


No. 49A02-9906-CV-449


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


725 N.E.2d 891; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 263



March 9, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 4, 2000. Rehearing Denied April 17, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 2291.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable William T. Lawrence, Judge. Cause No. 49C01-9905-CP-1190.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the judgment of the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana), granting appellee Indiana Department of State Revenue's motion to dismiss appellants' suit for a tax refund, based upon lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Appellants filed a class action suit in alleging that the Motor Carrier Fuel Tax, Ind. Code § 6-6-4.1-1 et seq., imposed upon commercial vehicles was unconstitutional. Appellants specifically contended the fuel consumed upon the Indiana Toll Road should be tax exempt. Appellants consisted of out-of-state commercial motor carriers who paid tax for fuel used based upon the miles they drove within Indiana. The court affirmed the dismissal of appellants' suit, finding that the relevant portions of Ind. Code § 6-6-4.1-1 et seq. and the International Fuel Tax Agreement did not exempt appellants from seeking a claim for refund from appellee before seeking judicial review. Also, the court found that because appellants' class action suit asked for a tax refund, until each member complied with the administrative requirements, no court had subject matter jurisdiction over their cause of action.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; because appellants' class action suit asked for a tax refund, until each member complied with the administrative requirements, no court had subject matter jurisdiction over their cause of action.

 

798 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


State v. Price


No. 79A02-9911-CR-749


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


724 N.E.2d 670; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 248



February 29, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE COUNTY COURT. The Honorable Gregory J. Donat, Judge. Cause No. 79E01-9810-DF-340.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions that trial court vacate its order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order from the Tippecanoe County Court (Indiana) in favor of defendant suppressing all evidence obtained pursuant to the stop of defendant's vehicle holding that the stop was not authorized.


OVERVIEW: The State appealed a suppression order disallowing evidence obtained by a police officer who stopped appellee driver because appellee was not wearing a seatbelt and after smelling alcohol gave appellee alcohol tests, which appellee failed. However, the court held that the officer had reasonable suspicion to make the stop because he noticed that the seatbelt was slack and to the side of appellee's seat. Appellee argued that individuals with higher incomes who drive sport utility vehicles and trucks were not subject to stops for not wearing seatbelts. Consequently, individuals who could not afford sport utility vehicles, such as the appellee, were denied equal protection. The court, however, held that the disparate treatment in the seatbelt enforcement statute was reasonably related to inherent characteristics, which distinguished the unequally treated classes.


OUTCOME: The suppression order was reversed and remanded with instructions to vacate because the officer did have reasonable suspicion to stop the vehicle and because the statute did not unconstitutionally deny equal protection.

 

799 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Save the Valley, Inc. v. Indiana Dep't of Envtl. Mgmt.


No. 49A02-9904-CV-266


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


724 N.E.2d 665; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 253



February 29, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 13, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 2218.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Richard P. Good, Special Judge. Cause No. 49F12-9809-CP-3118.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an environmental group and certain landowners, appealed from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which granted appellee Indiana Department of Environmental Management's motion to dismiss appellants' suit based on appellants' failure to exhaust administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, an environmental group and certain landowners, brought suit against appellee Indiana Department of Environmental Management, claiming that Ind. Code § 13-18-10 et seq., the statute giving appellee the authority to review and evaluate confined animal feeding operation (CAFO) applications, was unconstitutional. Appellants argued that the trial court erred in determining that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction because appellants failed to exhaust all administrative remedies. Appellants also argued that they were not required to exhaust administrative remedies. However, appellee had primary jurisdiction over all challenges to confined animal feeding operation applications, and appellants were not directly affected by the CAFO statute and permitting procedures. Judgment affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Trial court properly dismissed complaint for lack of jurisdiction. Appellee had primary jurisdiction over challenges to the confined animal feeding operation (CAFO) statute and any applications thereunder. Appellants, since they were not applicants, were not directly affected by the CAFO statute and permitting procedures.

 

800 of 1119 DOCUMENTS


Ledbetter v. Ball Mem'l Hosp.


No. 18A02-9907-CV-459


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, SECOND DISTRICT


724 N.E.2d 1113; 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 254



February 29, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE DELAWARE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Robert L. Barnet, Judge. Cause No. 18D01-9802-CP-0043.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed order of Delaware Superior Court (Indiana) which granted summary judgment to defendant healthcare providers since plaintiffs' deceased daughter was not child under Child Wrongful Death Act (Act), Ind. Code § 34-23-2-1 et seq., and Act was not unequal treatment in violation of Ind. Const. art. I, § 23.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff parents brought an action under the Child Wrongful Death Act (Act), Ind. Code § 34-23-2-1 et seq., alleging medical malpractice by defendant healthcare providers resulting in the death of plaintiffs' daughter. The court held that, although plaintiff's daughter was under 23 years of age, she was not enrolled in an institution of higher learning or vocational program and was thus not deemed a child for purposes of the Act. The fact that the daughter was previously enrolled in such an institution and intended to pursue a degree did not constitute enrollment under the Act, and evidence of such intent was properly excluded. Further, the Act did not violate Ind. Const. art. I, § 23, as an unequal treatment of different classes because it was rationally related to young persons dependent on their parents while pursuing an education and the Act was equally applicable to all members of that class.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment was affirmed; statutory requirement for enrollment in an educational institution to qualify as a child for wrongful death purposes was not satisfied by plaintiffs' deceased daughter's intent to pursue a degree, and the statute was constitutionally applicable equally to all young persons actually enrolled in an educational institution.
